O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O ye, most precious sons, I have completed this book which is the following of the science of medicine, assembled and fulfilled by its completion, and made the end according to its explanations and by its declaration.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in vision that I will complete this with your help, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forced in our region and strange everywhere, so has been lost the science and forgotten, and there remains only from it that the small descriptions in books of the ancients which have been moved by hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and the folly, and are closed the intentions, and are far away the science.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I will live if I follow the order of this book according the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and came together the forms of the cautery instruments, and other tools of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there is no good master of hands to be found in our times, the art of medicine has been stretched.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary that he who enters into this practice should understand the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows how to measure the limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and joints and the number of these parts, and the movement and the stillness, and from them their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And by this, Hippocrates says that the needle is much with the flesh and little with the work.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and even in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We say in the introduction of this book that he who is not familiar with the things said before should be careful lest he err and lose men.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	and so I have wanted to warn many times of those who intervene in this science and abandon their knowledge and sense, and experiments.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	I saw a madman who cut open an abscess of boils or neck of a woman, and cut the arteries at the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood came out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another madman who cut a stone from an old man’s body, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	so he took out a piece of the bladder with it and died of internal injuries three days later.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had heard that they call it the treatment, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the wound, and I knew whether the patient would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another madman who took treatment from the duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the fracture he inflicted an injury;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the madman who was ignorant of his craft tied the fracture to the wound with strong leather and did not allow it to be cleaned, and so he finished off the patient.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he instructs him not to remove it;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and stayed like that until the leg was completely withdrawn and the foot came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I am summoned to come to him, and I hasten to come to remove the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I saw it was dislocated, he had peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the corruption in his body was already confirmed on the limb, and it could not be cured;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease to spread through the limb until the limb was entirely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there is another method which destroys the pus and charms it, and then inflames with the evil of its power.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a cancer when it is purified with melancholic humors does not require that it be touched with iron unless there is no chance to remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear son, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	It means "This is to know, for there is risk in many types of dispositions;".
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And I will show in each one of these books where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For this reason it is necessary that you keep them to yourself, so that your enemies cannot speak badly of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take up your arms in consideration, and carry your patients gently but firmly, and use the best course, if it is through the grace of God that you will come to safety and be praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave frightful diseases without health.
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	And hold your arms against what makes you doubt, and have faith in them so that you can come from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Gallien says of some their admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Don't take it as a cure for a bad illness, unless you are called "fool's medicine".
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are of fire cautery and cold medicine, and the chapters are ordered from head to feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and of forms of discharges, and iron tools for cautery, and of all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapters are of cutting and piercing, and air viceses, and wounds, and extractions of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and the chapters are ordered and the forms of discharges.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and to be ordered by just as much weight, and by the shapes of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we remember the work, it is fitting to say what the quality of aid and the danger of each condition are.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of aid and the malady are the longest words and subtle knowledge and the secret responses;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and of this they spoke the many wise men, and agreed with it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and they softened their words a little, because I am of long speech.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery brings aid universally to all complexion, whatever the material it is of;
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	which are hot complexion with matter, and dry complexion with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry assembly of matter, they discussed and said that fire cautery is great aid.
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that fire cautery is of no value to an illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be treated with cold for heat, nor with dryness.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and this one who said the opposite that fire cautery is great aid to hot and dry illnesses that come into the body of humans.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you buy the body of man and its moisture is in accordance with the nature of fire, you find that the body freezes.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And not to involve fire unless he who has tried it, and knows through long usage of the cautery book, and the diversity of human complexities, their diseases' causes and conditions, and remedies and space of time.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	We have no fear of other kinds of humors, namely cold and moist ones.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors agreed and concurred on using cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, sons, that cautery combines fire with the secrets of cures, and greater good than applying hot medication.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not come from fire except to a limb that is burned, and it does not affect any other limb if it is not named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Medicines applied from part to part by moving them, bring diseases and pains of the body.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	And sometimes it brings on the disease in the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire for its heat and because of the nature of its substance does not do that, unless it has been superfluous.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this is what I have found by experience and through the length of time served in the art, and this was revealed to me on the nature of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	And for this reason I make excuses for the length of my speech, because it is not pleasing to me that I impart the secret which is restored by fire, and the quality of the work, how it cures diseases of the body, as the philosopher said when he demonstrated.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, when they will agree on what time the cauterizations must be done, and they set up prayers.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is advantageous in all times, because the harmful consequences are avoided by the aid of cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and himself, when he cuts, inflicts pain necessary and unavoidable, that the time which is more severe than great evil does not come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And do not think dear son, how they make fools of men.
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	because to the disease that is cured by cautery there is no return.
et il le dient ensi;	and he says so;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it's not so as they think, because cautery is not that medicine which changes the complexion, and dries up the humors that are the cause of pain, but rather worthless medicine for haste's sake, and because of the virtue of its work and lordship.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that the disease comes at any time according to the patient's complexion, and the nature of the disease, and its virtue;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and the humors are assembled in him with superfluities through the acquisition of food and similar things; but if you do not administer cauterization to him when he has little superfluity and moisture, as is done by cauteries on the dens for pain, and the similar things, because then the pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	but this happens little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And most people do not understand why cauterization is called the rear of medicine, and this means seeing;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterization is worth after medicine, but their understanding is false, and it is cauterization the rear of medicine because when we administer ways of cures in any disease and they are worthless, then we administer to it our cautere, and it is valuable.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	And then open, for cutting with fire is the medicine of the rear parts, not according to the foolish opinions.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancient ones said that cautery with an instrument of gold is more effective than with iron, and they say that fires were used only for the quality of gold and for the height of its substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the effects of cautery do not cause decay, but this is not seen because I have tried it and found that it is seen in some people;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and that instruments of gold are more valuable than iron, as they have said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And all you see when you hold an instrument of gold is not how it is charged with the quality of gold, and if it has just now cooled down;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if it is heated too much;
si font au feu;	so they are made of fire.
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is a great hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery so that what has been moved may be fixed at our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have ordered this chapter on the treatment of the upper joints just as if they were at the foot.
dou cautere olivaire	of olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moist and cold on the head, because one does it for the cause of a disease called "soda", and also for many humors that come out of the head to the eyes, ears, and because of numerous dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and themselves for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with medicine to dissolve the humors or four humors, according as the virtues and the blood and the accustomed condition of the patient can bear.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make red the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands and place his hands on a soft cushion.
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	after placing the root of your palm above the root of his nail, between his two eyes.
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and when you strike with your two fingers, if it bleeds from the incision then heat the cautery which is called "olivare", because this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And put on the left shoulder a mark of ink, and make it descend and pull back your hand little by little in turning;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand immediately, and reward the left shoulder if you see a small bone.
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After taking a small portion of the wool, and put it in a warm cloth, and place it on the shoulder, and let him stay for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	after putting cotton moistened in butter.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and let it stay until the inflammation is gone;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound, the "tetrafarmacón" which is called an ointment, so long as it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancients say that when you keep the wound open longer, it purges.
et por ce si aide mues.	and therefore one is advised to close it.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that you must so cauterize the wound that part of the bone is burned, and then replace what has been burned with bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And they say that one must cauterize it so long as the flesh is loose, and push it so strongly as to press down on a bone just as wide as a thread which women sew into their bodices because this causes the humors to flow out through the wound.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must keep the wound open for a long time afterwards.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards one should cure and apply ointment.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two kinds of cauterizations do not seem good to me altogether, fire whether in some people there is a way of living with fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and I think it's better to leave.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	because the joints are weakened by continued exposure to nature, as we have observed in other parts.
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and the same when a patient's joints are weak from nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more salubrious and beneficial to me, and that's why I work on it accordingly therefore this is salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When in all the head comes chronic pain that lasts a long time, then the patient must use herbs and pills called "cockie", and cleansing of the head with oils and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	And if they make the cautery as we have said, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Watch that if the head of the sick person is of strong constitution, and it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	and then the cautery should be done below as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After doing the cautery on each corner of the head just where the bone is, as we have said, and do the cautery on the one that is called "wasser", or blood vessel;
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is the point where you put a dressing.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	And hold your hand so that you do not feel with your fingers just against the bone;
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much more great pain in this cautery than the others, and I will speak elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is fitting that the cauterizing of horns are more subtle than those which cauterize the mortality of the head, and this is their form:
dou cautere dou chief	Fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain comes in one part of the head, and disease is spread from there to the bone, and the joints are purified by medicines that bring forth blood, and other cures have been done as I mentioned earlier for the division of diseases, and all this does not help.
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	therefore the cut must be cauterized in two ways, namely by hot medicine and by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	the cauterizing by hot medicine is that you prick a double [thickness] of flesh, and remove the skin and apply two points to the joints, and then make an opening in the temple where the pain resides in such a way that you can put back the doubled thickness of flesh under the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	And when she is reset so that the ligature and restraint are done well, and she is left to rest for 12 hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then remove the bandage and apply fire to the dose of garlic, and leave the wound for 2 days or 3.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then put on a cotton poultice in butter until it stops bleeding.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment of dressing, until he is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see, do as I have written or prescribed the medicine to burn.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery of what is this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closer" because the head is shaped like a bell or has a little bird's beak, and in its middle there is a small appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	And put the sore on the shoulder, and hold your hand there and twist the flesh a little lighter, until the moisture of the cure is burned.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	Leave your hand where the arteries are not inflamed, which is in front, and because of excessive bleeding.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After putting cotton on the wound to clean it, and put a poultice on the shoulder for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then I put cotton wet in butter, and then treat the shoulder with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	And if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare", at all points, and keep the artery covered in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	of the migraine.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat migraine in the way we have said in divisions of diseases, and do not benefit from it, and see that those who use cautery before say about medicine and iron did not suffer, then it is necessary to heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it becomes white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and so cut on the limb a line of half an inch long, and grasp your hand once, and strain so that you do not cover the artery and that it does not live until the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and guard the mandible which dies when you chew, and let the nerves not touch anything but the dead flesh and that spasms do not come to the patient, and guard against the corruption of blood from the artery when it is cut, or if it is cut there will be great fear and myself and others who are experienced.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the work in its original place;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where in this book it occurs.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and if you see that this cautery does not bring relief to the disease, and the patient suffers greatly, cauterize the affected area also as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said or the chapter of artery extraction, with the cautery that has two punctures;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and is this cautery more effective than that one and more beneficial.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of pain from the ears due to frostbite.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes from the ear due to frost, and you have tried solutive medicines and other cures that we have said on division, and the pains do not cease, then apply this cauterization which is called "pins", because it has this form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After poking all around the diseased ear, or in between the two when the pain holds in both, and you remove a little outward from the root of the ear then mark the spot with the instrument.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	And hold a distance of X points between each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment, let him be so healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	From the torture of the mouth.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Torture that must be cured with cautery except for those that are moved by inflammation, as we have said in divisions of disease;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not perform cautery on symptoms that come from a scab and phlegm of nose.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this symptom of torture that is moved by inflammation of the head and nose, and those are not cured with phlegm and purging, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one in the root of the ear, and another near the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and put the cautery in the part that is open and healthy, and they make a cautery straight on the head of the ear above one piece below the forehead, and another as far as the length of our finger;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and let the cautery stay above until the moisture of the wound is burned.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is the resemblance of a knife like that which we have shown before, but it is slightly more subtle and therefore it should be that the knives are slightly larger;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the wound has healed as I have said, until it is fully cured.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When epilepsy is ancient and you cure it as we have said, but the patient does not recover, and there is no fever, then do four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	In the second place concerning the two horns of the head and the eye where we have named "vasselez", as we previously said, and cauterizing on the lower part of the stomach's mouth;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and are treated in the same way as we have said before.
de litargie	of lachrymation (lacrimation).
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness it is customary to give the patient large and bitter pills, a brain-stimulating substance.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After removing the head of the patient, and applying on it a poultice made from sainfoin, which is written to treat poultices.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the manner of cauterizing:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is so afflicted, then good is his state;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if it is not so, make three cauterizations of the neck in front of the chin, with a space of two fingers between each cauterization.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and the treatment as for the others, and if you have any other symptoms, and the patient suffers, then make one cauterization in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it is so, two other cauterizations on the two horns, and the treatment until he is healthy;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let them be the cauterizations called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed with wine and what we have previously said;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	After the patient has recovered, take the head of the sick person, and then perform fire cautery on each ear and on the middle of the spine.
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	And if you need further treatment, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is severe, then perform fire cautery on the spine at the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	And let it dry for as long as possible to cool down, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	After the treatment as long as it is safe and sound, and so the cautery which is called "olivare" that we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should use fire cautery only on those who are flaky, and it is best to first cleanse the brain of years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and suffers from many pain medicines.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot suffer, then make gargling and masticating of molarium to clean the brain often with boiled meat.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the king's head is cut open, and he follows our instruction, and we perform the fire cautery according to what we have said previously, and we perform the fire cautery on the neck, and on each corner;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is strong and suffers, we will perform fire cautery as I have told to one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine at the back and neck, and so we will perform olive cautery according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is sick, then if they make the fire cautery subtle according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When by the cause of melancholy there are superfluities or moist ones corrupted and swollen greatly, then the cautery for cuttings as we have said to those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by the cause of melancholy the superfluities are declining to melancholy, and the body of the sick person is moist, then the doctor should give him something for which the intellects must be purified, according to what it is in front in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After the king's head is cut open on the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	after placing a linen bandage well made, like a circle, on the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and if they cross their arms, and are well held in all parts;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	After presenting the linen, take vinegar made from old wool fat.
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and hold the heat tempered with fire, so that the patient may bear it.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	After drawing a circle inside the head, and letting it cool down;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient each week once with good governance, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see cautery being done while making multiple pricks all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This kind of cauterization increases the brain's inflammation;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on moist cotton in butter and fat from gelatin.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye pain comes first from the signs that I said in the division, then begin and do thus: give to the patient a purifying drink of wine, and clean off all moisture from the head, and make him sweat or take a bath several times at dawn.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After instructing him to repeat his head, and doing cauterization inside the head again, and then doing it again on both temples, if there are two swellings of the fever in one temple together with its eyes, or in the other.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	And cut at all the cautery on every vein and artery that is under the skin, and so let them be cut long according to the length of the temple.
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	And be careful of the decrement of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stain with powdered iron as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in incising how to take care when you extract them;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And sometimes one cuts or applies cauterization under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the eyes' blood
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the lashes of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or on the arteries that appear under the forehead outside.
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and we see that this is due to superficial cold swelling, so make the fire cautery which I have mentioned earlier, applying it under the eyelids.
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	Apply the fire cautery to the forehead, and apply it to both temples, and apply it below the two bones.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if there is further damage, then make the fire cautery more severely applied above the eyebrow to all small cauterizations.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	A man's body in sorrow through within his eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you have prescribed medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not profit him at all, then take away three noxious medicines from the patient.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After the king-like treatment of the forehead, and make fire cautery on one side of the middle cauterization olive oil.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	And do the second cautery on the cautery which is called "clavilis" on both shoulders, a little below the neck;
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and guard the artery so you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see, do the second cautery on both shoulders just as long as the shoulder is.
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not hold back your hand except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to what I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	One hair that sticks out when it's wet.
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Never has happened that the hair of the oiled person is converted into parchment, and pricked with ointment, and then do cauteries according to two manners:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	Instruct the patient to let his hair grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	And if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they have grown and are even, then put the patient on a healthy bed;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	After putting on paper around the eyes a figure like that of the mirror of myrtle, and as it was at the beginning of signs of hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then put cotton soaked in oil and myrrh of persimmon on the wound, then take off the cautery to see how it is shaped:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cutting on the figure you have drawn, slowly and slowly a little at a time, until the color is reddened to the spot;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of health for the work is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs raised at the tip of the nail;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and therefore lift your hand, and let it stay for three days, then put cotton soaked in butter until the swelling is gone;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the ointment treatment until it is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	and if after that the hairs grow and the paper becomes soft then again apply the fire cautery on the same spot as you did first.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are fallen off then apply fire cautery until the paper rises to its natural position, and becomes even, and no longer touches the hair with the nail.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The cauterizing of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; then make a parchment the shape of mint leaves.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take French soap and live charcoal, one of each.
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and make it quickly, if it does not freeze; then sprinkle upon the shape you made like the leaf of mint, and put on paper eyes.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the sickness is held in only one oil, then you must apply it to both.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and put the oil-soaked cotton cloth around the wound.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the patient's joints are in your healthy state, and show the medicine to the doctor, and press one poultice at a time whenever the patient feels pain from the medicine, for he feels it as if of fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your body.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the inflammation of the cautery has passed, lift the limb from above, and repair so that if you see the paper lifted as it was lifted by constraint of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is thus, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If this is not so, then apply again the medicine to the limb or if it has not worked, until your work is even and your eyes are put in their place.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on cotton moistened in butter until the wounds are closed, after applying "dysphene" and other cures until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must guard yourself well at your wound with great care so that it does not touch the medicine,
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes swollen after, and the hair is pricked in oil, then resume the medicine on that limb which has become swollen from the paper properly, just as you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment so that they are healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the poultice made with the leaves of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And so it is known that the eyes of men are different in size and in smallness, and according to this be your constraints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And do not respond with the straight way to one who has studied this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistula by fire cauterization.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your cures are not profitable, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head on your healthy side;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and have the patient's chin between your hands in such a way that it does not move or turn its head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	After put cotton soaked in vinegar or persil juice on the wound;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	After the cauterization which is a part of:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it sticks to the head like a quill from a pen, so that they stick together.
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see, if it is stuck between the one head and the other, and if you see, so that they are joined together like a tent.
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but this is true only for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing the abscess it bursts open, and extracting the pus, and drying.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, then you work on it again, and extracting fires the bowels.
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	after putting the cauterization on, and keeping your hand to the cauterized part on the skin, so that your hands do not go mad.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and set the fire cautery in the fat of oil, and let it corrupt.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you are coming to the beginning of the cautery just at the bone, then it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If this does not work, repeat the fire cautery once more, and if you need to do it again, let it remain for three days.
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After that, place it on wet cotton in butter, and apply the cure of the ointment desiccant until he is cured, and if forty days have passed and he is still not cured, then apply the medicine that is acid and corrosive until the bones are uncovered.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and let him follow according to what he comes into his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is also a method of cautery for a fistula that none of the ancient ones said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	To cure an abscess, and take it away from the patient;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	After placing in the wound a subtle thread of what is its form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and they cut to the length of one pound.
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand firmly, and do not move the patient at all, except for when the pus is drawn out of the wound.
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is advisable to put some cotton wool soaked in wine or oil on the wound.
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the pus is drawn out and the healthy part remains in its place of movement.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	But if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If it is not so, then if necessary administer poultices on the wound, and bring the fistula back to the body according to what seems good in his own proper care.
des crevaices en levres	of fissures in the lips.
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often there are fissures in the lips called "poil", and similarly in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these fissures according to what we have said in our divisions, and the treatment does not help, then take a small cauterization with a culinary knife in that shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And put it at once into those crevices until it comes out in the same place.
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	after drawing out the pus, keep the animal intact until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the ear, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after being putrid and rotten, and has become a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	And you cure him just as we have said in divisions, and it does not bring any benefit:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	Therefore it is fitting that you cut according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	After the bandage or dressing of the fistula, and hold your hand where the iron needle goes into him;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do so once or twice, after the treatment we have said in treatments, until he is fully recovered;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if he is cured thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, it is fitting to discover the cause and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in his book.
dou movement des dens	Double movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat with medicine and it does not work, then put the head of the sick person on a safe place.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	After using the cautery, which will form a wound in this manner, then place a chain on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put the cautery hot in there so tightly that you hold it with one hand and let the patient feel the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	After lifting your hand and then recommencing the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	After filling the patient's mouth with a solution of water and salt, let it sit for an hour and rich fires.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in such a way the teeth which were moving are fixed, and the gums softened restrained, and the moistures corrupted dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When pain of teeth comes from coldness, or if there is coldness in the ear, and the remedies of medicine are worth nothing, then it must be necessary to perform cautery according to two manners:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and butter cautery, and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Butter cautery if it is so that you grease with butter of vinegar, and the end in a iron or bronze spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	after taking cotton and covering it with vinegar-soaked cloth on the tip of a tent needle, and the gum is set in butter, and put on the painful tooth hastily and hold until it cools;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and so does it many times until the virtues come to the root of the tooth, and if you see that gummed cotton and cloth in butter burn, and put on the painful tooth, and place iron hot so that the heat comes to the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cautery is assembled with the fire so that you grasp a chain of iron or flint, and it is thick enough so that the flames do not reach the mouth of the patient;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, it will form there afterwards, and place it on the tooth, holding your hand until the cautery cools;
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	do this often, because the pain will be eliminated on the same day or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	and it is fitting that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in haste while applying the cautery, and then rubs it on.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery on that head wher thou wilt, and according to thy power;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the knife:
des scrophules	Described by scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrophules are swollen from cold and moistors, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then take the fire knife, for this is what comes next, and apply two openings to the swelled part in order that the fumes may escape with the cautery of the other side.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and place the fire knife hot on the abscess once, or until it begins to flow with its own blood.
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, put knife according to its quantity, and leave it so for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and cover with a moistened cloth in butter until the sore is healed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	After a cure, the joint of limbs is restored with ointments and poultices until it is healthy.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the snake.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture overcomes the channels of the flesh, and when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is fitting that patients be evacuated first by medicinal solutes;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	After cutting fire at the root of the neck, and keeping in mind that you do not come near the throat, but rather avoid burning the wound with little heat.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After cutting fire at the shoulder joint near the head of the spine, and applying cautery to what is called "clavicle" because we have a shape like it.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	And restore the joint as we previously said, until it is healthy.
de la toust	of the tooth
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and malady of the womb are caused by cold moisture, and the patient has no fever nor thirst, and it is a long-standing disease, they should make two cauteries on the liver in their bodies.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery at the navel between the two nipples;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and that which is called "clavicle" according to its shape, is before mentioned.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	If you see, perform a cautery in pricking at the entire cautery which is called "points" because of its form, that is before mentioned in the disease of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and the points should be done at a depth of just thirty-three or forty.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the treatment according to what is said before, and let there be three pricks according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because it is easier to do so, because you make three cuts at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	After, rub the patient on his back and on his chest;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	After the knife is lifted from the itch, take it with your left hand.
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated within, then cut with a hot knife of two nerves, it is in that form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and burn the wound until it is felt on this side, and the fester of the cautery together with four burns:
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and because of this, it is done with the cautery that has three nerves, because the figures of cautery are so many cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and they are nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the cautery with three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And at times it is pressed against this nerve because there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After put on the cautery pearl-encrusted broth with thread;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After a period of rest, instruct the patient not to move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if the head of the shoulder is dislocated, since this happens little often, then apply cauterizing on thick bone or many cauterizing points.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and it is covered with moisture and it heals the patient.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When frost is in the stomach and much moisture remains, then it must be extracted to its condition, and many purges occur to it, and the usual remedies do not benefit it, therefore it is necessary that the patient lies on his back, and extends his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	After that, perform 3 fire cauteries (I) under the nail of the finger, in proportion to the size of two, all over the cautery clavicle; and 2 more cauteries on either side so that the edges of the cauteries are at 3 angles, and there is an equal space between one and the other so they do not come together when rotting.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cauteries be so deep that they stain the two parts of the skin, and so make the shape of the cauteries in this form with adjacency:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see a cautery being performed over a large wound in the stomach in this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	And he who fears this cautery, should prick himself and point at the stomach with that quantity.
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cut him to the entire cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the treatment we had before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	As for the liver, pain arises from cold and moisture and great ventosity, so much that it is forced to change its natural composition because of the superfluities;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the sick are cured of those things which we have said in divisions, and they do not benefit from it, if it is necessary to bring them down onto their haunches;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and the third incision according to this form and shape and quantity on the liver, excluding the hypochonders, when the ribs come into contact with it;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and hold an interval of space between each cautery the size of a dog.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauterization be long along the body, and do not press hard on your hand at all during the cauterization.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and let it be burned only on the moist parts of the wound, and let the patient keep his feet right.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, so let it be for the groin, and stretch his legs, and lift his knees.
et c’est li forme:	and this is
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if you wish to, cauterize those cuts on the sword's edge, if you are subtle and wise in this art, and be careful not to burn all the wound, for you will dry out the whole body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and let him not come until he is sufficiently cooled, for the keys are very subtle at that place, and his senses must be watched in order to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you see whether it is in the flesh of the liver or in the linen.
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, he feels the patient's pain but not too much.
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the linen, he feels a painful frenzy.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment requires applying poultices, it is advisable that the patient lies on his head.
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then sign the patient where the abscess is, and then apply heat to the cautery which resembles a splinter, so that it can take the form.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize as long as the keys are hot, and it comes just from a sore, until the wound is completely set aflame;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment as prescribed according to the treatment of the wounds until it is healed.
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not fitting to use this cauterization on anyone else but those who have studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have been cured once.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	And so one can boldly perform it, and often I think that wounds should be left alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of cauterizing the pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancient said that we should do cauterization of pleurisy with roots of arsotle, and in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	take a root of arsotle that is longest, the one you can find, and make it dry, and so large and as long as your thumbs.
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and the warts in oil, and seize with fire, and cauterize between the navel and the neck, and cut off two cuts down from descending to the part which is below the beard;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and cut off between the fifth and sixth ribs, declining back a little.
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and cauterize the little toe, and another on the stomach, between two spines, and two along the two ribs, before the one that is between the two spines;
