Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	and it should have between the two cuts one inch of large needle, and then when you insert both needles, and warm iron on top so that it comes in just to the bone, cut the vein in two.
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	And let them separate between the two shoulder bones because there is no soldering of this cautery with all.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and it is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the eyelids shed tears from the veins that are on top of the forehead of the face, and he does not benefit from a cure with medicine that one makes, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and feel his forehead for walking as if in pain.
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and so that the oil is kept and moist, if the hair of the scalpel falls out, and the scabbing of the papers, and burns from the heat of the tears, if it is necessary for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And they called it the ancient "cure contused", and you must make on the patient who has this disease the hairs of his forehead, then make three incisions or evenly according to the length of the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	And so one of the cuts is like two, dividing both front and back in half, where it comes to the neck at the same time, and the other has two at the breast above the papers, and you must keep away from the incision of the arteries that are located above the papers;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	And keep your hand away from continuing the two mandibles, and let each cut be three times across both sides;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have prepared a sponge and some rags to absorb the blood, then pour out the styptic mixture, which is two parts of this form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	of the incision that is left above the temple, just before the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	And scorch all the wound that is between the two cuts to the surface of the bone, then make another cut from the first incision up to the second one, and then pull out this styptic mixture.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If it is cut in the first wound with the instrument called "cultellary", and is very sharp from one side and the other, soft not cutting, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And cuts the costal bone towards the raw flesh at the wound, and the costal bone is soft towards the bone, and it presses hard until it comes to the middle wound.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And bind tightly the vessels that descend from the forehead to the eyes until the incision is complete just as soon as the bleeding stops, and then again make an incision in the middle cut just before the other separation.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then pull out the vein equally, and press the vein so that it does not leak.
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	Then put a piece of cotton wool in each incision, and cover it with moist cloths soaked in wine and oil and salt, so that the pus does not come out.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And on the third day remove the bandage, and administer a great quantity of vinegar water, then apply the treatment with Basilicum oil with rose oil, and other remedies for wounds until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	They must hold their eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When an affliction of the eye comes to be used in a regular manner, and you see the eyelids closed tight and red, and fainting occurs, and papers are burned;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hairs become thin, and in the center of the forehead there is great pain, and the patient is thrown into convulsions;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Therefore, through these accidents you know that those matters and this cough come from many veins, and the male cure is present if it is so.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to raise his forehead, then make a great cut along the eyebrows.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And beginning from the split of the left temple to the right temple, and performing an incision just beyond the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and remove your hand from the nerves of the temples which move downward;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bones are exposed, soak all the blood in an sponge, and then squeeze between the two lips of the cut and put cotton wool there, and try with linen.
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then cover the above wrapped cloth with moist linen and oil, and keep away from the hot place.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is raw, if it is fitting that you rub the bone until the blood starts to come out, then treat with an antiseptic medicine that brings on charring.
En teil maniere:	In this manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of powdered coal, and mix them.
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and apply this to the wounds for charring all over.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the bursting of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Everything that falls into the ear is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or grain, or flesh, or a piece of metal from a mine, or something similar like iron.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, like fireflies, bees, and grasshoppers.
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or thing that flows, like water and ice, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it comes out of the ear stone or in some other manner of thing that does not adhere to the ear, nor grows in the ear, if you put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, then if it distills any small amount of violet oil or oil of sages, then extract it.
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and the treatment is to make it vomit by condensing, and put a cloth or wool over the nose when vomiting comes, and put a piece of fabric into the ear.
et estent l’oreille au desus.	And let them put the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times it comes by this cure;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	And if she does not come, they must extract with subtle pinches, because thus there is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it happens by those pinches, it's good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	else if they must extract with subtle stitching at the warts.
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not happen by that, make a cauldron of resin and pour the chief down the cauldron or ear canal very deeply, and warm up the thing that is around the cauldron with wax so that the venoms cannot enter with the cauldron;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	Then the joint will form, because many a time it occurs when we have said so.
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	And if it does not come by this manner, when it pricks the glue of which it pricked the hairs, and puts in some instrument with a point to do that, and puts a little cotton around;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the glue on the stone or whatever it may be, and make a joint.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not happen as all that we have said, then hasten to split the ear so that you pierce an abscess and a vein;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	And the way of the cut is such that you first make the patient healthy of the cephalic part, and extract the blood according to its virtue, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut in the root of the ear at the fat or where it depends.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	And instruct the wound to heal like a moon, until you reach the bone; then set the bone according to your power, and suck it hastily into your mouth.
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment until it is sound.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it's an abscess that has formed and inflamed, administer extraction.
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, so administer a thin poultice in the same form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And instruct the patient to make a cut at that point.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many cuts.
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract with fine needles and suck it out, as we have said, so that the extraction may be easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water then it is best to vomit into the ear; and that the patient may use early condiments, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And also if it is swollen on the same ear or in the water.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it falls through for that reason, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If this is not so, then instruct the patient to prick many pains according to the length of his body must be kept and light, and cover one part with fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and put the sick in ear pain or piercing from his ear and runs up to it from his other foot and fear of one more pierce on the pierce that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and does not cease to pierce stone into stone until the wound is healed completely and again it heals completely;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see, prick a joint and pour one of the poultices into the ear, and the other pierce with fire until the smallest bone is burned;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then make another of those joints until the wound is healed, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	When extracting a bone, if it is of small size, like a thorn and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division.
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	But if it is of large size, and it can be felt, then extract by pinches.
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	And this is the lighter thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	When extracting worms in the ears, add ear drops to it as we have said in the division and when treating infections, if the treatment does not help, then you should look at the ear by sunlight:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If there are no worms seen, then take the ear under fine pinches, and if they do not appear, seize the canna (ear canal) so that this is its form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it may be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And pour out the most subtle part of the head into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then success forms at all the joints.
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often until all the veins appear.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not come out, when it is stuck between the chain of cotton as I said in the stone.
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not come out as we have said, administer infusions that the ancient ones have used in the treatment of worms, and you will find or use them for infusions.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, because there is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And let it be of silver or gold; for so is made the mouth of the pertain tubes, and above it to distill.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press inside the distillation of the well-made instrument of gold, and if you see the rasp and rub it through until the point is covered with cotton.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then I pour your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicine in the cane, and let it be in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then pour into the rasp all the cotton, and press your hand in time until the oil is distilled or has almost reached the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient feels it inside, and let the distilled poison be thrown into his mouth also as one is distilling in the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And keep them from being too cold, for the medicines are not very good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the bursting of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born who does not have some defect in their ears.
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	And the same thing happens to adults because of an outlet or wound inside the ear, and these wounds often do not heal in the ear if you can't see them.
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	And sometimes it happens that there is a small defect and the person sees well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	So when it comes to a wound that is closed and cannot be seen, if you are in a state of weakness or illness, then you must put the patient's ear to the sun.
et regarde dedens:	and look within:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	If you see the inflammation appearing, if the work has all this splinter of blood, then it is the shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And if they are swollen and punctures in front and behind all flat, if it does not affect the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the inflammation is in the skull or ear bone, if you have fine punctures and strike lightly enough, so that the charred bone is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	If the swelling is in the ear, then take a fine needle lighter and place it on the flesh of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the inflammation where the patients feel great pain in the ear, puncture lightly, and guard so that you do not weigh down the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then put a tent in the ear according to its width and the moisture in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Instruct to do this every day until the wound is healed, or you take an poultice and the poultice is made from mold in vinegar and red wine, and powder on top of vitriol.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear swollen, then apply the poultice and move another poultice moistened in cherry oil and beeswax until the swelling is removed.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat so that the patient becomes healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the blood comes to flow again, then plunge an sponge and wring it in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that can relieve bleeding from the flow which are for treating oozings.
de la char des papieres	from the flesh of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This that come out on paper of the eyes when they are moist and dry, if it is needed to be stretched with tongs and tweezers, and cut off by a spatula from its roots;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put on the eye vitriol powder.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if without removal, so the cauterizes with fire cautery, the delicate lensular subtil, and the cauterizer after the incision is moved;
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and often repair, for no part remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, the roots are burned and do not return again.
de la gresle	From the shoe.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Often bring forth from the eyes some things that appear to be gristle in form and hardness, and because of this it is called "grain" disease, and is an assembly of great moisture on top and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	the wounds are such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	to beware if the grain dies from one side and the other, and this is a light thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	The wound is then dressed with powder, then the scab is scraped from each part lightly, then it is taken off by pinches, and then it is chopped.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cover it with a dressing after piercing the skin, so as not to give the patient pain.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the wound is large, you should put together with stitches and treat it until it heals.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, you shouldn't make any forced treatment, because the stitches will restore it at once and cause more harm.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	and if the granulation is falling from inside of the ear towards the upper part, you will turn down the dressing and pinch with tweezers, and cut and press on both sides.
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	And if the paper is separated by the incision, it brings no harm.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And when the gravel is struck, clean the oil of salted water, and treat the patient so that they are cured by burning charcoal until they are healed.
de la graisse des eulz	From the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	This is a fat that burns in woven nets of paper above, and it often kills infants who have no one to care for them, and causes great pain to their eyes, and they come to catarrh in the mornings, and cannot see into the light of the sun because their tears stop flowing to their eyes.
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And for this they lie on their faces because of the fire, and sleep above it, and their moist papers under their eyebrows are inflamed with the fat that burns in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint with your hands and feel the swelling inside.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And so are the ways of this work, for the patient must put his head into your hands;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	And then take a linen drapery, and set up a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity contained within each part, and then place it above the patient;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	And press with both hands from one side and the other, so that the parts are gathered into the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make at the midpoint of the moisture on the scaphoid bone cutting a slit to a width no greater than the wound that was made on the vein.
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and let the skin be drawn over the part until you see the parts come together;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and from this multitude of positions comes expiration from the wound, according to the form of a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Then take a piece of cloth gauze and bind it around both your arms in front, and turn your hand to right and left so that it is spread.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and that you do not add anything to the wound, lest you come to all the spectacle of the blood just at the oil, and that you do not burn it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the blood does not flow at first in the beginning of the wound, then apply a little to the wound lightly so that it appears.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then take it as we have said, then wrap it in cloth gently and with water, and put on the linen, and tie with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if such men who break the silken thread and place it in order to corrupt that moisture which has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer as long as he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to a swollen joint, so that the patient is being treated with emplaster until he is well.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of paper.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When the hairs are growing on the nose that are not in their natural place, and have become inflamed, if they prick at the eyes, and do come up with kinds of illnesses such as sneezing and softening of the hairs and albugine, until it is the cause of destruction of the eyes;
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and there are four ways to treat this.
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by fire cautery assembled with heat, or by water according to what is in front of the chapter of fire cautery, and either done by incision and stitching or by cauterizing, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you put the patient's head in your own hand, then turn the hair of the nose from the oil to your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	She has been converted; it is good.
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	If they do not comply, put an arrow into all of the above (i.e. the above mentioned wounds).
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and even if it is on the edge of the paper or where the hair grows from those hairs, and pull the thread above all over the paper, and turn to the shaver;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make in the lower part of the paper, below the hairs joined, all over the scalp cutting, from the great braid to the little.
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then pull out the thread, and put under the paper a small tent made of cotton and fabric, then cut above the paper an eyebrow shape, as in the image of mirte, so that it suits the amount of hair you lifted from the paper which is divided into all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if to someone who has need, one cuts off a great quantity of paper according to what the paper is softened.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then makes all the surrounding area around the two lines you signed, and begins to sew loose linen just above small.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and if one of the cuts is near the natural hairs in the size of a root, then pour on the onion into one of the two corners cut, and scorch all.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then brings the two lips together to sew with an aglet of a needle to all the fine threads of wool, and sucks out the blood, and makes the swelling dry on the surface of the filth above both wounds and sticky things, if you see such.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	If this is not so, then do not treat it. Then leave the wound and hair for three days or four.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then cure the wound with a dressing of dry things and binding, because the paper will revive at the moment of the wound's opening and reassembly, but the binding is weak (as they said the old ones), and it's a work with fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	And if there is another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And it is that you know the paper of a figure which is as the miter's wool, just like we have told, three inches apart according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut off that which overhangs because of small, even, equal parts according to its shape.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you do not have the power to hold the tongs, and the thing is not even, take a needle or it has one thread, and bind around the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	And put one finger of your left hand on a strong nail, and your second finger on a small nail, and equally join between your two fingers.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin where you have marked it, as we have counted; then bring together the two lips of the wound by stitching, and the cure until he is healed.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, dress it with crotone and similar ointment soothing.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes happens that the hair of a paper is converted.
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	so you must use what we have said about the incision.
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitching in both is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The cure for the joints is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and that you convert the paper and the felt into it according to what I have said, and then make two joints by art, and two subtle ligatures as long as the paper and the width of the spindle is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut to two parts, where you hold the strings;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble one and the other subtly above what protrudes from the oil paper, and strain the two joints of the two parts together;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and let it be thus for some days, and the skin that was strained will wither and contract and harden, as if it had come to itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it lingers, if he has some strength, then let him stay until he is healed.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	And when the wound is stitched with silver, and it is lifted and the paper is taken out, and there will be no more pain in the hair.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And this is the form of the two canals that you will make according to this figure and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the wounds are such that you will pierce with a fine needle, and you pour in soft and fine thread;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then tie the stitches and do not hold one and the other too tightly, so that the length of the thread is equal to a palm.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then place another fine thread of silk in the chase tightly, and no loose ends.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Now put the patient's head on your own healthy one;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let the sun shine so that the wound is clearly visible, for it is a subtle and small one; then poke the needle into the root of the attached hair, and pierce through the paper hastily until you bring it out above the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then pull the hair all the way out to where the needle was inserted, and fill in with the needle that was pulled out, if there are one, two, three, or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then pull your hand back so that the hairs come forward all the way to the end of the needle with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	and if the needle is applied and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the needle downwards to the end of the thread that you ordered, until the needle comes out through the pores above and you see it by the sight of oil.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	And then you should pull out the thread and the needle, and clothe the wound with oil, and let it rest for two or three days, until the hair grows in its place and the scar subsides;
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hairs are small, then accompany the short hair with the long hair from the chest area, and raise it with that which you leave, until it is lengthened and then set.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil's spoilage
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this sickness is called "aleacrati" or when the putrefaction comes into the oil, it happens in two ways:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one is natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden injury or cutting or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And in the treatment of the pus, it is that you cut open the scab, and dress the lips with it, and put linen bags inside, and tie them up until they are healed;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and must not be used only in the treatment of dry things that constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	But if you do this, it will come back worse than the first time;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but working on softening things, as fenugreek.
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the root of mullein or rose-water and seeds of flax are cooked, and ointments made from melted diaquilone in any of the oils, and cover it with a cloth, and treat thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasures of your treatment are that you keep them safe so they do not become corrupted as before their form.
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and what we have said is not fire but only an expression of this disease, which it does not return to its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the fat that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is outside, and truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident happens from a wound and tearing, and cautery, and similar things.
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the vein of the work is like this: you prick with an awl, in which it has a double thread, and the needle in the flesh, and make it pierce from the left shoulder to the right, so that the thread comes out through two joints of the arm;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then the flesh is stretched over all the awl, and a wide stiletto.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	and if the mark on the paper returns according to what is wanted, that's good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if it does not come, then take the razor and put it in the wound, and turn the paper, and make two cuts on either side of the paper inside.
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	And let the heads of the two cuts at the two corners of the incision be made so that when they are assembled, the figure is as it were of a letter with no «I griesche».
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then take the bone, according to how much its edge is attached below, from that which is indicated by the parchment, then add the two halves of what is cut, and sew with a thread of linen.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply the remedy to what we have said about soft medicines and poultices, until he is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from a cut or a seam or a cautery, so that you may make a clear cut below the hairs of the papers, and according to what was said before.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	After the fire cautery, make a deep incision between the second and third fingers of a tent peg, as I have said.
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must make the work according to the shape of the illness, because it is very different in form, and the wise masters will use the engine for every type of poor strength so that the figure returns to its natural form.
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And the patients themselves, according to those things which they need for work and treatment for more severe conditions.
dou soudement de la papiere	and suddenly from the paper.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this binding has happened in a certain way, that is to say the paper above is stuck with white oil, and it cannot move or do its natural work, so if you need to then apply the point of a rasp over the paper, and lift it up towards the top;
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and the length as pinches, until you cut what is sharp at the subtle needle, which should not be too thin nor too thick, so that the patient cannot suffer from the needle being too thin or leaking oil.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and so your incision, if you scorch the assembled flesh lightly, according to its natural form;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and the whole assembled flesh is healthy, and it never happens that there is any pus in the infected oil, and you lift off the foul water with gentle broth.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then put a linen cloth between the paper and the oil, and place the linen-oiled cloth on top of the oil.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after three days, use the broth and other strong things until it is healthy.
de l’ungle de l’oil	From the uncleanliness of oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	The joint has two forms:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	There are two types of joints: one is hard like bone, and another that does not feel nerve-like but appears frozen with cold moisture; when it is touched with iron and treated with patience, there is a wound.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	And both types of joints begin to resemble the great tendons, and they grow little by little until they cover all the vein and all the light, and the movement of the sinew.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And there are two ways of making an incision, so that the patient puts his head on the healthy side, then he opens his eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	And lifts the paper with his hand, then coils the joint like stitches of small doubling, and extends it upwards;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	Then take a needle, and put some horse hair, or sheep hair, or cow hair, into it, and make it very long.
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	And double the point of the needle a little and tie it with a string, so that it is fastened to the top, and scrape all along the length of the needle on both sides, leaving just enough hair at the end of the nose, then cut off the remaining part at the root of the eyelash down to the spot where it meets the skin, then pierce the remaining part back up into the lobe of the ear until you reach the small spot where the membrane is thin and make an incision that will allow the blood to flow according to nature.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	And sometimes you attach just the needle to the wound and then to the string.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	Then the scorching is applied to all the soft parts where this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And make sure that the soft parts do not touch the tough skin and break, and that the pulse is felt;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	And after the incision, pour a little oil on the broken part and apply linseed oil to the collar, and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then restore what is needed so that he may be healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not inflamed, and you cannot push the needle in, and the wound cannot be opened, this similarity of an ingrown nail is often cured with remedies.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, then apply oil to the patient, and take a soft cautery according to this form;
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And carefully remove the warts from beneath with subtlety; and if you see that they do not diminish at all, and your reason is impeded by them, then distill from your mouth into a vinegar made of lime, which causes redness of the throat, and break it off, for it numbs.
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then resume the other work according to this same work, until it is all bone.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is against you in the oil, as with a wound, then take the ointment and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed; then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the skin is darkened with pus in the oil for great harm, so that the swelling increases, and you cut off a part of it, not too much, lest blood comes from the wound.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	then distill in the vinegar made red, which is made of lime.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the flesh born on the eyelid.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	The eyes of some men never turn red, and cover the pimple and restrain on the papers and thorns to avoid, and it seems like a rose from the bough;
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	And if the wound is such that the patient puts his head on a healthy one, then he opens the eyes, and coils all that has suitable strings to it, and supports it with strength;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	Then he cuts the first string, and goes copating to the rasur until the end, and keeps that you do not cut the oil at the wound;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	And if the incision is through the splintile, just as we have said in the incision of the ungue and with small forces because one may break the limb, as the form shows after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is completed and all the flesh has fallen off, apply oil of silk or distill rose-coloured wine and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the oil with cotton wool wrapped around an onion.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if it does not heal at all, and the flesh is sore and swollen, then let the oil remain and treat the inflammation with soothing measures.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work as soon as you are healed, and similarly place the char ( probably referring to the onion) in the oil by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But it is wise to lighten the healing treatment for each person with a weak oil, according to the natural remedy.
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and from a false vein, for metal.
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not strike with your hand in any of these works until you see that the limbs are suffering from this injury.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These veins are red and covered on the skin, and they hold back their own work and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	The first thing is to look at the wound and see in what way it is, whether it is inflamed, open, or no other fire-like disease except that inflammation.
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	and then apply the binding in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put his head on your healthy one, then suspend those veins all over the wound according to his wisdom, and so be those subtle veins doubled in that form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two on one side by degree in the four according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	and then bind those veins tightly with forceps, and apply the wound for an hour after another, until you see that the fiery veins are removed from the wound;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and keep in mind that the hairs at the base of the scalp are sensitive, and do not touch with your fingers at those points, and perform this operation at noon, in front of the sun, and be very careful in your work so that you do not cut yourself only when the veins are opened.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, if you want to destroy that which remains in the vein, distill it into oil that is green and red to corrupt what has stayed there since yesterday.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you do not have the power to remove all that remains in that hour, then apply oil of soothing things on the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains are soothed, and be sure of a pus forming, and then resume according to this manner as long as the patient is healed.
et c’est li forme des forces:	and thus it is the form of the force:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	the wound they call "arissati" fistula:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	when you cure it by cautery and by medicine with hot water according to what I have said, and it is not healed, then there is an infection in it where you cut open the abscess, lest it kill you, and remove all the moisture that is in it, until the bones are uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	and when the bones are uncovered and you see the corruption and darkness, if the wound has all the instruments by which it is formed;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and is called "aspere chief", and it should be made from the fine iron in this place, and you should pierce it like a nail as sharp as one that is now in its present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place on him the law of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand hard enough so that you know well which is the corruption.
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this no more than once, then restore the law of the medicine extracts.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the law is sealed, and it swells, and the bowel’s flesh is swollen, and remains like this for forty days, and does not become inflamed again, and no more accidents come to pass, then you know he is cured.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	if this not so, if there is no other remedy but to return the fistula to its original place according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and that you discover the second time by iron, and by sharp medicines, and when it heals, uncover it as per this form, and if the joints of iron are bent to three angles, and the fistula is relaxed up to the head, just like that which you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	Then put it on the surface of the bone near the joint, and remove your hand from the oil for a little while, then turn to the entire forest until you pierce the bone and feel the patient through this that they come in if they hold their hand over their neck;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then return the limb to the medicine that is dry, just as I have taught you, and when the chariot (or possibly "the liver") nourishes and hardens the limbs, let the material reach the neck;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	so it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Of the issue of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are open all the time, and they do not come to rest on the nose, or become smaller, then it is best that you tie up the patient;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	First let the healthy one, then put ventouses or haterel to pierce for relief, then put on oil like he made of ice and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then strain the oil, and apply it to the plaster with bandages and cloths;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	And the manner of the bandages is that you take soft cloths, and wrap each one around four times, and then put one on top of another according to how much skin there is needed;
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then strain it over a hard bandage, and then put on the ventouses again to relieve by piercing.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then take off the ventouses and let the oil bind tightly for day and night, and if you tie it with a bandage, so that you can tighten it more.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then take care of the bone after the day and night, and if you see it repairing itself, this is good;
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	But if it does not heal again, and the plaster is reapplied and the bandages are put back on, and the bone and the wounds remain in place until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Drop of fallen hair
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When the inflammation comes into the eye, then opens and brings forth papers like grains of resin, and is wonderfully astonishing to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you cover the eye with work, such that you put an awl into the root of the lower part of this wound, and then put another awl where there is a double thread from the upper part of the corner;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	And cut to open it, and let the first needle pierce, according to its shape.
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	Then cut the liver with a double-edged knife and bind a part of the right side, and tie it well, then pull out the needle and apply oil of linseed in abundance to it.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	And let it be until the liver is stuck to the gallbladder, then apply oil from soothing things until the wound is healed.
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And at no time should the wound be restrained by a bandage of cloth around each part of a circular shape, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eyes have great appearance, then pierce with a fine needle that comes from beneath the oil, and draw out the moisture and downward let enter.
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	Now let them wait until they are whole.
de la bowe de l’oil	of oil from the bowel.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This illness, which is called "alcunnati", consists only of the bowels assembled in oil, resembling fever descending, and it is not true fever.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	And the manner of its appearance is that you should make the patient lie on an upright stool and straight, then take his head in both hands of two parts, and pull it until you see the bowel rising up to your eyes.
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	Then tie it up and do not let it descend, nor let the light shine, and see how the patient is doing as he usually does.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	And if it does not descend under, see that it is fever, and if the descent of the bowel is prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	If you sit the patient between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make above the eyebrow by the continuation of the connection with the eyebrow skin and the crown, as long as the bow is attached;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when it is released, if it distills into oil of hot water mixed with honey or to fenugreek boiled in honey, then apply another treatment until she is cured.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have the signs of water in the section, and what is needed for puncturing;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary to sit the patient between your hands crossed, a fire from the light by the sun, and apply oil of health tightly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	Then place the paper of oil on your left hand if his eyes are on your right, or on your right hand if they are on your left.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	Then take in your right hand if his eyes are on your left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if they are on your right.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the point of the instrument into the crown, by the size of an arrow, in that thin layer of oil on the skin where it is nearest to the bone; then carefully blow the instrument which is called "almagda", violently, and twist your hand until it pierces through the oil, and feel that almagda is coming out of the empty thing.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is proper that the measure of almagda's depth be equal to the space from the root of the hazel tree to the end of the nail.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the crown of oil;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	If you will see the bone in that paper because of the clarity of the linen cloth, and put the instrument just near to where the liquid is, then press from one side after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If they are now bleeding, so he sees the patient before him and the instrument on his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After resting for a little while, and if the liquid rises up the second way, put some force with the instrument, and when it is stuck in place and does not rise again, carefully remove it lightly by turning your hand a little at a time;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put some wool or gem in water, and rinse off the oil inside;
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put the oil-stained cloth or a moist linen in olive oil and plenty of wine, and bind with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	So, and for those of our time, let us put on a common broth with plenty of wine.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the arm cannot enter into the oil because of its hardness, for it has many people who have very hard eyes, so it is necessary that you take hold of the instrument which is called "alberit", for this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not cut too much down into it, but make a new subtle cut, and bathe in that liquid, just as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	And as the work is completed on the patient's body, the doctor appears before him at night, in which case he lies down on his dark bed;
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	And so he must refrain from all movements, and take light foods, and not move his head to the right nor to the left, and should be bound according to his disposition just for three days;
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then he releases him from the same dark chamber, and opens his eyes, and shows him some things, and then he sets him free again after seven days;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not necessary to do that in the urine of the patient or after the incision now, but it is necessary to lighten him, because the water mounts suddenly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	When an abscess comes to a head, let you loosen the oil in front of the seventh day, and take care of one who cures the abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	And when it is healing, if you loosen the eye and put on its lower eyelid to cover any day, and so remains in that dark and obscure house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then one goes into the house little by little, and turns it over in its cases;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and knows that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from the East, who told me that in some far-off land, people do make almagda (a medicinal substance), because of which they get drunk, but I have never seen it or known it in our country, nor has it been written about it in the books of the ancients.
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And by chance, this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the forms of alum, because those who do not know them can see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	are of pure iron.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the head of this same subtlety, and the behind in three angles of inflammation.
de la char sor le neis	From the sword near the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	There is no occasion for the birth of different kinds of worms, because there are some that resemble scorpions to a great extent.
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there are such ones where the worm is covered in a red flesh color, and some have worm flesh of a white bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	Then in the case of those worms that are not covered with flesh, it is necessary to sit the patient between your hands against the sun.
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	And work on his nose, and put the cloth on those wounds, and tie up the fuses;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	for cut what you must support under the subtle, small instrument, from one side, until you see that the wound is entirely closed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there is anything left that cannot be covered, if you apply all the subtle instruments lightly, so that it does not stay anywhere.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if you do not find any pus or abscess, cut it as needed.
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cautery as much as you can until the area is sterilized and all the wounds are closed, then put on linen or vinegar either hot or cold wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If his nerves are overgrown, and moisture arrives just at the palace, he knows that it is safe.
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	And if moisture does not penetrate as it should, he knows that there is a bone cleft in the above, because the humors do not come to cut.
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Then he must put a small thread of flax into the wound, and let it be drawn out by hands, and should have between each person some space to draw it out, and it must not be less than.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	And put the patient's head into the wound in such a way that it will come out with great force, and treat him with an odorant until it comes out through the nose.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	And many times this is done to children in school, and it's a light thing for him who does it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	Then hold the head that comes from inflammation with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and check each one after the other while smelling like us who are in the field.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the flesh has not corrupted because of the wound, then cut the fingers, wash the wound, and moisten the finger in Egyptian ointment, and put it back above (the level) of the skin as before.
