fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this for three days or more, until the ointments have corrupted all that remains of the flesh.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	And then put the wound under linen wrapped in cloth for some days until it is healed, and if he needs to apply dry medicines, so that.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, because one distills the oil and medicine or other substances:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	and let it be of silver or lead, resembling a lamp over the top, like an earthenware pot, and so conduct it:
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see, make a narrow tube, and let the instruments be flat for purging the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have a mesh at the head to hold it when you heat the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the sword near the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times the head swells from the application of medicine with a painful boil, and grows and becomes large so that it is visible to be looked at;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this reason it is necessary to apply the cauterization or hot medicine at first, and then put on the head a poultice made of all its parts.
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if you hold it to cover until it is large, take care if it is hard, of the red color, of poor sensation:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if you don't touch it with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when one cuts it once, great evil comes to the patient.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is from a soft touch, not from a red color, and you see that it can be completely covered, evacuate the patient and let him cut with fear, and treat the thing as dry and restrain.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nails are struck and crushed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	So that when some continuation of solution comes to one of these overgrown cartilages, it is not enjoyed at all, whether in any person.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary to do the same if this happens to anyone, when you see whether the wound is fresh with all its blood.
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then join the two lips to a stitch, and treat until he is well.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are swollen on one side and the other, so you should scrape all the parts of their heat until they heal, then assemble the two lips to a seam, bind them, and sprinkle with powder of dragon's blood, and hot incense.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put on the powder a piece of plaster of strong or other plaster setting, and let it dry so that it sticks to him, then treat with ointment until he is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of the seam if you are assembling:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the seam on the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I told you.
des apostemes des levres	of swellings of the lips.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	My mouth hurts inside the abscessed gum like grains of rice, and sometimes smaller, larger ones.
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	Therefore it is advisable to return the lips, and cut each one of them, and press with pliers and strike into every part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply the hot liver after the application of vitriol powder, until the wound is stained.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then apply the herbal medicine from elsewhere, and treat the liver of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times there are swellings on the gums near where they call "albulus".
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	it is advisable to sustain it with tongs, and cut at its root, and let the wound or blood flow.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	Then put vinegar on the wound; or other powder binding and drying.
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if the wound comes back after the incision and it has happened many times, so that you have to cut again, and cauterize.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not come back after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are signs of pus that need to be covered.
des sordens	From the sound
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Never are they assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and painful sores;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes are the teeth black and yellowish and putrid, until corruption comes to the gum, and they become foul.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	If you must do this, instruct the patient to sit between your hands and have his joints placed in your hand, and when bones or scars are exposed, leave nothing there.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and then do the purging of black bile and green bile, and yellow bile and the other humors, until they are cleansed.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if you extract what is at the first joint, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if this does not work, resume on the next day and the joint, until you have all of them.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and observe that the teeth have need of various shapes of instruments to cut, according to what the work shows, because the sawers who are used for cutting through the teeth have other shapes than those which are used between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others are to be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when treating a patient's pain in the tooth that you wait as long as possible before performing the treatment, for this should not be delayed.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a highly potent substance just created, therefore we have no excuse for failing to take care.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is forced to take it out, if you want to be certain of the tooth's vitality.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Often the pain is worse in the patient, and consider it to be a tooth that needs to be extracted, and treat the good tooth.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and do not take the pain away immediately, as it may cause new problems, because we have already tried to get rid of it with these physicians.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are certain about the tooth that is inflamed, it is wise to burn all around the tooth with a strong caustic powder to protect the gums from all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	Now the arm you must move to your elbow or use sharp nails at first, and then pull out the nails until they are well cleared, then firmly fix them.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	And if the joints of the patient are between your thighs, and his tendon is well fixed so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth from the cheek directly, and if it doesn't fly out, take any of these instruments and put them inside each side lightly, and move them as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the bone is perceived and broken, so it should be filled with cloth, to or where the fracture is.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	And if you tie it subtly with nails, so that it does not break when being tied.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And it is necessary to apply much care over the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient when the root becomes infected, causing greater pains than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And be careful so that you do not do as the uneducated doctors who rush and are too bold, breaking the chariot every time, and bringing in nothing but what we have told.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but it comes sometimes from the onion of this great disease through its roots that remain, or because the cartilage is broken, as we have often wished;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the teeth are cracked, wash the root with wine or with ash and salt;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if it bleeds when the bone is broken, which often happens, apply the root of vinegar.
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the swellings are such that if you first try to extract the tooth, they have long points and large roots, which will not double back when you pull.
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And are long roots if they do not bend when pulled, and are thick limbs well made, and have teeth to hold them in place.
de la racine des dens	of the tooth root
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root stays at the cauterization, it is advisable to put some moistened cotton wool on the shoulder so that it will become swollen, until the swelling subsides, for then you can loosen with tongs called "algefri", because the joint seems like a sore.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and they are made similarly to a lime and that's their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out from all these ties, so it is fitting that you uncover the whole chariot around the root, and put the instrument which is called "althal", namely palm, in order to make this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be thick and large if it does not break apart, and if the root jumps out of that, it is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if that does not happen, if you use all the instruments, then the shapes will come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if it is helped by this instrument which has two veins, then surely the form will be:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front in the region of the teeth, and from this instrument which seems like great pincers, whose form is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And if these instruments are strong that they cannot break, and when you know that many instruments are needed;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also of other disorders which are not mentioned;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise masters who are subtle in their treatment use it himself with his own instrument, according to what he has shown by his work and the disease, for there are some diseases where the ancient physicians do not know how to treat an instrument because of the diversity of these and so when they break a bone or other bones, if they search for instruments that are needed, I have told you, and helped with gestures, because this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and well-held to hold the bone, so that it does not break, but can still be held and removed;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the patient to the use of medicines suitable for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, so that he can make full use of this instrument;
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth are not as they should be in accordance with their natural form and the shape is ugly and especially in young girls, it is necessary that you know whether the teeth are new after the tooth, and it is not in its rightful place, and one cannot endure or fix it.
adonques lou raie;	so therefore the line.
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is near the tooth, take this instrument which has its form and resembles a small beak, and it should be made of iron in good quality.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut the gum with a small instrument daily because of the hardness of the tooth, and in order not to move the other teeth, if it appears that you can put it in, take some kind of glue as shown here.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and is also like the nail that you make the needles from.
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and in lime, pound the tooth with teeth for several days lightly, until it does not move at all.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	The patient should let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the tooth in front of a lock, or by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press up to what they bite, and you have cured them with restraining medicines, then this does not help.
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if they would restrict with a thread of gold, because the threads of silver turn green and rot, but gold does not change its form.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and so that the threads are neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you see straight between the teeth, take the thread and put it double the space between two healthy teeth, then insert the stitches between the affected teeth, as many times as there are, until you come to the healthy tooth on one side.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then restart the covering from where you began, and strain your hand subtly and carefully, until it does not move at all.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and bind tightly to the root of the tooth if he cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then strike the nails of the thread with tongs, and assemble them, and put them back between the sound tooth, and so that they do not bite the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then let him stay tight as much as it can endure, and if he loosens, or the threads come out, if they are strained with another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	so that it remains and serves like this for the full extent of its time, and that is the form of the teeth and the shape of the two sound teeth and the two molar teeth, as you can see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, so it is reset in its place, fresh as we said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and do not let anyone intervene who is not knowledgeable or skilled, and at no time make a dummy tooth out of an old bone, and place it in the affected area, and tie it up as we have said, and hold for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	There is no case where an intestine comes from under the tongue or in nature, that it happens as such.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by an accidental wound.
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the injuries are such that you open the mouth of the patient, and put their head on a healthy one, and lift up the tongue.
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	Then cut the nerve of the neck down to its large place, until the tongue is loose from its place, and if it has hardness or any other thing, and this is sudden pain, then inject the powder and cut down the tendon;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and make sure the incision is not too deep, lest it damage the artery which is underneath.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have finished, lift the patient up to hot water and vinegar, or cold water, then apply a cloth made of linen under the tongue;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and treat each patient with maggots every night so they cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if the blood comes out upon him, he applies vinegar to the wound;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the vein is not swollen, then burn it with the cautery slowly, which is good for those.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then let another treatment be done until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see a foul odor, whether it is red or black or hard, as long as the patient does not feel pain and you do not touch any point, for it is a chancre.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is inclining towards the whiteness and there is moisture, if you excise the tumor, and make a small incision with a spatula, and deliver from one side and the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the vein is not swollen at its surface, apply vitriol splinters to the area as long as it remains stained, and then return to its surface until you treat the entire area.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the limb from its rest and from its bed, and let the cure do other cures until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	Evacuation of abscesses from the throat.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	There is never a lump in the throat called "godath", and they are properly named the two glands, and when you treat them, as we have said in the section of division, and if they are not healthy, be careful:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if it has hard pus of little sense and of fleshy colour, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is big, do not touch it with iron either, because of the loss of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it be left until it is dead, and then you will take it out, because it would break apart by itself;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	In case the inflammation is of white colour and the roots are subtle, if you have prepared the instrument to cover, but first examine whether the pus-filled abscesses rest and are calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	So then have the patient sit in front of the sun, and his joints be healthy, and he open his mouth and the surgeon presses the lancet between his hands, and pushes the tongue down with it, so that this is the form;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and be made of silver or fine gold as much as the knife cuts.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Can you press the tongue with this entire instrument, and then you see the abscess, if you take a needle and thrust it into the horn, and pull out from above as much as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	And take no care of anything with threads or strings, for if you cut it with an instrument, it will show the shape that resembles force;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And every bone is curved, and one place is bent to another, and they are very good, and made of iron or antimony;
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument before it, then take a pair of tongs, because this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And if cut from one side, and the other side also.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other in the same manner also; and after making the incision, gargle the patient with hot, cold, and sweet water; or cook the rinds of pomace grapes, or myrtle shoots, and similar things, until the wound is stopped from bleeding.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then the cure is until he is healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And there are no other abscesses born in the throat except two mandrubs, if they bind them then as the two mandrabs.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside the throat, namely the small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and had tightly closed her whole throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked channel, and could neither eat nor drink, and she was dead if she stayed like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses are raised so high that they have been forced to break two times by two wounds on the neck.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	Then I did immediately, and put in one of the lancets, then the fire was applied, and a great portion of powder.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then re-examine another part of the body on the other side, and let the work proceed with the mouth open and pressing the tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After pricking one in those abscesses, and cutting off a part of it, only a little blood came out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And thus they cut off the throat of the woman, and now she began to drink cool water and then wine, and did not cease cutting that abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the abscesses reopened again, and filled up what I had emptied, until it became very large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	So I inserted and cauterized inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	Then she remained for a while without growing worse.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I depart from these parts, and do not know what God has made after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When a swelling rises up, and it is inflamed and long, if it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	And if it is very large and round, then it is called a "swelling".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit, and you see that the abscesses are calmed down, and it is subtle, then it is fitting to copy it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	And when it is round and assembled, but not long.
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	And if it is bloody or of the flesh color or black, then it is fitting to close the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is therefore necessary, whenever you see it, according to the manner I have told you, that you sit the patient in the sun's rays, and press his tongue with the instrument we remember having made here before.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then pull out the gall bladder from under it, and draw it out, and strike at both of the two fingers that I have told you about in the incision of the two glands.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not strike beyond the superfluity, which lies outside of its natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	because if you strike beyond it further, the voice and speech will be grievous.
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have told about in the incision of the two glands, and treat it so that it may be healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, it is advisable to use a fire engine at the cauterying of the painful senses.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is wet water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And the patient should put his head on your sound, and then press the tongue against the instrument that we have said in this chapter of cautery, with hot vinegar shoes, so it is not too thick or too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and then take hold of this instrument's edge, by which there will be the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And if on his head there is either one hair or some mucus, as with the hands of a spoon, and put the instrument all over the medicine on the eye;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient be gagged on his side so that saliva and mucus run from his mouth through the medicine inside, until they do not descend to the throat, and the bleeding.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand over the medicine and press it on the eye, for half an hour's worth of measure, until you see it numbed and the morsifications of the medicine are assuaged.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	If you see it, take cotton and envelop it over any instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and pour the instrument into all of that on the cloth in the cane above, until the cotton sticks to your eye;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and cast after four or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you have to repeat the cautery of the medicine, so that it is repeated, and after the cautery wipe all around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and purify what is around the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be given cold water to drink, and be cured with gargles until he is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This cure is safer than cauterization.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	When cured by fumigation in this manner, take calamus, hyssop, and origanum and rue and camomile and such herbs, and mix them all together or any of them in a pot, and make it into a paste, and boil.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	And the pots should be well sealed with strong earth, and have a handle as in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And be of silver or lead, and put one of the needles into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises up to the eye through the nostrils, until the eye is numbed.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	afterwards it is repeated often until the eye dries up, and remember not to do this at the beginning of the onset of the swollen abscess, for many things happen.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not do this except when the blood blister forms.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	and if this instrument is not present, take a knife and put it inside the patient's mouth so that their throat does not get too hot;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	because the heat of the knife does not weigh down the breath, and this is a good cure for good health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	often it hurts at the throat, as if on an arrow of fish, or nothing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so it is fitting that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instruments, so that you may see the thing.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what does not offend and is returned to the throat, it is fitting that you make the patient vomit so that the meat may be cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	In case of an accident if it happens by vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of onion, or a root of lettuce, or a dry bread crumb;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie the sponge to the spine and then cut it.
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when she comes to the patient, if he swallows, and then you pull it out.
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if she does not come by what we have said, then take the instrument of force according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And if the instruments are curved at the head so that it can enter more easily into the throat, and the head is lifted up high.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	And beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all your life goes, or do not thrust the bone into the throat.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and hold fast that you pour the instrument into him, for he will feel it unless the thing is smooth.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if she vomits, or brings it forth unevenly with the instrument, until all of it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	about the cutting of the throat.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	there is no medicine if he has not been treated with the medicine as I said in the division.
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when he does not profit from it, then look to the throat of the patient in the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the wound, so the arrow has come out at its small end, or you have fine tongs that are worth it.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	If this is not worth it, take a caustic horsehair, and put the bottle in the throat of the sick person, then pour or touch the caustic horsehair to the warm metal, and do it often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the sick person suffers from water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take full doses of cold water to drink, and work the mouth open, and swallow in that direction, and move it with your hand many times.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if at once they feel the cold water, spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if she does not spit as we have said, then perfume the sick person with asafoetida, at the instrument that I mentioned for the fumigation of the nose.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, because she will vomit with tartar.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the way of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are charcoal sticks, and it is covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in that place are the keyholes of the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then I will administer the purgation, and the patient will put their head in a cage, and close the mouth, so that the smoke does not escape from it, but comes out just there.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the blood will now flow, and if it does not, repeat the purgation many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient will suffer from thirst, and eat unclean and spoiled things, and shall not drink any water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and therefore the case is considered to be resolved by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the blood, namely, when it is visible, resembles curved tongs with nails that enter into the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	And has a resemblance to the neck of the doctor, and it is rough like lime, so that whoever takes it will not be able to let it go.
et vez ci la forme:	and when this occurs:
li chapistres des apostemes	The physicians who treat abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many symptoms of abscesses are found in this book, and they vary according to the remembrance that comes after both in front and behind.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is two ways, one of which is the same as itself, and by what it holds together.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second kind is for when they are inside or in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	because the abscesses in the head are different from those on the lower jaw, and the abscesses of the shoulder bone are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if in abscesses we should not pierce it, until the bowel is dead according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if there are some that it is necessary to pierce them when they are thought to be dead, and do not die according to their completion, as abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess comes from the joints, and one leaves it there until it is full of pus, by chance if it infects the ligament and nerve of the joint, because that is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Where the abscess is close to the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is dead, it will harm the principal member;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or if you cut to the foundation, if you cut so that it dies;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not good to pierce the abscess while its digestion is complete, because the heat will penetrate too deeply into what lies at the foundation, and thus cause it to burst outward, and a fistula will form;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot be cured in great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	and you must know the urine of the perforation of the abscess which is dead according to completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the departures of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the dulling of the swelling and the sharpening of the headache from the abscess, and other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	And you must place the opening so that it is seated above or below the abscess, and where they make a hole.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And so the opening should be in the long bone of the body, and if the abscess is near the hands or feet, or in joints, nails, and arteries, where they are even and there is no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those joints that are swollen, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And if there is an abscess in the jawbone, so that it will be left open until it has been fully digested and confirmed, just as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	But if you pierce in front of this, the flesh is filled with a large amount of filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance they harden and penetrate deeper into it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that must be pierced according to the size of the body, according to how much it needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you must bring in small abscesses, small punctures;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large punctures, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	And if there are such abscesses where it is advisable to shave the skin around it and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When the wound is as healed as if it were a dressing, and it is soothed, then it must be done in the same way as we do for boils:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are those that are cut into three parts, and if there are such wounds where one cuts as with the gallnut of myrrh, just as abscesses from thorns;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are those where one makes a round cut, and other sizes, and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who do not have a head, like superficial abscesses, it must be that you pierce them straight through;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is advisable when the abscess is large and has collected great pus, that you pierce, but do not extract all of it in one hour, but only take part of it;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	Then I will stop the abscess from growing on the other side, then I will take out anything that is behind it.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this repeatedly in small pieces until the bowel has passed completely;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Even when the patient is weak, or a woman in childbirth, or small children, or old men who are decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	But you must hope for the worst-case scenario at all times with the outcome of the pus, so that by chance the patient may die, and you will not be disappointed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Then beware of this chapter with great care, and when you have pierced the abscess, if it heals, and inspect whether the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it's a clean cut, then apply tanned linen or old cotton strips;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it's a large abscess and there's much pus, then you should sew into each one a tent so that they come together.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have hit a part of the abscess with your finger, and you cut it open, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cloth or rags of linen without moisture, and tie it to the same day;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the bones, and the one who heals with poultice until they are healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if you find blood has come out to your work, then tend it with cool and easy water and salt, and cover it with the same cloth again many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the pus persists, then apply some government and cure, and the poultices that I have told you to take in this book; and if it is during winter, and the pus is very swollen, then it is necessary that you put on tenths and draperies moist with wine and hot oil;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in this state, and the swelling is hardened, then it is necessary that you put on moist draperies with water and oil, or with wine and hot oil, every day, just as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then remove the abscess and clean it up and treat it, if necessary, so that it is safe.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this requires knowing universally in treating abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	Or you have said comment on must be told before treating abscesses, and thus here is the chapter.
des soros	he heals with fire command to the sick person that he lets the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the pus of head wounds come out small abscesses, and there are those things similar to cloth, as is the wick of a cat's skin, and there are many such appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fat and similar to pus.
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	And some that are hard and stony to cut, where there is no doubt if the artery is injured.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the arrow wounds of the shoulder are such that if you examine all the instruments called "entromissoire", because the form comes after this, what kind it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they will cut from above the long bone.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is dry, if you scrape off the skin around it, leaving nothing behind because it comes back again when you leave nothing.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Plunges cotton soaked in Egyptian oil, if present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, soak it in water and cloth, apply the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And those who will be left overnight.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then resume the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the bandage, until you know well that it will not stay overnight;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with oil suitable for it, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscesses do not burst out soon, apply according to this form, repeatedly.
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and then take out the pus, and scrape off all its parts, and put all your care in treating the wound where it is.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the arteries cause a contrary reaction, then do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do thus with an abscess if it is hollow, and when cutting and when curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And he cuts on the abscess if it is hollow and moist, for if it is lighter, because there is less blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of those abscesses or swellings do not have any moisture and if the second abscess that I copied or the swelling of an old woman's head,
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the abscess just like a cold, hard stone, rough and frozen, and it could not break.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if we have found any blood in it, then we have performed a wound just like cutting into stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses that come or swellings elsewhere, wherever these occur on the head of children and the roots of the ears, always open them right away until they begin to flow.
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat him accordingly.
des scrophules	Described by scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	This happens often to abscesses on the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they occur elsewhere or in the body, and are very foul, and often join one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each abscess is properly located within its side, as the wound and the swelling of the head, as we have said.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the similarities to these abscesses are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malignant and do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one where you see good disposition at the elbow joint, and it is similar in color to the flesh, and mute from every part, and not inflamed like the veins of the neck or artery, nor shallower than the ribs.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	therefore it is convenient that you copy it from above, and scrape off every part, so that both lips are of the color of the gums, if you need to, as we have said about wounds on the head.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and the wound is small by small, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or the vein, and do not apply the salve too loosely nor prick with needles, lest your hand tremble, and your sight be blurred, so that you do not cut what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cover the vein or artery, and that does not allow you to continue, apply vitriol on the wound to break it, or any powder that stops the bleeding, and hold the wound closed.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and let it remain until the abscess is allayed, and the wound is softened, and begins to discharge.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the sutures are loosened, return to your work, until you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	After they prick at it, see if there are any small swellings that will not go away.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein in the swelling, so that you should not cut it except at its root, but tie with a strong double thread and let it fall down without trouble.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply a wound of old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then the treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you hit the entire scrofula, it is fitting that you assemble both lips of the wound and sew now, because there will be no remaining fluid from the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is fitting that you listen to cover the root of it, and treat with force, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those swellings that have excessive swelling, prick it on either side where it is open.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and prick it so that it opens like the one we mentioned before, depending on its condition; then apply poultices with ointment and similar things, if it corrupts what remains of the corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, so long as the dressing is kept tight.
de squinance	of squanderment
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	They said and spoke of the operation on the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	But it is necessary for those who have cut their throat that the opening of the throat called "epiglottis" be avoided;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	And do not help them because all the veins and the flesh in the patient are found at those who have made a deep cut in the mouth, or throat, or both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the membranes, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it under three circles or four a small incision through the quantity of the incision over or between the two circles, neither in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and they are thus considered suitable for epiglottectomy when there is no scar, and the vessels are long in size.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the masters are fearful, it is recommended that he extends the skin of the throat to its fullest extent, then cuts the wound as long as it comes to the neck.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and excise the wounded vessels, if you see anything, and then cut into the sac, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and demonstrated by the section of the tongue from the neck, because it springs forth from the animal that is broken, and through the defect of the voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open a little.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour is past because we doubt strangulation, assemble both lips of the wound from which it came, and the skin all torn away towards the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that cause pain, until it is cured.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this (cutting) until the throat is completely stuffed, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect in the liver.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore secure the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and the ancients ordered to leave the wound uncovered until the illness is passed, and it is passed in three days or four days; therefore they ordered that the wound be sewn and cured until it was fully healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young woman took an arrow, and stuck it in her neck, and cut off part of the hair on her forehead.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure her, and found her in the same condition as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had been drawn from it, and I saw well that she had not injured herself nor cut her vein only to the throat, but that the vein came out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I had to leave, but I sewed up the wound, and cured her until she was well.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and this happened to the young woman that she remained red in the throat, and returned after her illness.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because of this I thought that there was no fear in the throat's sewing (or opening).
de la grosse gorge	of the great throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it's a large abscess in the color of a blackberry, and it's very common among women.
et est selonc II manieres:	And occurs according to two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	Nature (by art) and accident.
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Or it has no cause or origin.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accident occurs in two manners: because one is similar to a bruise, and the other is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it is not advisable to apply hot fires only in one who has a small wound, and he must examine and probe the interior.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it like a bruise and there is no inflammation, if you cut, as one cuts the skin, and remove all its covering, if there is nothing else.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and carefully search all of it, and the doctor as he wishes, until he is completely healed.
des nous	from ourselves
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways to us that I will tell you all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary that I tell you all the differences between a thing and its opposite.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that when an issue is present and fever persists, until the ebullitions have passed and it has been completed by puttingridity;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	and therefore the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With nothing, there is no heat, no fever, and no pain, but it contains the spleen, which are its own sacs, according to the color of the body, and begins to swell like a bag, and becomes large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two forms, or grays, or moist, and much of their color as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of this thing, that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument called "entromissoire", according to its form or chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses is that you prick or moisten it more than what you find at the abscess, and turn your two fingers back and forth slowly until you see that the strumens have pierced the heart, then so much according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then pull out the middle layer, and be careful that it does not burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the corrupted skin is cut off, as its color is, just like for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if the middle layer does not come back moist after cutting it off, know that it is fatty, so cut it across, and take hold of it with pincers, and lightly scrape off each part, wearing a cloth where you place it, in order to treat it soundly with the new.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot treat it with safety, then treat it by parts so that it does not stay.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	but if it stays, then it will return repeatedly;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it stays for a little while and does not cause you harm, then apply the wound to some sharp, acidic powders, tie up the wound, and put on soothing substances near the abscess, and perform other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the abscess is large, then sew both cheeks of the wound, and cure the one that swells.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the vein is swollen against it or otherwise, and you hasten to apply the new vitriol powder, let it be applied for two days or three days, until the wound starts to heal, and allow the cooling of the blood.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	Then comes back to cover what is left behind where it stays out.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Look here at the forms of interstitial swellings, and they are three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	large, medium, and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and in it there are three quarters, which are called "albrets", and one which is called "breb", and there are them in three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, to enclose the swellings of fistulae;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and are also like the needles with which we sew the sutures, and are of citron iron, or steel, or silver, and move to match those who are yellow, and are more convenient for sewing the swollen bags of a fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	And they are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Grands, moindres, and little ones, according to the size of the wound.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of ulcers are many similarities, just as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	Grands, moindres, and little ones;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if ulcers have two corners of three kinds also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if ulcers have three corners, and are so of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if ulcers have two corners, and one corner only, and are of three kinds;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And all this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of those who do this injury are made sharp, and of such men there is one who does not cut through evenly from both sides, from which we scrape the skin, so that you do not cut the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these insertions are the arteries returned in handbags, so that the patient does not lose them when opening the abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	great, small, and moderate, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and do not cut through more than in the thigh, like knees, arms, and breasts, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and at no time do they make another small instrument, like scabbards of fistulas, according to this shape, by which we stain the vein;
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it on no occasion at the place which is healthy to have veins cut, and arteries, and never return according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Never do the breasts swell up on some men when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like the breasts of a woman;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and keep them swollen and inflamed, and whoever wishes to cure them should follow this form of the line from 2.b. to 5.g.:
