puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and apply the wound with a medicinal ointment made of char, then close the two lips of the wound on sutures, and treat until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast swells down and becomes inflamed like a woman's, if it has grown so large that it is painful to touch, then cut two incisions on either side above.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that the one is tied to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from 2.b. until line g;.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape the skin which is between the two lips, and cut away the fat, and apply what we have said about dressing and powders, and what is necessary for the cure, until he is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if he is not healed, or the incision has not been entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the accumulation of blood, so it is necessary to fill the wound with moistened cotton in a corrosive salve.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until he has consumed the remaining and the fat, then treat him until he is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	The evacuation of blood from an abscess
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are hard scrofulas or it has scars, and if there is moisture in them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line .b. up to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the whole bow of the abscess is empty, apply the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment suitable for that until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofulas, treat them as we have said in incising scrofulas, and if the wound is about a vein, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the artery removal
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the veins are cut and the skin is bound above, if it comes to multiple abscesses, and so does it have a vein that has escaped and an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if it is found to be so when cut as far as the artery, because there are long abscesses within by its depth.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and if you feel it at your joints, then you will have straining.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is due to a vein, if there are signs of swelling appearing.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and this is madness when covering the abscess, and especially when it is under the armpits and in the neck, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to abandon the iron treatment, and those who have head problems should also abandon it, and for those with swelling of an artery, make a cut above the skin for a long time.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then cover the chest with a sheet, and let it be exposed completely so that the artery is discovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then take a needle and pierce it just on the other side, and tie off the artery with two thin threads of silk, as I have taught you in the extraction of both arteries that are located in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then point to the area between the two threads of an intestinal instrument until there is no more inflammation and the abscess is cut open;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply a poultice made of herbs, as it was decided by the physicians, until the wound closes;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat this condition similarly to those, so that it may be cured.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	If the artery is near the size of the vein, so it's convenient to stain your hand with that, as much as you can apply the arrow from the vein to the whole skin, then pull out the needle from the place where you are holding your hand, and pierce it again, and let it go twice, so that you draw it from one side of the skin.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then tie the arrow, just like I told you, or connect it with one of the two parts of the second joint.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the threads won't come out, so I tie another needle all over each thread under the incision of the first needle.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the arrow until the superfluity comes out, then cut the superfluity again at the point and let what's tied.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The patient is then placed under a wet cloth dipped in wine and oil, and then given treatments of poultices and ointments until they are healthy.
des apostemes des ners	In the wounds of those who have suffered from this cautery there are often evacuations of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	So too do abscesses come in the artery and vein, and abscesses appear at the wounds when they are fresh, or due to excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often at the shoulders and elbows where there are joints, and it's an abscess, and its color resembles that of the flesh, and is accompanied by many dieings from pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when they are stretched tightly, the patient feels pain, and it's not exactly as painful in the chest, but rather below the heart.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	And it is quiet in all parts, and does not go forward or backward, neither up nor down, and the one who has joints should not be covered with iron.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	perhaps it will contract;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and those who have a skin wound on the head or on the forehead, perform the dressing with the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If there is an abscess that needs to be cut open, if you have a pair of pliers and cut at the root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, if the patient has applied an onion to clean and scorch it, then cut the bone and sew the wound to the chest, and the cure until he is well.
des grosses boces pendans	of great mouths hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	It never occurs in the abdomen and not in any other part of the body, it is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to an abscess, with subtle roots and fat.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and in it there are both small and large ones;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw in the home that had two people who were ill with a disease which was more like fungi than any other thing, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a small root, and their skin was split, and it corrupted afterwards with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I took one of them and found that it weighed 18 ounces in the other, because if you look at the incision on a patient who is moist, and the color of the ulcer is pale and moist with a subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if you scrape it with a spatula large, and they are in your presence the cautery on fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	But when cutting comes with many great bleeding, and if they do not watch you, then hasten then to the cautery.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	And if you see the patient is anxious and fearful of the incision with fire, take a well-made thread from below tight, and bind the ankle so that we have said, and let it rest for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	And then hold the thread tight and do not cease to tighten it until it cuts through the ankle, feeling it with each cut.
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	And if the roots are thick, if he is afraid to cut himself with the same motion on his abdomen, but you can well cut half of it, then cauterize it so that it does not return.
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then treat the wound, and make sure you do not cut the root which is of poor quality color and sensitive to pain and inflammation.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	This is an enchantment or spell, and I came to this cure for the chancre after.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil bursts
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of a wound comes from cautery of a cut or a slice in the scapha, and it is on the belly and in some areas of the groin, so as to happen in other ways, or from blood that cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness.
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it's from the cut of the scapha and from the exit of the bowel, so that the color of the abscess seems like the color of the body, and is a light thing with pain, and opens to various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it comes from the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when you press on both sides, it returns, and then goes away, and by chance it becomes scarred, and increases greatly at the entrance of the bath and for strong work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	and if it's because of moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press with your hand, do not constrict.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it's because of blood, so it opens by these signs: big and hard abscesses, and they occur in a certain quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to a wind or illness, so that the shoulder is soft, and the wounds are such that you should examine whether their appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is fitting to leave the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	But because of doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter about abscesses, for arteries and veins.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	and if their appearance is for the intestine or the gall bladder, it is fitting that you instruct the patient to bend his knee, and lie down straight, then stitch everything around the wound.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then command the patient to lie supine between your hands, then go around the knee that you have stitched all along the abdomen, then cut the half of the abscess above all the great incision.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie the patient around a strong thread or a cord of strong silk tightly, and secure him with that single ligature.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	After the fire cautery, work on the half of the abscess is stretched over the ligament, and insert your instrument into it, and choose the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught on the ligament, release it, and insert the intestine into the space outside of the abdomen;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find it is burned, take it out by the sinus, and cut off its superfluous part;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the arteries cause contractions or the veins, go well into them, then return to your work and take out two arrows, and insert two needles, and push them back in the way you made them pierced;
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then strain the abscess in four leagues above the needles, and if you see, take out the needles, and let it remain until it stops oozing, and cut off the dead part by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	When you strike it when it is subtle and poor, then the cure will do what it should, and cut off the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or the moisture you find, then cure the patient of what they need, and bind the joint.
dou chancre	A skin sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	As we have said in the division of the chancre, and how it should be treated with medicines, and how one must avoid iron treatment;
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and say that the chancre infects in the groin, and great care must be taken in its treatment, and the ancients said that when chancre is present on the flesh, or can be scratched as chancre on the breast, or in the testicles, and similar places, one should remove all of it when it begins to appear.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	And when it is great and old, so do not approach it, for I have never seen a sinner.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	I have never seen anyone cured in front of me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And in the case of ulcers, when it is in its place or can be removed, as we have said, is that you should never purify the patient with black bile.
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make the patient healthy if he has shown signs of fullness, and then make the ulcer in its proper place.
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then cut off your ulcers or chancre, and the head of all parts, and remove the bone from all parts without leaving anything behind.
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and expect well that it will heal in its own time, or at your hand, or at anything, and if they start bleeding from the incision of an artery or a vein, then cauterize until there is no more bleeding.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Now the patient must undergo another cure until he is healed.
de ydropisie	Fever of dropsies.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have previously described the similarity of dropsy, and in what way the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each one, and the medicine that is used to treat it, as well as those who are cured with iron.
si est eclites soulement;	if only it has inflammation;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and iron should not be touched in these two similarities:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	which are tympanitis and suppurative arthritis, because it is a mortal thing;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	Therefore when you use medicine for this similarity of dropsy called "eclites" and the cure does not work, if you examine whether the patient is weak or has another illness than dropsy, such as stomach problems and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	If it's not touched with iron, because there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient of great virtue, and he has only dropsy, and is neither too thin nor too large, then thus operate:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Lift the patient upright on your hands, and the attendants press the abdomen towards the bottom of the groin, then take the spike (or pointed instrument) according to this shape:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let them cut from both sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	pointed, so that there is neither too great an entrance, lest he come to the intestine when you pierce it, and cannot be closed.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then examine whether the dropsy is located near the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	It is necessary that you cut around the swell of the third. You must cut downwards from there over the nail.
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if there is an abscess on the left side of the swell of the third, cut.
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is because of the muscle, on the right side, and do not let the patient lie on the wound so that the swelling does not run to the weak part.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and the vein, and lift your hand to cover the space between the skin and the sac as you drain it out as much as an angle or less.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the sac until the space reaches eight, and this is the point of the fluid, then tear it out, and drain this instrument from which this shape comes:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it seems like a chain of silver fine, made from iron or ash wood light, and in the part underneath there is little split;
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on this side it has three splits;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on the other side, and one on the other.
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the knives are cut like a pen, and this is the form of the incision that the scribes shape the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	on the top of it is the little bone, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it now rises up on the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	then you empty the third part, for if you empty more than it is necessary in this hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit due to the arm, or he will spit blood, or he will approach death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the disposition of his virtue signifies in the patient, and his hairs;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then take the instrument and hold the water, and it is held now because of the clot which blocks the puncture that is above the sac, as I have said, so you should pierce according to this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then continue the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering from it, and take a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do this on another day, and guard yourself from folly until it does not remain but a small amount of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	and if you doubt the patient, and you give a great amount of water to them, if the doctor prescribes a burial or hot salt, and after much sweating or bathing, and drinking vinegar;
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the healer of medicinal remedies makes dry as soon as they are cured, and cauters on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the water, just as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the swelling of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without any deformity in the penis, or if there are deformities they are small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If they wish to pierce at once, so that it cannot be pierced on the entire length of the penis very subtly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	and then puts a subcutaneous needle deep into the flesh, and ties it and holds it for three days or four, and whenever he wants to make urine, if the stitches are removed, makes urine, and then puts them back.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and in case it does not come out at all, because the urine that comes is not held back.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those of whom there is a puncture are small, if it is treated with the clove of garlic, as we have said, because they will swell.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	those who do not have the needle in their own body are blackened, because no one is born with the needle on the head of the penis, because they cannot urinate before lifting their penis up.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot come by injury because the material is unable to reach just at the spot where it occurred, and this is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the way of the work is that the patient lies on his back, so the head of the rod is placed and cut with the same length as a grain of barley, so that the puncture marks in the middle, as it should be.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and beware of the bleeding that often comes, and if it happens, if the one who bleeds causes the bleeding, treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of swellings of the rod
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times come cysts in the rod, and this is an ugly appearance.
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and some are malignant while others are not.
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	If it is necessary to grasp them at one time subtlety, then hold and cut all of them, then put cotton moistened with Egyptian oil on the wound.
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the dressing be repeated until it is safe.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the inflammation is malignant, of a foul color and smelling, then it is fitting that you apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you cut it and the flesh is tender under the edge of the wound, with some inside the skin and some outside, if necessary, then you must take out the flesh that is inside first.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	And when it is bound up, remove it afterwards.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	Because when you cure the joint together, be sure to secure it so that the flesh is not perceived on the edge of the wound, for then blackening and corruption come onto the joint.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to cover all that which is black and corrupted, then tie above the affected area with a plaster made of honey and flour, which is made from pomace of grapes and walnuts, then cure other remedies until he heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if the hemorrhaging comes, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cautery can help in two different assemblies:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	that is to say, by stopping the flow of blood and by preventing corruption.
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the staff is corrupted and withdrawn, then it is necessary to tie or conduct a cord around the staff, and pour the patient out among them.
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the hair grows on the head of the staff that has touched those who have not been circumcised, or it is wounded or infected, then it is necessary to scorch it with an instrument like a razor, until the bonds are loosed, and deliver the head of the staff from all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if it is this painful thing to examine, then it is suitable that you scorch with the staff of the spindle any point on the scalp and beard.
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then serve it well between two, and place under one of the fingers, so that it does not burn directly.
de la circoncision	About circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	There is no difference in healing from other wounds.
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	all means should be used if we do this work on our own will, and especially for children, since it is necessary to make the best and easiest treatment for their safety.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	They did not say that they cut the circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	Because I have sought the greatest part of the masters and healers who performed circumcisions during the time of our lord, and learned many things.
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	If it is frozen because of the cold, and by chance if they hit those above and lingered there below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Or they recover the wound, and there is great pain, and because of the inflammation that does not have a certain degree to be sure about the tip of the member;
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and because of the inflammation of the ulcer by chance they stop the iron, and they treat the wound, and many times it happens so that it needs no further treatment and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Through the cleansing which is done on all parts of the limb I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut exactly equally above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	Because when you press your hand, if they are equal in size all around the skin tenses;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the thread is well drawn into the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and if the manner of the first operation is that you think of the child, if it understands, then you make only to tie the thread around the rod so tightly, and only do so in all kinds of ways as you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	Then make him sterile between your hands straight on, and then bring back the strength between your hands or below your feet that the children do not see, nor any of the swellings.
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	Then put your hand on the vein and blow or kiss it, and take it up so that the head of the vein is exposed.
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then clean it well of the dirt that is assembled there, then bind with a double thread, and tie below the point to another point.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	And tie it to the second joint with the double thread on the pouchet and the vein's index, cut between the two threads, then lift the wound up immediately and take out the head of the vein.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	Then let the blood flow little by little, for it is the mother.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to put powder on and above the powder; and drizzle with a mixture of rose water, cooked from milk, desiccated in warm water, mixed with good olive oil and fresh, and let it dry for the next day; and the cure will perform another cure until he is cured.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	If this is the form of force during purification,
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The two heads are closed and pinched, and the size is equal to that of a finger.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	the error during purification occurs when the keys inside are torn at the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	therefore it is necessary to extend it to your vein, so that the abscess forms.
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	And let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	But if they have been bleeding for three days, and that which is below the vein is swollen, let it be left to allow the swelling to subside, and scorch lightly.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If you cut it as the movement allows, and keep away from the vein part, it will do no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Therefore cure the swellings of sudden wounds with powder, as we have said when treating powders, and if you cut too far over the measure, it will rise up to the top, doing no harm.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore cure him as we have said, until he is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	When retention of urine occurs.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to obstruction by stone, or freezing of blood, or bowel obstruction, or a blockage in the neck, or similar things that we have mentioned earlier.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine is not flowing, and you see that there is a retention due to a stone being lodged at the neck of the bladder, then it is advisable for the patient to be raised up on his knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	And let the stones be put on his back, and extend his belly from above his back, and restrain the patient as far as he can.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And thus the neck of the bladder is constricted to express the stone at the top, for the urine will flow again.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patients feel great pain, so you should administer extraction to all the instruments that are called "siringue", because of this form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it be made of subtle and light silver thread, like the feathers of a bird;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and it be half an inch long palm wood and subtle at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of the issue of urine if it is that you take a double thread, and tie to the head a small amount of wool or linen, and pour the head into the "siringue";
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and seal the superfluity of the linen and pour it just into the head of the "siringue", then anoint the siringue with oil or butter and powdered aloe, and have the patient sit on the stool, and raise the bladder and the phlegm moistened with oil of olives and water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	Then gently insert the suture into the vein, until it comes to the root of the vein, then double the vein above over the wound.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then pour the suture before just reaching the bladder, and feel that the patient comes to just before the empty space, and this is not done according to this order because it was twisted in the way it was supposed to be.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then pull the thread all along the spine very little by little, and the urine follows the thread, then extract it and make the patient urinate;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And restart the suture until the bladder is empty, and relieve the patient's pain.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorching or pus comes to the bladder, when putrefaction is assembled, and you see water and medicine dripping, do this with all the instrument called "clepsedre", and it's the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed and if it has three holes:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	We come from one side and we go from the other;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the swollen veins, because of which the medicine can be applied so that it covers well the part with an addition, if possible to treat the moisture, and push when necessary is;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see that you can get your medicines into the bladder, put the chief seat in the moisture, and draw as soon as possible are;
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you drain the moisture at the keeper, and then push hard the pulling in.
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	if the moisture enters again, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the subtle form of the cystoscope by which you can cauterize the bladder:
si est ci:	If there is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is of silver or of copper, and the nails are higher.
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and lower than where the sinew meets.
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture which you see clotting like a vessel, then tie it between the two breasts to form a good double thread, and heat it over the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then pour the head into the vein, then strain your hand on the vessel with all the moisture immediately, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the vein;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you don't have a vessel, take a piece of parchment and make a circle on it, and pierce it all around.
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	Then put a strong poultice on these wounds, then assemble the circle as you assemble the gall, and place inside what you see with oil, moisture, and water, and bind it in the instrument.
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do so as you have made of the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture appears in the bladder.
de la piere	From the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have said in the division of stones and the extraction of medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and I have said the difference between the stone that burns with fire and rain, and all the signs, and in which stone one must cut or reduce.
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder and in the phallus;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you about it plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stones which are entrapped in the bladder occur more often in children, and it is a sign that the water jumps out of the bladder like water in its subtlety.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and if the wound is opened and he pricks his patient's finger, and then pierces it multiple times, and afterwards poisons.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and after many of those wounds, the foundations collapse;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and it is lighter in children until they are four years old, and is very troublesome in the elderly, and is at the joints which are between youth and old age;
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and it is easier to treat those who have large stones than those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, so it is fitting first to purify the patient by cupping, in order to draw out all the blood that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	But it is often not worth seeking to cut stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Take the patient by the feet and pull them down and move downward so that the pain descends to the bottom of the bladder, and do not let it rise again on him;
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then place the patient seated between your hands prepared, and let his knees be down below his thighs so that the bladder is all inclined downward;
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then draw it and touch inside;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten and cut on the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not come out on the toucher to all, wet your right index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is sick, or your right middle finger, if the patient is young and accomplished.
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	And let the bottle be placed in its foundation, and to pierce in it, and when you sense at your throat, if it is small at the neck of the bladder;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	Then press upon it at your throat, and the bottle in front as soon as you see that you are cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and he commands that he extend his right hand to the fingers up high, and his left hand pull back the skin which is underneath the fingers at the place where you are cutting.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then take out the spatula (or spoon) and cut it, for this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And make a hole between the fingers and the foundation, not in the middle but to the left side of the right skin.
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and so it should be straight on the stone, and your toes should be tied to the ground or foundation, and if the size of the stone requires a larger opening than usual, but also narrower inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	in case the pressure causes the toe to jump or fall out of place.
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and see if there are any stones or edges where it has corners and margins.
si est griés a issir;	if it is brittle and prone to cracking.
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is something that is smooth, like the sound of a bell, and round, from which light issues.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	Therefore, if it has corners and edges, make the incision larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	And if it does not break, so it is advisable to strain the nails which are like a lime at the top, to press down the stone so that it will not escape.
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	where you pour into the subtle instrument curved at the top;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot put it in that way, enlarge the pore of the puncture, and if it is not smoothed out, strain with glass.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there are more stones, pour the largest one into the bladder's neck first, then cut it up, and then pull out the smaller ones afterwards.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then make a larger wound and cut.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	or he dies, or his urine comes out in abundance because of a wound that the pus cannot dry.
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	But force yourself to pull, or to cut with shears, until you pull it apart by pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	And when you have completed your work, apply the ointment of encens and aloe and dragon’s blood to the wound and bind it; and place above it the drapery moistened in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the abscess.
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Then revive the patient on his neck and do not release the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release it, apply a lot of oil and water to the patient well, then give him an application of diffinicon and basilicon ointment until he is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if the abscesses come to a boil in the wound and cause corrosion, and a frozen mass of blood forms in the bladder, and it is retained by this means, which is known in this manner, that without urinating with urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Push it then onto the wound, and extract that blood, because if it stays, they will bleed the bladder, and burst.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift the wound with water and aid, and help in all kinds of ways that you know, until it is healed.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is fitting that all the treatments you administer, bind both knees, and assemble the medicine on the patient.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is near the urethra, and stuck, and the urine cannot come out;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	so that the treatment for what I am saying is to cut off repeatedly, you are excused from cutting again for this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tried it thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take iron according to this shape and stick three nails into one tile:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Now take the flesh of the child and wrap it around the joint under the stone, so that she cannot come again into the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	Then pour in the forest lightly into the joint until it comes out to the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	And turn the forest round to your hand in the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone on the other side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	If it comes to that point, then press your hand down on the thing which is remaining in the stone which is inside the joint.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it breaks at once and comes out with the urine, and the patient is saved;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	And if you cannot do that for any reason which prevents it, then wrap the flesh under the stone and around it, then make the vein run straight into the stone between the two tendons, then pull out the tendon, and untie the ligament, and clean the frozen wound in the injury;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the healer as long as he is sane.
de la piere des femmes	About women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It happens that a stone pierces a woman, and if it has happened once, the healer is troubled, and is forbidden for three reasons:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one of which is that by chance the woman is virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second one is that you cannot find a woman who knows how to shave her eyebrows, especially when she is clean.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	and the third reason is that by chance you cannot find a woman who knows this art of hands.
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth reason is that the stone in a woman's body is more deeply embedded than in a man's, because it requires a deeper wound, and great fear there is. And if necessity arises for this, you must take a skilled midwife, and to her you must go, and if you do not find one, choose a clever woman instead.
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And the present a wise treatment in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and commands that she do this thing which you command from the inquiry of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look very carefully if the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then he must put his thumb or root and search for the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, he must apply pressure with his thumb or root, and commands her to put her thumb on the wound, and squeeze and press her left hand onto the bladder form.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	and if he finds it, then it is fitting that she move her thumb from the entrance of the bladder to the lower part of the crotch, until she reaches the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	Then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh in the middle where it is swollen and meets the bone; there or you will find the bone.
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move his two fingers above or below the bone, and put them on the first joint.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then pour out the blood from the joint, if you feel it is nearby the wound as far as the bone can come out, and see that there are many kinds of stones.
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	this is to say, small and large, sharp and dull, long and rounded, and those with marrow.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and if they are not inflamed, pour on white vinegar and break it, and hold onto it for an hour until the skin is dried.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	Afterwards return to your work, until the bone is healed, and you have the strappings that I told you in the extraction of the bone for your own aid in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if the patient does not take it, and it is of the artery that has been cut, then apply powder on the limb and the strapping of tents and bandages, and do not resume this again, and let the bone alone, lest the patient may die by chance.
puis cure la plaie.	then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the wound is appeased, and the swelling subsides, then returns to his work, until the pain subsides.
de hernie carnouse	of caruncle or varicose hernia.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Ramsy water is nothing but a mixture of moisture or white syrup that is beneath the knee, which contains egg.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "syfac", and it is never properly found in the eggshell, if one thinks that it might be a different kind of egg.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and this is the skin of the elbow between the white flesh which we have said.
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and this does not happen.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this rice water is from weakness that comes to the joints, and it spreads out that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And never happens if it comes from a blow on the joints, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it's yellowish in decline, or without red, or black, or white and watery, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs of a certain assembly, because if it is white and fleshy as we have said, then it is abscesses in return, I do not see it long since like the figure of an ox, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in its own membrane, then it is abscesses with a part of the bone, and because of this one thinks it is another ox;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the groin and the white flesh, he feels well;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	then when you see the color of the moisture, if it appears on the entire inner quadrangular space, then the form is in front of.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Then judge what is inside according to what comes after the surrounding area.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we treat with iron, it is fitting that the patient be healthy according to our power and the replenishment of their body;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then he applies a bandage over his back on top of something high and puts a great deal of cloth on it;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then he places it above his left side and commands the minister to place it on his right, and extends the rod to one of the two holes near the groin;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Take the powder of silver and take it to the wound, and cut the skin around the navel up to its length until the point; and make your incision entirely straight in shaving the skin around the navel just like that white stuff, and scorch it subtly according to one's strength.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the white stuff from water into the large puncture, and extract all the water, and then place your linens, and fix the white stuff above.
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the skin around the navel, but only the white stuff.
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	cut it all or in pieces at the same time along its length, so that if you do not cut it properly with sharpness, it will return to flowing again.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the blood jumps to your side, then tie it off at its place when you have completed cutting the white stuff.
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then assemble the two leaves from the same wound at one stitch, then treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the corrupted vein of another disease, it is advisable to tie off the vessels that are superficially suspended, in doubt about the progression of the blood.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then tie off the vein to all that is superficially suspended, and extract the vein, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if an abscess is assembled in two parts, so that they are two branches;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	if you tie off the other part in the same way, then drain the blood, and put a clean line moistened with rose oil into the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another type of wool in oil and in wine, and put on the two sides, and cover it with doubled cloths, and tie it to all the thread that corresponds to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, and use woolen felt of the same shape and are sewn together in the neck of the breeches, and one of the knees takes hold on the foundation just below the back, and the other at the leg bone.
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two knees above the two arms, and so everything is stitched together in the loop of the girdle.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and at no time is this medicine a substitute for hot iron treatment in place of the size of metal, and so you take a cautery knife very fine, cut the skin on the sides, and be heated as we have said, until the white stuff that contains the water is uncovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the fire cautery according to this form, and pierce that spot on the skin, and scorch with this subtle fire cautery hot:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And cut it in all ways that you can, until you mark everything;
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and keep the fire from touching the eyes;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is more safe;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and beware of the danger of bleeding, and watch out for the work of injuries to the joints;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if no harm comes to you, or there is an abscess or bleeding or any other thing, then cure what harms you according to what has been said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	If the patient is fearful and will not wait for this treatment due to its horror, then perform perforation, just as I told you, and it is that when you are certain by the meanings we have said that water is laid down, so place the patient on a raised bed.
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	Then pierce the abscess at the lower part and to a distance equal in length to the breadth of the spleen, and make the perforation deep into the body.
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and so that the wounds are wide enough, so that all the flow of blood is stopped.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton on the wound, and tie it, and let it dry out until the remaining blood flows off, then treat him until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the whitened cloth does not allow the blood to flow out of the wound's mouth, then it is best to put in a quill or the instrument used for treating dropsical swelling, because this shape was as before.
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	Increasing the size of the wound, and observing that the pus returns, and it is assembled after six months or in what time it enters, when it is assembled as before, and thus will pass for the patient their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the teeth.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Observing that in the cutting of this branch there is fear of more deaths because of some situation, therefore it seems worth leaving it;
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and similar signs of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	Therefore, most abscesses come from flesh, and also cause pain;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and this is because of many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	which is that the acidity and water are spread out to the wounds, or by percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and does not bring any pain, and it is an abscess that causes grief;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and sometimes is an abscess that is painful and pious, with purple color, and never comes from a new artery, or swells the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is not from a new artery, it is discovered by the swelling of the abscess when you press on it with your two hands;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and should not be touched by anyone.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	The one that swells the vein is discovered by its swelling when touched with two hands, and it can be felt well by anyone, and on this appearance, and on others.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	And it is that you strike the heart of the veins, then stand up in the upper part, and throw the flesh down to white, and deliver the suspension from all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the vein is already swollen with these black marks, then it is necessary that you treat the vein and cut it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if there is blood in the flesh, or what is within the vessels, it is necessary that you deliver all of that vein, and cut it around.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the child is at your back side, it is fitting that you copy it all over and extract the phlegm, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your wounds are finished, apply the wound of soft linen moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat with other treatments until he is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the teeth.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess that has burst out with a swelling similar to the jawbone, with softening of the veins, and the patient dies greatly when it ruptures.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the cure for this disease is as frightening as before, and we will tell you about it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you place the patient on a high stool, then pour the suspension from the joints above to your two hands, all of the vessel which are near the groin, and stretch the masters, and extend in form;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	then strike with the spatula deep through the center of the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then burn from each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in the temples;
