Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small or large syringe is used when they are closed and bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and if there is a hemorrhage or the stomach is tied up, as you see, and the head is felt to be inside.
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and if it has a puncture on one side and an incision on the other;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And if a woman puts the medicine of a vessel of best or parchment on her belly, and perceives all around these small holes, and there are also among each of these holes an I must take space, then pour in these holes a strong thread from a very thick rope, and tie tightly as you would not do wrong on X or within them.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, if it sticks to the instrument with a strong thread, then close.
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and this is like the form of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And if the medicine is not too hot nor too cold, and anoints the head with oil or ash of beeswax, or some similar thing, then pour in lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then tighten the ministers' hands around both of his limbs, until he is totally whole, then extract the incision, and lift up the patient's legs to the view, and if the medicine comes out, so that the swelling will not be too big.
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he falls asleep tonight, then it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you blisterize him in an illness of descending wind, and the medicine comes out quickly, then he will start bleeding again until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	and if the hemorrhoids are on the fundament or abscess, whether on the soft tissue like an infant;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and it is the form of a small cyst above where the skin is tightly bound:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have said in the division the treatment for wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or we would say the treatments for hands and medicine according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they were made of, and according to the place or where wounds are made, and because of which they were made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	Things are made for wounds by cutting with a stone, sword, and knife, or lance, fist, or arrow, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or what are made according to the humors of the body, such as wounds that bleed on the neck, head, back, belly, liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds on the head, because it is written in his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I tell you that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if it is from a stone or similar things, be careful because the skin is completely torn apart and the wound is great, and you have some doubt about an abscess.
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if you treat it as soon as possible on the head itself if it comes from a vein of the wound, and treating the opposite side of the belly.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and the patients are replenished with wine and coarse meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not wish to be healed, so that his meat is made thin and he does not drink wine or eat flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and apply the poultice to the wound, if an abscess forms there, cotton wool soaked in oil or rosewater alone, or vinegar tincture.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess, apply to the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it does not move from the air, powder.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if they have moved it, apply some ointments until it is cured.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like a cut from a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be closed by stitches, then they are sewn together, just like I will say of wounds on the belly, from suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed to bone and splits, and does not hold together but only at one point.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then treat the wound with medicine, and set a hard cartilage in its place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat large quantities of meat, such as roasted flesh, just like fowl and bread, also similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	If you find rot or corruption on your skin, and it is not in the bone, then cut out the rot completely, and throw away, then see the doctor.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without covering, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then cut the artery, and if you find it loosened, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, then apply the cautery.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light.
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and apply this powder that will bind as well as the artery has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And here is the manner of the powder if it is:
pren encens une partie;	Take a piece of cotton;
sanc de dragon II parties;	Take half an ounce.
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	Take three live charcoals and the subtle powder; apply the wound and bind it firmly until the powder has absorbed well and united with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then tie it well, and let it remain until it does not swell.
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	because one should not lose medicine until the patient is cured.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes only calmed vivarium is used, when one does not have either the cense or the blood of the dragon, but the arrow has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	and if the arrow has moved the wound, especially when it was set, so as not to put on this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive ointments or flour of barley made with water and honey until it is cast in a bowl;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the cure of other treatments has healed him.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if an os fracture comes with the wound and it is small, so hold the bandage tight.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you this after the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is at the neck and it is simple, and there is no difference between it and a head fracture, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, so leave the cure alone and put no other binding on him, for he will have night sweats and they will cause him to retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not cover the wound with anything hot, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of this affluence is near the brain, which is in the higher members.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but if it is medicine, as calomel is dissolved in sweet water, and mixed with olive oil, and the calomel is also cooked in sweet water, and other minerals such as according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, so tie on gauze bands, then cure until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	If the wounds are deep and he is bald and full of blood, then let him be pierced more deeply.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	If the artery is cut and blood continues to flow in, if he has been turned, and lanced, and cauterized properly.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	If the arrow or the bow is cut from the throat, or if the neck is injured, and he is kept upright because his blood flows freely, then tie the neck with a string, so that the flesh adheres, and do not touch but rather apply pressure according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then bind tightly afterwards, and let him rest for some days, then the surgeon will treat his wounds with ointments until he is cured.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	If the wound has caused impression in the bone, then see it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And if it has pieces of bone, so that the joints are completely closed and you cannot see them, and those which you cannot see at all, leave until the wound heals and is closed, and make the joint straight again.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, so powder on the powder that I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is an abscess, then the treatment is as I have said in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from arrow or sword wounds
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it's a wound from an arrow or a dagger, and the wound is deep, then look to see if there are windings around the wound that will make the patient suffer.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	then you know that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it's not deep, and it's fresh with all its blood, then don't put powder on the wound in the first hour, nor tie it to stop the bleeding only when you have seen the vein closed up again, return to the heart, and care for the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	But I apply attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you do not have ointment, put cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and let the patient sleep on it for three or four days, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	but if there is no spasm, nor evil motion of the body due to a single movement.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the bone's disposition, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure it with various remedies and treatments, until he is completely healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot be healed and cured, then know that there is an abscess.
si la cure si com on doit.	If you prick at your base, hold your eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, and it's on the flesh, or on the back, then treat the part in front of it.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	even if it is large, stitch it up.
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it's small, use powder; and if it's stuck in the bone and has broken into fragments, apply it to the wound, and remove the festerings if they are open.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if there are no festerings, leave the wound to dry out, as this will ease the extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on different parts of the body, it is the judgment that is to be applied, as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	A fall from the belly.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The brokenness of the belly is large and square and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	Of great wound there is no time for the intestines to be introduced or for the nerves of the intestines, because of the introduction of pus;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the sutures are more painful, and there is no time when small wounds are better than great ones, because for that we put more pins in the intestines so that they do not come loose from both ends;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell soon after that they feel pain, if they are pinned down again, and for this reason it is better to have moist wounds, because we must tie up the intestines to their place, like others II.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And it is said that there are four kinds of belly cutting:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common wounds occur in the wound of the stomach, and the other wounds on the body have two other common wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And all of them are more suited with the wound of the stomach, and I will say each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I said that when the wound is small, and no part of the intestine has been severed, and a great deal is difficult to put back, this is one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because of the small size of the wound, as we said, or because the intestine is swollen from the injury.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, sew him in a certain way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	mix an onion with water and salt, or sew him with an ointment of hot water, or soak in hot water only, or boil it in hot water with herbs, and once the intestine swells up it will open;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And sometimes this treatment is repeated, and it weakens the soul to burst forth.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling departing, if you moisten the intestine with water or cook it and make them more bitter, because this is alleviating the entry to a little thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then they make a little cut in the instrument of which they press the hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	And the first treatment is to make it dry that we should not cut it further unless there is great necessity and it does not happen.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the stratum to be split;
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so it tears inside the hollow and does not fail, and then you see this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines bulge out, so it is reset according to its natural form in its own place, if you have the power, because this is best.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the stomach area, so you must make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the lower part of the stomach area, then raise his head and belly higher than the lower parts, and thus, if you meet a wound in one of the two parts, make sure that the navel area is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and so it is fitting to follow what I say in treating large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	For small wounds, apply what is suitable, then have between your fingers the pitiful minister who carries the entire wound in his hand, and put together the lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	And this is the common way of sewing wounds, and it is that you grasp a needle or arrows according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then let one inch from the edge of the wound two inches, and stitch with a good strong thread;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two nails of the skin with the two needles of the suture, from inside the skin, until you make it pierced from that part, and assemble the two ends of the suture four times;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then tie the ends of a double thread around the needle for two parts, then assemble the two ends of the wound immediately, and let one inch, and stitch another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then tie the thread of the yarn as you made the first needle, and do not stop doing that until all the wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be medium-sized, between subtle and coarse, because fine needles cut through all of it, and too large ones cannot enter very well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	because they should be medium-sized;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not fitting to push the needles too far into the flesh and on the sinew, because they cut and open the wound before the suturing;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cut the threads of the needles, so that they do not annoy the patient when sleeping, and tie or wrap the threads around the ends of the needles to keep them from coming loose, and leave them until the wound is sutured;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this way of sewing with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because there is one or two stitches.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second dressings are common, and are that you join the two skin bones and the two skin flaps together with an awl or have one strong thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have joined those bones together with four skin flaps, if the awl breaks into the part where you started it, in the way of sewing threads;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each dressing the size of half a small coin;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This dressing is seven days long, and I sewed a wound on one man who had an arrow wound in his abdomen, which was caused by a sharp sword, and the wound was over one palm of great size, and it included two palms of great intestine length, and the wound was towards his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	The patient's intestines I restored, since he had been ill for XXIV hours, and the wound was closed after XV days, and the treatment, and the patient recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they had predicted he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where no one could be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And applied a cotton cloth twice a day on the wound, and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and thread from the part in front of this one inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	until it has pierced the vein in a straight line, whichever side you insert the needle or thread first, then pierce it on the other side from this one inside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Instruct the patient to hold his ears steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second way of dressing wounds, which the Galenians call properly, is to assemble both parts together naturally and then apply one end of the suturing thread to the other end, in such a manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Stick an awl or a suture needle close to the site, and pierce it only, leaving the two ends of the suturing thread.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the awl and pierce it from the opposite side of that within, in both ends of the suturing thread.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then pierce one and the other from the opposite side to that within, in two other threads of suture on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most common way of sewing and the more so.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	The Galenians say this, and none of them witness it, so we should sew the abdomen with two needles, one having thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one needle should be put in from this side and the other from that side, like those who sew corsets.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and it is known that when a rupture occurs in the abdomen, the sewing is more painful than for other wounds in the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is like that of all other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, just as if the art had moved it, then reattach the intestine and sew.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	Then put on the powder and ignite the charcoal, and if they have moved it to some extent, then put on any ointment that is present, so that the wound may heal;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the thread, and sew up the opening, and apply the mercury;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound in the same way as the others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you do not have medicine, then put it on, immediately until it comes to a boil, cotton wool, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no need for other medicines in addition to these, when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wounds are making a community or spreading to the principal members, then it is advisable to apply a lighter linen soaked in hot olive oil or rose oil, and put it over the abscesses, and under the scars;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	And if he feels pain or corruption in the bowels, and this happens many times, for the cysts of black wine cause it, and likewise the corruption comes just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and the cut is made inside, and it's observed that when it's in the large intestines, it is easier to heal than in the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "youth" cannot be healed when it is barren, and this is because of the plant of women that is in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and its proximity to its natural enemies.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the gallbladder bursts from the wound, and it is put back in place like the intestine, as long as it's fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it's old and has turned to black, then it's proper to bind the patient who is black, because there are veins and arteries that do not bleed again.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut what is between the ligature, and hang both the gallbladder and the two fingers down from the part below the wound until the gallbladders spurt out, and the wounds close.
de la routure dou boueil	of cutting with a burn
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are wounded and the wound is small, it can be restored in some cases, because I have seen that one man was killed or pierced through the belly with a spear.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it was the wound in the right side of the stomach, and became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and from this arose vomiting and diarrhea.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it according to what I knew, and did not cease to apply subtle remedies until he was cured, and the symptoms disappeared.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw that it had healed, I doubted that the patients did not have an illness in their belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and it had no ill effects, but instead recovered in good health, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and said any experienced ones that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in that way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	tie the lips around the wound, and when the tie is pulled tight enough to close the mouth, put it on both lips if she pulls her mouth shut.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cut the head, and this holds so that it cannot be untied, and put another tie after in that manner as before, until the wound is completely closed.
et cout la plaie.	bind the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	This is done when the intestines are tied in the intestine of an animal, with a fine thread that has been cut from the intestine of an animal, in that way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the head of this thread from the intestine which is very much shaved, and then tie to the head of that thread a thin thread of linen twisted, then push the thread into the needle, and enclose the intestine, and pull it back into the wound.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of stitching wounds is not always successful only according to the way of expectation and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestine, there will be no gain or healing, unless using subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whichever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Since any wound or abscess, when it dries up, is called "fistula", and especially when it becomes swollen and has pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And an abscess occurs when the vertebra is infected with a hard, painful, and swollen mass, or one does not feel pain, and it is also similar to the beak of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in clear blood, and other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not healed, and does not have pus, is due to fire from one of the seven causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of the wound or the body;
ou por sa malice;	or for its malevolence;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because it has a hard purulent thing inside, and on the lips, which does not allow pus to form;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because there is too much blood.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	The thing with the feet is poor, and the material is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	for the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	because of which corruption is a sign of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in that place is late for digestion, and late for health, and flees by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones;
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have shown all these causes, signs, and remedies of medicine in the section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is fitting that I inform you of the treatment for a fistula, which is made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that an abscess has occurred in every member of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	because there are abscesses that occur at the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or in the sinuses, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or on the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	And if at some time it comes to the property of the main member, and so resembles them.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the ulcers that are of this kind are caused by harm to health, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if there is no ulcer that appears after I have said so and you have believed in the cure, and you see it grow, then take a piece of iron or flint, since the ulcer is straight, if it is curved.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	And if the ulcer is twisted, then search for a subtle attempt to flatten it, because the points are bent into the twisting.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	And if the ulcer has broken skin and you cannot see it well by searching with instruments, then clothe one of its wounds, because the moisture is too close to another wound, and infects.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Now the pain will arise in your power, that you may know if there is a bone or nerve, and it is stuck in the forehead, and ask the patient well about the pain they feel when pressing with your hand, and see where it feels.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you know truly where it is, and if it is near a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or any of the things I have told you, cut according to what I have told you, and be careful to remove the faulty bone and the corrupted flesh that are inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the cure until it is sound, and if the fistula is deep and straight, so that you can cut it, then copy into its depths as long as you can, and put moist poultices in medicine vinegar, and pour it onto the fistula's head, until the medicine corrodes the remaining superfluous matter at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then I apply salve to the open wound so that it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it does not heal by this method, then cut as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then strike.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve strikes you or the principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackening, then cut as much of it away as the corruption; and apply salve to the wound so that it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it does not heal, and the bow (or arrow) has been inserted in front, knowing that you are going to die soon.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	so uncover and cure it as much as you can, until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then put back in place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if he is thus treated, this is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	But if not so, know that the corruption has gone too far, and you will have no chance.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is only another remedy than from the lasser at nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if he has small corrupted bones and you can treat him with tongs, so that the strap fits well on him, and if he has many bones, then take out all of them, do not leave one.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture causes him harm, and there is no error or fear, cut through the moisture, char, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, set the wound with a poultice for putrefaction, and let it sit until the pus is inside the bones, and then they will be easier to remove.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	And if it is a great bone, such as the leg or thigh, then cut out only the corruption so that the black flesh is completely bone; then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is great part of corruption and comes just to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	so that it is sewn and covers everything just to the level of the corruption, and then treat him until he is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to someone at home in their leg, so that you may take example and help with your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	There was a young man of thirty-three years, who had pain in his leg due to something that came from within the body, until the materials came to the leg, and an abscess emerged and there was no apparent reason to open.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But the doctor by their folly overcame it so much that the abscesses opened up and they spent a lot of material, and it turned into a fistula, and many suffered severe damage to the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And many doctors within two years treated it with no success, and there was no skill in the art of hands, until I called upon them, and they came to his leg and the remedies used to treat him, and what caused by the wounds severely damaged the body.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the boy's skin became red and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I sewed a tent in one of the wounds, and then searched for all the wounds, and found that some came together at every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I then hesitated and cut into one of the wounds until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and perforated, and the corruption had spread to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I have been shown who was corrupted by bone rot, and I believed that there was no other corruption than the one that I retained;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with saltwater and soda, but it would not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began again, and discovered the bone as it was before, and found that the corruption had continued in the bone, and I saw it, and then I preserved it, and then I considered sewing it back;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not do so until I copied over the joint by palm of bone, and treated it to its full depth, then restored it with medicine;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it healed quickly and was sewn together, and I did not have to repeat the work for that patient again, except by the weakness of the sick one, who could not endure, and because of the fear of death that I had in him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often causes harm but if the patient is completely healed and in good health, and there was formed on his own bones a hard cartilage, he turned out to be of good disposition and did not have any inconvenience or contrary effect whatsoever, neither at rest nor when coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, so it must be dressed in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	bind the linen and strain the blood from the head of the bone which opens, and command that it be stretched in the top.
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another linen band on the bone that is first wrapped, and tie it over the flesh which has opened the bone, and stretch it to the head, so that you treat the corrupted flesh downwards, and uncover the good flesh as soon as you see it, so that the dressing does not cling to the corrupted flesh.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a thorn or a plate on top of the bone to cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to dress again whenever you can see and feel the corruption, and then again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted, and it does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, so uncover all the flesh.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then put the bone in place, and then sew it from one part to another, the higher the flesh is from the corruption, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is in the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint, and sew the bone where it contains from another part.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other artery than by covering.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if the corruption is at the finger of the hand, or at the toe of the foot, then it is very strong in that place, but you must always inquire about that corruption, how it opens.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	And clean it with all sorts of methods as you can, but do not let the vein or nerve be contrary to you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And know that the incisors and the hairs to cover these bones are many, according to the base of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is fitting to prepare each similarity of work with the corresponding instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the instrument which you have most need of, according to knowledge of this art, and evidence of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so that you may consider the instrument which you have most need of, according to what it is suitable for.
dou feu	By fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder can become dislocated due to either internal causes or external causes.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have treated the dislocation with medicine and it does not help, it is advisable to cover the affected limb from head to toe where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes death or by the malice of the limb's failure, which is more severe.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	And the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if it were burned with fire, and after the blackening, the corrosion of the membrane spreads to one part of the body and then to another, taking hold all over the body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you hasten to cover it, and if this is due to the impact of certain venomous beasts, such as scorpions from the sea and lizards and similar ones, and the corruption is at the head of the neck, if it touches, do not give it any space until it reaches your hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes just next to the hand, so the knife cuts at the joint, so that the corruption does not come before the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, so the knife cuts at the bone;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the bone, then it is death, and no fire or burn is beneficial except for a quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do so in the same way whenever corruption comes to the bone;
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	when it comes to the first joint, cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to a bone, cut all of the bone;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the thigh, cut at the joint of the knee.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes from above the groin, there is no other way to treat the patient except by killing them.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and tie the member in both above and below, and stretch some menisters one over one of the ligatures below, and another one over the other ligature above, and serve the flesh which is between the two ligatures to a width of one span, until the bone is uncovered.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or sew, and put a drapail of linen on each side so that the stitch does not touch the healthy part, and it comes to cause another wound and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if blood comes out when you work, then immediately cauterize the flesh or apply certain powders that restrain.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine until it is completed, then tie the affected limb with a convenient bandage, and treat the patient until he is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And then I will tell you what happened at home on that night:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	there was a black spot that seemed like a sore from fire, and this corruption came first on his foot and toes, until it consumed all of the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when he saw the corruption, he hastened to cover the foot, and was cured;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long after, the corruption returned to his hand, and it came to me, and I placed on him certain remedies after purifying the body, but he could not stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he says I will strike the hand, and I will not, unless I have hope of returning to matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also doubt that if I cut off his hand, he will not die, for the virtues of the flesh are weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he became desperate, and returned to his land, and sought to cover his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have done this without fire only because one does such things when one has need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No time is ever left for the abscess to grow and mature so long that it forms a great bowel.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they burst and perforate, and the bowel falls out, just like our intestines;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin that is above is just as subtle as silk, and does not run against the bone, or against the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy" and is not called "furuncle".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if she is so long that it comes against the bone in its entirety, then she is called "furuncle".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And the skin if is that you cut the whole piece of skin, and also when it is subtle, just as we weave.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have faith that the skin heals, and the corruption is not in its entirety, and the skin is thick with fat, then the physician will make a poultice like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look at if the breasts are large, and the bowels which are inside them are of a foul smell, then apply the Egyptian medicine that is made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take equal parts of ghee and oil, and lime juice, equally, and put them to cook in an ivory vessel over the fire until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take what is necessary of this according to your need, and put it into water and honey, and make a plaster for the breast, and bind up the wound;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine on for two hours, then extract it by pressing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breasts are well-formed and the pus is drawn out;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	And sometimes it's closed off by water of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and you take ashes from a grape wood, pour on the water, then let it flow, and close it up, until you know that the breast is well cleansed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	And if the patient cannot bear it, nor can he tolerate the Egyptian medicine or water of ashes, then when the closure of water and honey is applied, and there's a little bit of litargire broken;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	Or you close it with honey and wine, where the honey has property of purifying and washing, and the wine is made to dry the flesh;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And when you have done this, and you believe that the breasts are well purified, if the closure of this makes a fart in the body, and you take emplastrure diaphanite, make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	Instruct to bind or encircle with certain medications and ointments, of which I have stated the properties or treatment for the ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the rupture of the breast is small and the needle of the plaster cannot enter, then enlarge with a hot iron, and apply a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too large, so that only one side can be left open for the needle or plaster to enter, and if the rupture of the gut is above, cut or open it below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the gut is pierced all the way through, it must not be allowed to discharge anything;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	If you do not cover the head under so that it is visible to you, then arrange in such a way that the bowels descend as low as they can be, for when the bowels are fully prolapsed, do not let them return unless you cover the head under so that it is visible to you, and arrange in this manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the bowels fall gently downward, and do not let anything of the bowels.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidated medicines to lay upon the flesh, and spread them under a linen cloth that covers the entire flesh;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then press against the opening of the chest to make it smaller, for they apply ointments soft on the other cloth according to the quantity of the wound, and put them upon the wound to calm the bowels, and do not hold back the large cloth hot until after many days one time;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And the one who is afflicted with a perforated breast bone often pulls out the bone and looks to see what's happening with the bone, whether it's venom or poison or not digestible;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take care that the patient feels pain or numbness, and if it has an abscess or not, and when you have extended medicine in this manner and see the nature that's coming out from the perforated breast bone, then know whether the breasts are inflamed and approach the treatment.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then take it away in the morning, or the third day, and when you heal the wound, change another dressing, and renew the binding.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the shoulders lie bowed out of digest since many years, he will not recover.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle veins are cut after long time, do not despair of recovery, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	But there are some who take too long to recover from their wounds, and those who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if he swallows indigestion after many days, you will know that his breasts are not healed.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	And if the breasts are delayed to discharge and are far from opening, apply dried medicines in powder form and moist ones in virtue, like ointment because there is a great part of vinegar, and this is the back medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Apply ointment diffidently, and make it with rose oil and equal in quantity to the vinegar of old wine.
puis le confit et en use;	then the syrup and use.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and the same do as honey cooked swollen, when ointments diffidently are not present, or you take mirror and aloes and incense, and grind it, and make powder on the honey while it's on fire.
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	And then when the heat is applied to the skin, and it is stretched out on the breast, and at no time does one administer an aromatic oil or a celestial root, which is like flour for times and centuries;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and using simple remedies or compound ones;
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and crushes them, and makes powder, and applies it with the honey I mentioned, and uses;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the patient is still ill, and is not cured by this remedy, then you know that corruption has gone deep, and made impression on the bone, or in hard members, or in the sinews;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if a cure for an abscess, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the elephant
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Boils are a sort of abscess that form under the fingernail, or on the foot, or by chance in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And when it is elderly, and no care is taken for it, if an abscess forms on the leg, and they run and flee so much as to reach the root of the boil, and by chance they will have reached all of it;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion comes just to the bone, so that it brings forth foul odor and pain, and the joints swell up and become red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section on cutting, and if no cure is effective, then it is necessary to copy from it. Take away all the remaining swelling from the wound, and after that, cauterize the wound.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is very great help when the bone is sound and the ulcer is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the ulcer presses on the cartilage and begins to form a scab, so that it bleeds, if you want to help, then place a bandage below the ulcer, pointing the cartilage, and tie the cloth tight, and strike those thin threads with a sharp knife in a subtle and gentle manner, and apply the remaining part of the dressing hot medicines and corrosives to remove all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	the doctor of limbs instructs them so they are healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	and if the corruption is in the bone, if you cut and treat it, because as long as the bone is corrupted, it will not heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the abscess corroding, then cut into it at its source as is said, and the doctor will treat it until it heals.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is a boil or an abscess and you pour it out, and the patient feels great pain, then it is best to cure it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the inflammation with a sharp knife at an angle, and watch that the cut does not come to the bone under, because the patient will feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, put something on top that will soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from a sore throat of the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two bones that lie in the palms of some men are always curved, and sometimes they have bones, and never an angle, and sometimes birth occurs at the root of the joint, or no birth occurs in any of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are born in no direction but to the left do not move, and those who are born with the joint of the two limbs may move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the weight of him who is fat is lighter in some way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	weighed at the root of a large splint.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those who are born with a twist in the root of the joint are crippled to be cured:
si te tien dou coper.	if tied with leather.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In one born without in the buttocks, it is fitting to first copy around the curved scar just above the bone, then cut the bone at an appropriate length for that person, and then cure until he is sound.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sound that comes forth with the joining of two things is due to their birth, or by the suddenness of an injury, or by the heat of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is to be sewn up so that the wound can heal, then they must repair according to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two towels or wet cloths soaked in olive oil so they do not stick.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you put between two thin pieces of pumice stone so that the surface is smooth, as it requires.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the sound comes forth on any of its parts with the palm, if you copy that wound as it suits.
des vils	the old
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The wounds are large and swollen, full of melancholic humors that come into more limbs of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And it is most likely to happen in legs of those who go to work and walk, as well as other ones.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer no purging of gallstones at any time, and then cleanse the blood of the basilic.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The iron treatment has two kinds.
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is to cut and treat the black vein with iron.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other kind is that you tie off the vein and treat it with iron.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The limb is measured according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	the first one was the leg of hot water very strong, until it became thin; then pull the leg of the patient from above to below at the joint just above the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then strike the vein in the arm, either in the left or right arm, with a wide gash; then lift and pull out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, until as much of it comes out as the patient's virtue can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie him, and he commands that he take meat for a week, eating black broth.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommence the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are empty, and it is to the patient's harm.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The limbs of the body are according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	cut the leg of the sick person if he has much hair, then put it in hot water and make the leg swollen with cold water until it becomes red.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have hot water, then heat it over the fire and then cut the vein at the long end of the head of the groin, or in the lower part near the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then cover the skin with linen and burn the vein at each point until it stops bleeding when you feel it.
