et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and then you will see the vein red and black, and when it enters the skin, it looks like a white thread.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	Then pour out the wound below, until it is lifted up by the skin, and then pull it towards the neck slightly, then cut at once in another place as in the third part;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then raise the wound to the same place, just as you did, and pull towards another spot, just like you first did;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then cut another size, or more if needed, then raise it, and cut at the second foot, then pull and raise just to the same place as the other size;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract a size by size until it is completely removed, then cut;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot pull it and lift it, then put an arrow into the strong thread twice, and pull it, and scrape below the wound, and turn your hand one way and the other, until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And keep it from being wounded, for if she is wounded, then he cannot be treated or lifted, and it comes to harm the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have finished treating her, put on the linen cloth over the wound moistened in wine and olive oil;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him stay until he is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the gallbladder is swollen and twisted and ruptured altogether, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you should break it violently, but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	the form of the iron bar that is used to treat the gallbladder if it is curved, and do not cut it, lest you wound the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And it is a large crow, for if it were subtle, the vein would be cut, but it is big just as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the free woman
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is stuck in legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and on earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and sometimes it is found in other parts than the legs, and this happens because of rotting that comes from beneath the skin, just as it comes inside the body serpent-like and downwards, stuck between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes a great inflammation in the leg, then change the poultice, and as it begins to force itself out, so does like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the head is cut open, it is convenient that you wrap around one piece of cloth from half an inch to two inches, and the vein, and leave the cloth on the leg, and whenever it is not in front, wrap again around the cloth, and apply the new dressing.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, so cut off a part, and pull the rest away, and do not cover it in its root, until it is completely removed;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	But if you cut it, so it goes into the flesh, and brings forth abscess and putrefaction, and a bad disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	Therefore it is necessary to treat this thing little by little, until the head; and leave nothing behind in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And there is no vein at all when it is treated with two or three fingers, or sometimes one inch of blood comes from it, and when you cut it, so the wound bleeds or is punctured, and the pulse stops as far down as the finger that has come out, so that everything stops;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And let the matter that is inside be emptied out, and bring to the patient medicines to clean the wound every day, then the physician should treat him as they do for abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And no one should ever cut the vein when it's swollen, and especially when it opens up in the joint of the foot or the hand, and blood comes out in great abundance, and bones are broken.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	So treat him as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between the leather and the cartilage
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This illness is called "maladie de buef" in our land because it often occurs in cattle, and it's a small worm that nests between the hide and flesh, and moves throughout the body upwards and downwards, causing pain in every part of the body until the hide splits or it bursts forth.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is infected with putrefaction of some humors, just as certain snakes and worms and insects come and set up shop in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and doubts its illness, because when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes upon the eyes, by chance it enters, and destroys the eyes;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it needing to be cured and treated, one cannot wait, but rather must hurry.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so it is necessary to bind the patient firmly above and below with a strong cord tightly tied, then strike up at it and treat the wound, and if the vein is drawn down deeply into the flesh, and you cannot find it, then one must cauterize it with fire on top, until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest evils he causes, if it is to run with oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming towards the eye or close to the oil, then hold tight and press down on the forehead, and then pull out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is fitting to treat the patient with a mundification of body by soluble medicines for purging the bad humors, and use unwholesome food.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes into some members, and moves from one member to another;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have seen this myself.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of her arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	And after that, my vein swells up just like a worm on the shoulder, quicker than any thing, so swollen as if it were alive when it cuts through it at another place;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departs from that place and settles in the shoulder, and then a little after it cuts through all the body, until it comes to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	and then she told me that she was dying from within the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I am very much amazed at how it moves from member to member, because I have never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	I have often wanted to make sure that the pain from another joint also occurs, but I did not see it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that was why the woman had a dry body, and loose skin, and because of that appeared the swollen veins;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And do not appear so according to this reason to those who are diseased, and who have moist bodies and veins returned.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see treating this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears so as we have said, immediately lift up and down and then quickly strike on them so that the wind-constrained limb returns to its place.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the limb;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it in your eyes, as the cure of those who tie up the wind-constrained limb with rotten pills and serpent pills and similar ones.
des saiettes	From the arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are different according to their appearance and according to the limbs or where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The various types of them are that there are those with large points, and small ones, and needles, and soldered ones;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those who have two angles, and those with tongues, and of those where there are pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and when it spews in any member, spewing according to two manners:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the principal member, spewing, such as brain, liver, gall, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it spews then in any limb of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so that you should extract this arrow, because death comes after in many circumstances;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this malady does not appear to you, and the arrow is not stuck fast, then try to remove it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces and hits the bone, and the blood flows upward which is above the brain, is when there is a scotomia, delirium, confusion, redness and swelling in the eye, and inflammation, redness of the tongue, spasms, mixing of the senses, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps without pain in the nose or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it affects the speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and seeps out from the white wound like pus, and jumps about as if it were blood of charcoal;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if that sign appears to you, then take hold of the treatment, and extract the arrow when it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The mark of a stool when it falls or bursts is when it is near the left thigh, and feels just like it has been punctured by something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the stool moves just like the legs, and with great pain in the black blood, and comes cold sweat and pale face, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore one senses doubt that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never gets a chance to swell without bloody discharge from the wound, and the throat becomes swollen, and the patient's color changes, and they gasp loudly and look for the pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the stool falls into the covering of the leg, it is a sign that there are swellings on the small sides;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and spews great foam and great pain and sighs;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And all the limbs of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow vomits in the stomach, by chance, if it brings forth anything indigestible from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow vomits in the belly, and there is no expectation of recovery from the wound, or from removing the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow is discharged into the bladder, and urination comes out in a rush and comes pouring out from behind, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Which means that they know the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and the chest and the neck and the shoulder and the head and the back and the spine and the fists and the elbows and the groin and the knees and the legs, and the member that resembles them are safe according to more or less conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you has happened to me, so that you may do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened in one house with an arrow stuck in the arm or in the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to pull it out, and tore the flesh on the other side of the ear, under the fat, and was healed quickly.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And tore off another arrow that was stuck in the fat under the ear of the skin, and the arrowhead was returned, and could only reach with half an inch of its tip, and it was very light for a Turkish iron arrow.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	I have senses, and no bad accidents come to me.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And take a tourniquet from the neck of a Christian, and it was an Arab tourniquet around the ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I cut through the hair and carefully removed it, and the Christian was made healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And took a tourniquet to the inside of the belly, where he was lying on the ground, and thought he was going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after thirty days passed, his condition did not improve.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut off the tourniquet, tied it, and applied it again, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man who is wounded by an arrow or on his back, and the wound is closed.
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	but the arrow remained inside him, and he did not have pain or discomfort from any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man who has an arrow in his face, and the wound is closed.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and it remained there to cause him great suffering.
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And there is an arrow in the king's man who fell from his horse, and he is leaning to the right side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely still.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was unable to complete the request.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I sought it by all subtle means, and did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and felt a point or pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was a result of the arrow's point I put on the left shoulder joint, which is connected to the digestive tract, because the joint swelled;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and an arrow's swelling appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put on the emplastrum [the plaster or poultice] for three days, and solved the wound directly, and so stayed the patient for a long time, until he felt the arrow the day before next.
et il le me dist.	And he says.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put the medicinal powder on the wound with a corrosive substance in my hands for many days until it was broken down, and I tried it, and felt that the head of the arrow was drying out.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I pushed the head of the arrow into the wound with that medicine, until the joint of the arrow became visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it passed well the ends of three months, and then I felt if the wound had healed where I hammered in the tongs, both to one side and to the other, and would not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	and therefore I did not cease to try and devise ways of instruments, until I took it one day with tongs well made, according to what the form was at the end of this chapter, as it came, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	So I restore it then, and the wound is bound, and the patient is cured entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Unless you tell me the quality of extracting arrows, for you put your care on what I do not say, because the books cannot grasp everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but wise masters have done little more than a few things well, and with what is present and failing, they try new work and nine instruments, at the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows are inserted into the body only when they are stuck in two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	Where they enter through the joint, or where they are inserted,
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And that which breaks apart when it enters, is an arrow entering the bones, and now breaks apart for the first time.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not break apart now, let it stay until the bone is putrid and the joint is inflamed.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, let it stay for some days, and change it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it breaks apart, and if it does not break apart, if there is a perforation in the entire inner surface, until the bone is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if an arrow is embedded in the bone of the head, and it remains at one of the entrances of the brain, and some of the accidents I have mentioned are exposed to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	but if it is not treated, but lets it remain for some days until they are equalized after a while, because if the arrow comes just to this point (the surface), that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone alone, and does not come out immediately, and the patient remains in this state for some days without any further accidents, then try to extract it by pulling.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply embedded in such a way and cannot be extracted, then administer tartarized vinegar inside, as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the animal until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is returned to its place inside the body, and one cannot see it, if the patient has all of the symptoms;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, then if you have no suitable instrument,
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot cut through the tightness of the wound, and the deepness of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve visible, then cut as deeply as the wound.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	And if you can remove the arrow if it has ears in it to see why it holds, then take out the part that is stuck two parts deep into the flesh that you can reach, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can pull it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And gently as much as possible, so that the arrow does not break, pull it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot do it once, if the blood is spilled until the vein enters its opening, then take care, because extracting it is an ordeal.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the patient has a counteraction of blood from this cautery, follow what we have said in this chapter about the treatment.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And protect yourself from the incision in the nerve and vein, and put something in place so that you can move the arrow's shaft without risk, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And put the patient in such a form as he was when the arrow hit him, because this is the greatest aid for him, and if you are unable to do so, then put him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from the other side, or if it is blocked in any way, or if the skin is swollen and inflamed as we can see or feel immediately:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	So cut down then, until the tongs can take hold, and then extract it;
si saut fuer maintenant.	If now he is dying.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand around it completely, until it enters the bone, and then widen the bone, then pull.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if she cannot emerge, so let her remain still, and then continue to extract until it emerges.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the wound from the arrow is deep, pour the poultice all over the wound.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the arrow flies, and you see administering poultice, if you administer the instrument of the head, so that the points of the arrow enter into the hair of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then poultice it over, and if the arrow is tied up, pour the instrument with a point inside, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is touched, if it is deemed necessary to copy all the flesh around where the vein is located, so that you can, then treat the wound as it seems fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow flies or stings, or on the belly or near the bladder or on the side, and it is close to the surface, then cover it up, if you strike.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And keep guard the vein and the nerve, and then draw it out, and then sew the wound, for this is service.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the clamps used to treat arrow wounds are similar to an eagle's beak, and look like this:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	greats, middling sizes, and small ones, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the bow that presses the hair is like the feathers of a bird, to press against the tip of the arrow, as it looks like this:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of pliers for pressing and stitching if there is:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins on the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of veins where one's cure is thirty-one, because there are sixteen heads, which is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	two batans (or bursae) which are after the ears, called the "doux herbes" (meaning "soft herbs").
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing.
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And I show you that which are in the two sides of the two eyes, called "aspirés";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is closed on the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two guidelines which are on the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are under the lips of the mouth, and these are called "aughuerics";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins to which one commonly refers are four in each arm;
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, which is on the left side of the clavicle, and they call it "vein of the head" among the common people;
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	And the bone is called "fast", and it is composed of the cerebral and basilic parts, and they call it the "vein of the heart".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And the basilic is found on the left side of the costal region, and they call it "vein of the stomach", and it is located above the diaphragm, and it is that one where you breathe in, which opens up visibly into the stomach.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the ulnar vein is the vein that is between the little and ring finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is under the wing of the socket of the left shoulder, and the second is on the ankle of the right shoulder;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein which is called "nessel", is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and on the other leg, there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The suffering of the veins that are behind the ears if aided with old cathartics and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the sickness, if I tell you, and is that you raise the patient's head, and rub the vein or the veins with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then the patient's neck is pressed against one wrist, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in each of two lews (units) depending on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	unless then indeed you feel the pulse in your wrist, and where you feel it, that is the sign.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Take the lancet and take it down through the vein just above the bone; then lift your hand up all over the vein to the top, and strike and cut and clean the vein well. You should see two openings, and you must make them come out so that you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then tie it up tight until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have said the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	If the patient has suffered from two arteries located in the two temples, if they are suffering from ancient inflammation and soreness, and eye discomfort, and pain in the corners of the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the sores are as I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And so the patients strain their necks until the two veins appear open.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and they pull out the hair below the nail, and then sign.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the vein above the nail at the root of your finger, and cut the lancet under, and lift the vein above, and strike it, just as you have done in two other veins, and make a cross according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and put your finger on top of the vein for an hour, then put cotton on.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then bind it up, and leave it to be so until she is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken about their cauterizing and extraction, and the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The illness of the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the illness of the head due to ancient face diseases and migraines, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the qualities are that the sick person twists their neck until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "sickle" and has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and pierce upwards from your hand, or from another thing, and let the blood flow according to what you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then deliver to the sick person the neck, and tie the vein until it is clean and there is no more bleeding.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	It is not suitable to translate medical texts from a specific time period to modern medicine without proper review by medical professionals.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	And the healthy ones are also affected, because the bone is close, and by chance the wound splits when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The afflicted from the two veins that are in the two fingers if they hold fast and at the nail, and at the redness, and at the swelling, and at the pus in the eye, and with illnesses of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the qualities of their sickness are such that the sick person twists his neck in a strange way, turning from what it was before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	and the healthy one, and when it is through, then it goes in with a small cut on the long bone, a small deep wound, because there is no cartilage.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	If the flames are subtle, by chance they break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then make a correct cut of the wound, just as you have need to, and then bind it with cloth, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The wound of the vagina caused by menstruation so often brings fever, and cough, and diseases such as inflammation and redness that appear on the face, and also when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and if the quality of the wound is that the patient strains his throat, then strain your left hand on him, and take long, subtle flame, and strike it into the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well in that place, and now the bleeding will start.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too deeply into it, for cut deep according to your need, and then bind a night, for she is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The sickness of the two joints is most helpful in constricting the vein, and at the beginning of ulceration, and with much disease, and inflammation, and corruption, and herpes, and ulcers.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the qualities of the sickness are so that if the sick person strangles his neck with one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	And if the master is standing above the patient's head, and the sick person sees it in one vein, then pricks a vein long and slightly wide, then draws out the wound at the right time, or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then redo it again on the other vein, then cut the ligament, and hold the veins tight moderately, so that the patient does not choke.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let him alone until morning, so the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the cleansing of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cleansing of the veins of the liver above so helps to break down in the mouth, and to corrupt the gums, and splits in the lips, and does not heal well.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And if the wound is clean, then sit the patient in front of you and strap his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the hand, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right hand's thumb and the other on the left hand's thumb, and recognize them by what they are black, because there are small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	so that both of them are cut, and if you do not recognize one of them, or if you are in doubt, then cut the larger one from each side, just as you did for the two veins that are above and below.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the inflammation of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The sick who have veins below the tongue are aided after the headache, and it is at the constriction of the neck, and with diseases of the eye, and with diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of a healer are such that patients who suffer from illnesses between your hands in front of the sun, and they lift the tongue, and look under each nostril one black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then both veins are cut and do not be too deep, for under these are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	the veins of the arm which are commonly cut are cut according to two manners:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or puncturing at the point of the great mitral vein, or olive oil subtle like the tangents, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And they are large and subtle according to the size and narrowing of veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame is like a mirror so it is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins on the forehead when they are flat and contain great blood clots that appear.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is like the shape of an olive pit.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtle in point, and is to heal the small veins subtlety, or where there are subtle bloody spots.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps to alleviate diseases in the throat, neck, and chest, and abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is fitting for the lord that he should bleed and purify himself from the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery and blood comes out, then it is fitting to stitch up, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and do not let him grasp the flame, but cut it as you would with a needle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the abscess does not open manifestly, so you should extract it, and change to another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want to make the wound bleed, or you put a tourniquet on the arm below the vein.
elle apert manifestement;	if it opens manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut the flame with a needle, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	and if you see the vein of the wound, so also that you extract the arm, touch the limb until you know the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the vein of the incision, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with a needle.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and warn you not to cut at the artery when you see the swollen limb, for it is of the artery:
eschui la donques.	avoid then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it bulging like the urine of a child, and if there is no redness or subtlety, know that it is not an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry up then, and put on your knife long, then cut off the knife if it doesn't stain, because this has happened many times;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	if the limb is fixed, and left so, and do not move the patient's limbs;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be cautious, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if there is no inflammation when you prick him, and he falters, and the medicine does not reach him, then cut the artery since it opens up, because the head of the limb will be exposed.
et estainche li sans.	and inflame if you prick him.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a scab from a fistula and make it open, and take one of the halves and tie well to the other half.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if there is no inflammation, that's good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	but if not, if the doctor does it, as we have said, with the powders that bring inflammation.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the inflammation does not cause more pain in those who have a small leg of the wound and the power of the joint on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The patient of the vein has aid in treating the wound on the head above, and the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic vessels, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is fit for the master that he should cut at the nerve which is below, and if he cuts too deep, and it bleeds, and the nerves swell, and sometimes the patient does not recover;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve is often cut many times, and if it does not open in any man for its subtlety, it is fit that you should take out the healthy part of the instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid cutting the nerve at all.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has veins between the two nerves, so that they are cut to the long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The patient of the cephalic vein is aided, who applies treatment to the head wounds, and helps the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to save by applying the fire of olive or myrtle, for it is the safest of all veins, because it has no nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	For this route, it is necessary to choose the lighter one, and do not distress oneself if you must do it again for the first time, and continue.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance, it swells the vein in some people, but one must not distress oneself.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the cut depends on your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know to heal is that healing is only granted for the purpose of keeping health and avoiding diseases.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and whether healing is done in one of the three veins:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	It is to know, the head, the skull, the neck.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And one must observe in the beginning of the prayer at dawn, and in autumn and winter after fasting, when the signs of replenishment appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	And one must observe the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The remedy that is in use for all diseases has no fixed time determined, but rather when it is needed, whether in the morning or at night, in every hour and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not advisable to treat children under 13 years old, nor women who are pregnant only from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Do not attempt to heal those who are over 60 years old.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when some people wish to heal themselves, in whatever manner they choose, it is fitting that if someone confuses the bowels with a light castor oil, and has much pain retained, so that the veins are drawing out the intestines' superfluities, causing noxious evils to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	ne can heal oneself who is excessively salted in meats, nor one who is gouty, so much so that the disease becomes severe, or dropsical;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one is sick after a severe attack of colic, vomiting, and decline of the belly, and multiple times lying on a woman's couch, traveling, watching, and fasting, because all their strength, either by the arm or by the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly adjust the humors, without being too much so, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you have one;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	After the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let them take a bath, since no harm comes from it, in order to further their healing, and they will be healthy again after washing under the pig's entrails on the third day, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day of work, and pain, and luxury, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be calm and joyful, and make the healthy ones higher than those who are sick, and rub the arms twice or three times, then pull out the bandage at moderate pace, because when it is too tight or too loose, they cannot stop running without;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the healthy one with their hands, until the veins swell and are felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the healthy one with a little flame of oil vinegar, then place a drop of that vinegar from their left hand under the vein of the patient in a small amount or when it will heal, lest the vein is wounded and fails to heal.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	There are veins that flow like cords to the vein, and some of those have the same quality as empty strings, when one puts the flame on it, so it withdraws again from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is like these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if one opens the vein, then it is for those with the wound too narrow, so it is advised to have experienced surgeons in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens for the first time, that's good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if it doesn't happen again, then repeat the process a little under or above where the wound is located, if the blood does not swell.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the blood is swollen and the patient loses hope, let him stay for one day or two, and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	By chance I will bring abscesses with me;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter the bath, then resume the treatment if it pleases.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the wound is small, or if you cut beneath it subtly, and you doubt that there will be much blood as you see, then fear for this same wound itself will always be true.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and the work is done quickly, so that the patient does not become swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	because this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the patient swollen, do not resume the treatment, and apply a little bit of lard oil, because it lightens the body from the wound, and is more gentle in this place than the wound itself.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus attend to the tie of oil in each wound that you heal the veins, for to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	And thus the same is done as an arrow and a bow are made for it, when it is placed on the limb;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if you make it very thin and the splinter when it is too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there is one great abscess, which has happened many times, and similarly when it cannot be treated only at the time of opening the vein is small, then hasten, and put on a moist sponge soaked in water and a little salt, and restrain for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is advisable that you do this after the outcome of the vein's wound, and if it remains on the limb for some days without any color or greenery, then it will not be good.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see, put on no ointment of aloes or of myrrh renewed in juice of calmness, monster, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often happens an abscess and appearance on the belly of the basilisk:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Put therefore your hand on it, and if you find the place swollen under the pressure of the hand, then that is a bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Avoid then lest you put on anything of that which we have said, for by chance cutting without the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but to set a plaster dry to harden the place, then the cure of another cure, until it is made whole.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And apply to each person according to the quantity of their virtue, and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if not black, then let him leave it out to be discolored until it is red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see a large wound, let it remain so until it becomes subtle.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too heavy, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is thin and weak, and has need of blood extraction, to make the wound even larger and widen the flaps.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to heal him quickly and frequently, and he should be healed by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of healing is safe from decay of the blood and hematoma of the nerve, and is better than healing with a long or short knife.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	and to one whose blood must be given during healing, it is necessary to give him cold water moistened with juice of green apples.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If it is heated, if you draw out the blood three times or four; and if it is of cold complexion, if you apply a piece of moist bread in syruped wine, or in syrup with aromatic spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if the palm holds the wound, after a great amount of blood has been lost, it is fitting that he drink broth made from cheese and sweet syrup, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to open the vein on one arm and cure himself again, it is fitting that when he is weakened by great blood loss, he heal little by little, according to the continued quantity of his virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to open the vein on one arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong pulse, will recover in 7 hours after the first bleeding, or within an hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to cure himself on the other side, if he should have to cure himself on the second day or on the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood inside the body when it is heated, and brings on fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if one wishes to draw a great quantity of blood and enlarge the wound so that it may fall into the pelvis.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you should reward all the conditions of health, and put your hand under some pulleys when the patient heals, lest death come in its place, for this happens many times when the servants are negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not advisable when you see a person loosening their arm, and causing blood to flow the second time, and the wound is closed, that you press firmly on top of it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	unless if he is curved, extending the arm suddenly, for this would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let him wait until he has recovered a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or point the flame at the tip until the frozen part of the vein bleeds again, and put on some poultice made with water, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If the vein has been cut away, so let it remain and do not bind it tightly, until the abscess is closed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If a second wound needs to be treated with the same treatment as before, in the same vein or in another vein.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is closed in place of the vein at the head, because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of dressing the wound is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the flesh is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	First let the member remain still, so that the vein appears well; then set it straight now through, neither too wide nor too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the large punctures be closed, and set the hand well near to the joint of the hand; so that without coming out, put the hand in hot water, and leave the wound open in the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in this state, do not put the hand back into hot water, for you will put more pain into it than relief.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the healing of this vein is more safe than all other veins, for it has neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the small vein of the right hand is worth all other remedies for liver diseases, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand, and pour it into hot water, until the vein is freed, if you see.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the vein is crooked, and if you copy it all over in its entirety, nothing will be harmed.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not apply too much pressure, for the nerves are dried out in all of them when they are cut, and then put the hand into hot water again, if it is not frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have applied to the wound as much as necessary, put oil and sinew on the vein to sew up hastily, and do so for every cut.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sickness of the vein in the left hand is worth the disease of the mouse, and do it just as I told you over to the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickness of the liver is worth all kinds of diseases of the body, just as illnesses from the marrow, and retention of flowers, and illness of the kidneys, and joints, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of the vein if it is that when patients pour some salt into hot water and rub above the vein until it dies, and bind above the joint of the foot;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and if the vein is on the ankle, and through above the foot it goes very far.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	The body heals quickly on average or at the knee, where it can remain.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you heal it on top of the bone, so that you keep the nerve below from being damaged and cut through just as in cutting.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let it be still for a time.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If he cannot come out from it, so put his foot in the water, and let well drain the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it is not the first time that it heals, then it recurs again on top a little because it is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same thing for the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The veins of the groin are in the heel of force, and its cutting is worth pain of the hamstring when it's for blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of its healing if it is so that the patient goes in or out, and presses with a force of four on the ankle, twisting, because otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if she opens, then let him cut her in all the ways you can, and crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and holds that one should copy it, because the liver is spoiled, and she is very sensitive to the touch of the hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then let the healthy man have no rain of blood from what opens or on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the pox.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make a strong incision in the wound so you see what's inside, and then cut the ligature, and put on cotton and bind.
ele est maintenant sanee.	She is now cured.
des sainies de ventouse	of venous issues
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Ventriloques are made of horns, or of nails, or of glass.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And if evacuation of blood is performed according to two methods:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by pricking and attracting blood, or by pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this evacuation of blood which is done by pricking is according to two methods:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or when it is applied with fire, or not with fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and evacuation that is done by pricking and extracting blood is done in twelve locations of the body, because one is whole on the head.
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are tied to the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two more on each side of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the evacuation beneath the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	And let him apply the force of two shoulder blades;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and let him apply pressure above the groin;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and let him apply pressure on both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and let him apply pressure on both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and let him apply pressure on both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and let him not apply the force of the venous opening, except for small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and so much that one does not tire or weaken because of it, as is done with veinlet bleeding;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that they are administered, except when there is no fire or heat, in any disease coming from excess, until the entire body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessity requires that something is inserted, or by custom, then bring it in each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are those who, when they need to have something inserted, so weigh their head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who have redness and inflammation in their face, head, neck, and eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are those who have a red spot of blood in their mouth, and they have swollen the tongue, and have bleeding.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who dream, and see through the blood, and boils, and wounds, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and myself when it is time for the month, we command to be ventoused after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The sick from the moisture will be aided by the pain of the head ... so that it comes to their eyes, and should not happen only after the evacuation of all their body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this vomiting is in the place of the head pain, and should not happen to one with a cold complexion or who has catarrh, because it does them much harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore should not happen to one who uses vinegar or who has cold head ailments.
