Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from this often become blind, and therefore it is fitting to apply the venous suction a little lower by the examination of blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Vomiting in the throat is in place of head pain and a basilic, and for this it is valued to tighten the belly, and cut the channel of the womb, and to toast, and to swell.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is advisable to pound a little more, because if she holds too tightly, so she can cause an obstruction or stomach and bowel.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The vomiting has two costal swellings on the chest if it causes pains in the head, eyes and emigraine, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and is like a sickness of the basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is advisable that you command the lord to press his hand in putting it, so he does not strike an artery, and does not come into contact with bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	Vomiting under the chin if it causes illness of the mouth, and decay of gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and is like the sicknesses of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cutting on the shoulder blades causes disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The injury from a sword slash is worth as much as three veins of the arm because it draws blood from those large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the lord that he should not cut too deep into the flesh, because the veins are bare and located beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The vein on the flank is worth for hemorrhoids at the root, and for diseases beneath; it is advisable that the vein be large and be filled with blood, so as to properly treat them.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And if it were subtle, it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The veins of the legs heal completely, because they draw blood from the entire body, and are worth for ancient pains of rain, and of malaria, and of bladder troubles, and reduce swellings.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are found on both shoulders, and both knees, and all of them weaken the body after long use, and bring about fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply a poultice is that you should put it on first empty, and suck out in time, and put it hastily, and move evenly, and do not cease to do this, until you see the redness of the vein inflamed, and feel the red color in the wound;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then put the poultices back, and take care in the arrangement of the body, because there are many who have died from bad meat, and unclear pores;
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	it is often necessary to wound only once, and it is also suitable to make large wounds, and a little deep.
et suce legierement.	and cut gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if it is not large, he should be cauterized twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to subtlety the passage of the large vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	and if it is very thick, he should be cauterized a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to cut the vein little by little, if our force only lasts once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much of the vein, we should repeatedly resume.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if it is not thick, cut into the bone, and finish by cutting so that they are perceived suddenly; and cauterize to one who has a great skin and thick fur, and those with perforated pores, that you apply oil apertif and dissolutive on their surfaces of fingers
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	This is the oil used, anointing it with violets, or almond oil, or the oil of cucumber seeds;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and anointing it with turnip oil, or celery, or chamomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is great and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or balsam, or anise oil.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if those with skin that is sensitive and large pores, should not be put on oil, but should be washed after the application of rose water, or cold water, or grapevine juice, or cucumber juice, or other similar waters.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with much moisture, lift him up from the cold, or from the water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have great swellings lift themselves with old wine, or fresh water, or an onion decoction, or chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and should not be treated with a ventouse before the bath, or in the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and should not sleep after the treatment, and it is necessary to perform the ventouse again, whenever it is needed, or when it is applied.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And warn those who recover from this illness are choleric, and if they have not been too angry and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is necessary to take cold things, such as grapes, greens like pomegranate and lettuce at ease, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat porridge, and broth of chestnut, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with a cold complexion should take honey syrup, and fragrant wine of moderate age, which is between vintage and new, and eat little, and eat porridge, small fowl such as pigeons, and pease.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the next day when he will vomit, it is necessary for him to drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is fitting to give some patients three times or more stitches before the operation, or after, for the comfort of their limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And so be careful with wine, but it is not fitting for those who are already drunk to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The ventouses that are applied to cause bleeding are those that are placed on the liver, and on the groin, and on the feet, and on the abdomen, and the belly, and the rump, because that member does not bear pain from being poked, and one does not dare to pierce it unless to draw blood from a member into another, as we apply pressure to the breasts when they are inflamed.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to loosen the viscosity that is in the member, as we place ventouses on the abdomen and on the groin to ease the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And the pain ends, when it is an ulcer or a stone, so the pain ends by its attractive power by chance, or the ulcer of its own place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus he (the patient) is cut when you put him on the liver and on the muscle when there is retention of venosity, and these veins are cleaned out to suck blood alone.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are cleaned with fire, and sometimes plain water is used, just as in other maladies of the pleura, and thus one fills the vein with hot water or with it, there being suitable herbs boiled for that purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction to apply with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two fingers of length and half a palm from the tip, with a small puncture on one side around the middle of the finger, as if to insert an arrow, and so that it does not bleed the patient when you put the member on.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and it is in the middle of a point stuck by thorn or iron, to tie a bandage around it, and with them and great and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the suckers on children are different from those on adults, and smaller than larger ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must put this sucker on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	bind with a wax bandage or string and put it into the sucker through the point that is in the sucker, so that the clearness is at the end of the sucker, which will not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and tie so that it is above the puncture where we have said, if you want to remove, if the vapor comes out, and take off the sucker;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take hold of the linen just as before, and repeat it often, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the application of the vacuum, which is used for treating disease of pleurisy, has no advantage, has no point or puncture, and is only applied when it is full of fluid, and is placed on one limb only;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Seals and other instruments are not applied only in places where one cannot put the vacuum due to small size, such as lips and gums, and similar ones.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in their noses of wood, like two or nails, and other similar ones;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the qualities of the user when it is found that there are seals in clean and soft water, so take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And they put them on wet straw, until they are familiar with them, and have no wind in their stomachs.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be made clean with a vein and a cup, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on poultices.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are flat and dry, and have closed, if it is possible to put a cup on them, then put them on, because this is much after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not so, lift the limb away from the joint, and then into water, very well, and then inspect.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limbs are healed too late after the poultices on the skin, wrap them in a linen cloth soaked in cold water, and put it on, until the poultice dries.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the swelling is multiplied, then apply vitriol crushed or vinegar, or similar things, until it subsides.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or put salt on the swollen place, and leave it until the fever has dried up, if it will now subside.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other remedies.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the remedies do not take effect, then rub the swollen place with fresh sauce or prick it with a needle until the swelling disappears, and afterwards when they feel the pain, it will subside.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are crying, then powder on a little alum and crushed silk or ashes, if it will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	The book of fractures begins
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know well, dear son, that this fire cautery is unknown to the ancient books, nor do they read it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this, the art has been lost in our land, for I have never found any good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing but by the knowledge of ancient books, where I have studied and treated this art through experience, and from my life's habit.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and condensed it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of instruments that must be used, as I did in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in this prologue of this book the explanations and the chapters where the wise men put their understanding, and take care to explain it further, so that those who have learned from experience know and learn this noble art, and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when any break or dislocation or twisting or splintering comes to occur in anyone, if it is convenient to hasten to heal the sick person from one side and the other, since no further treatment can do them harm, as with weakness of body, or sickness, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	If they do not press (or apply pressure) too much, or are too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	And eat cold meat, that is to say frozen joints, and char of bird and of buck, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not stuff oneself too much with viands which fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about an abscess or a spreading of matter in the member.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient returns to his previous way of life after having used the cautery.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to restore itself, it is fitting that you nourish the patient with foods that cause great swelling, if they have viscosity, such as bread cooked in water, and cheese, and eggs, and butter, and pancakes, and fish fresh from the river, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	But swelling causes more representation of wounds and the break occurs faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that old bones and decayed ones cannot be well mended or soldered according to their nature due to the dryness of the members, nor can those that are too tender, like the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	But there is no cure, so set the broken bone in place with great care, and let us hold it firmly together with a strong thread that will secure it, as soon as it is joined.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and not at all when his work is done, and for this reason they must be nourished with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or thigh, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that occur at the neck, and others from cutting, just like the length of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there are fractures with wounds, and fractures with a small split or crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own instrument and tool, and one that is kept clean in the restoration, as the memory of what was done comes to mind.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the bone breakage is by twisting of the limb, and opening well because of the pressure, when pressed with the finger.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or bumping of the bone at the joint, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But he can have tortuosity, or a cut, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not good to move the fingers at all, but apply the medicines that come after this, and then pull it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And this is known that when the break is in the joint, and the two parts are separated, it must now be put together equally, so that the abscess does not come.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if it comes to swelling at the joint, he must let one day pass, until the swelling is calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then he puts it in the joint with a measure that you can lightly apply and feel, and this is known to be more lightweight than restoration when there are pieces.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then binds it, as he knows afterward.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there is broken bone in the body, where it has two parts, then whether it's with flesh or meat, or with one small member, or with two cords, or with one cord and with the hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And put the member according to its natural form, so that when the parts of the broken limb are severed, you gather all the fragments in their place until you can fix them as best you can, and take care that by your work no further injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And then properly align the two bones of the bone according to the better forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And if it seems to you that it is not quite right, check well with him.
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if you dress it properly and do not strain it too much, nor press it so hard as those who make it come by their operation cause inflammation and heat in the member, just as we have experienced many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is at an end, keep well the patient so that he does not move, neither watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And well-guarded should be your limbs so they do not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	But when it feels no pain, you should not take it for granted, and instead put the limbs into rest so they feel no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And guard well that it is placed correctly, so twistedness does not come to it when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The broken limb is of various size, shape, and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For it has small limbs, just like arms and fingers and similar ones.
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	So you should wrap the linen bandage with wool and subtle cloth.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	And for those that are large, like thighs and legs.
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	It is fitting to wrap with a strong bandage, because the long bands constrict the entire large limb, and bind it from all sides equally, so that there is no weakness.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then tie light tourniquets, three turns or four according to the limb, and bind your hand tightly to the entire bandage, then go up to the break and bind it less, so that the break moves a little away from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and moisten the bandage little by little, until you are pinching a great part of the healthy limb, then take another bandage and turn back to the upper part of the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the lower part of the break and bind it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first book above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Instruct the patient to place stapes of linen or a strip between the ligatures, until they are all even; then tie everything together above the bend, and then put your needles well made on it, if there is an abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	If there is an abscess or inflammation, apply the soothing paste to it, which will draw out the swelling and leave it after some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then pull out your needles, and let them be of a good thickness, like the width of a well-made saw blade or a piece from a log used for making cleats, or palm tree shavings, according to this shape.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is proper that the needle placed on the break be a little thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and so let it be as long as it needs to be on the limb of a small or great size;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then tie the surrounding vessels as you did on the first incision, then tie over with an adhesive bandage, as you did on the previous wound.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is wrapped, the worse.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it should be that the bandage is not too tight, nor too loose or too thin, but made of fine linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the bandage is too thick, like I have had trouble with making ointments from the leaves that make their incisions so prone to forming knots in the linen cord, and this is a great error, for it is not possible for an incision to be even if it is too subtle, and it should not lie between each vein less than two fingers' breadth.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is weak from the pains of the arrows after the straining in their safe place, then put stoppers made of linen or wool on them, so they will not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bones are broken, I will tell you the cure as follows.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not good to strain the arrows every member at once, the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	When the limbs are large, it is not advisable to place a splint before five or seven days, or as soon as your safety allows.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and thus there is the method of the ancient embalmers to restore breaks, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and take flour that remains on the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and put this confection, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, for this is the common method of the embalmers restoring breaks in many situations, especially in women and small children, since it's neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of embalming to restore breaks and dislocations and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take away hair and beard and nail and aseptic area and gum Arabic and mulled wine for X days;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Eye drops and aloes, for five days;
alechil VIIII З.;	Alechil seven times a day.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make powder, and mix with honey and egg whites;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the complexion of the humors is hot, then apply this plaster, because it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and saves many lives.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of plaster that is valued for its twisting.
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mulled wine and vinegar, for ten days;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Mirror and oil, seven times seven.
acaice VI З.;	Acacia six.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Boline Armenian ten, and it breaks well, and conifies with water or honey, and anointing.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of applying plaster to joints and you take away from the bone what is necessary, and appeases the following pain, and uses the bone, and breaks the fracture.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Apply linen novel, and the moss in salt and oil cooked, and put on anew.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore the health, but they are good for soothing an abscess.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of plaster which restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take leaves of dried fig, and leaves of earthy pasture, and break together, and make plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to splint for restoring the break of the bone and for easing the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of wormwood, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour from vetches, of each one a portion;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and crush, and mix with wine, so that the limbs are warmed up; or mix with moist coriander water, or plain water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to apply plaster more strongly than the first, when an abscess is formed on the restored limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of wormwood, and seeds of flax, balsam, melilot, and sansuc, and violet flowers and chamomile flowers, each one a portion;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and crush, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, there is no place to put a broken limb for repair so that the salve made of wax and oil is applied, and nothing else, and he says it should be between too soft and too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that you must put a broken limb on, to restore, things dry with a little hot, just like myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way to treat an open sore that brings on pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take out the nails and thorns of a corpse, or the needles of an animal, and shave them evenly, and cut, and make them into plaster, and bind the limb.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then take out the bone a little after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has they lost their sense of the joint.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if you do not cut out the bone by hands often.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the limb, or it pricks, with rest or swells, quickly take action, cut it out, and now remove the plaster.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a lighter bandage, and a moist sponge, and plunge it in water, and lift up the limb, until the prickling stops, and the pain is eased.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, then put on a clean cloth, either wet in water or in oil rosary, and bind above with a nail, until you are sure of the abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and rest the inflammation of the limb, and let the bone be set, then resume the subtle application, and a little ointment, and do not strain it too hard as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and subtly until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess is red and swollen and painful and inflamed, I have a bone that has been broken into all of them, and you must apply plaster and tie it up again, as you did first when it was even.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if the limb does not come back to its place as we have said, do not let it be released after three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and never let it stay for twenty days, according to what we see, until the fracture has set and approaches the joint again.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	And then he restrains it even more than before, and fattens his flesh, as I have said previously.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see that the liver is drying out more than necessary, know that it cannot be saved.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	therefore the disease rises from hot water, every time you open a wound, and this happens to everyone on the fourth day, and especially in cases of soreness.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	therefore, by this work, cut off the diseased member and make haste to bind what the foolish surgeons do, lest the limb be contorted.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	this is evil, and if there is a great pain, and I see nothing but to lacerate and overstretch it directly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of different kinds of breakage
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of breaks are there, and various forms, and the causes are destined.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for when there are breaks that are made with the force of a sword and the collarbone is broken through all the bone down to where it is under the bone, just as it happens from hitting or being struck.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason it is called that kind of break "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	where the sword strikes the bone from above and pierces it, and is called that kind of break "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and there are two kinds of wounds for these two breaks big or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has been pierced by a blow that has embedded itself, or is a fracture, or of the collarbone on stone, or of the shoulder on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a persistent fracture, which approaches the tendon that is under the bone, or above the bone, and is this wound big or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is sewn back into the bone as subtly as we sew, and there is a small split, and for this reason it is called that break "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound is made or by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by some similar thing, and the bone fragment enters into the flesh and it is like the fingers of the cauterian when they heat above the cauldron;
si entre li piere dedens.	if the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those with moist bones, like children's heads;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and occurs in all such fractures where small pieces are discharged like splinters;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about this on his behalf.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by removing them from under them, and the inquiry has tested them, and by the corrupting fire that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like resemblance is known because when the bone has been discovered and the surface is rubbed upon, if it opens the fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be careful for any accidents in the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting blood, loss of understanding, extension, palsiness, fever, and the eyes are forced out and become red, and other similar symptoms more than usual, then it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any extraordinary accidents, and you hope for recovery, as soon as you begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when you come first to me, and it's in winter, it is fitting to withdraw the bone before the eighteenth day after the moon.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in this state, so hastening to withdraw the bone before the seventh day, and thus making the flesh underneath the bone corrupt, and bringing on the accidents that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the bone fracture comes just next to the cloth that covers the brain, you must break the broken part in such a way:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And instruct the patient to press his head with pain, and uncover on the bone in all ways you can, and on the shape of the wound as well as you can, because if blood comes from the uncovering of the bone or abscess, help him with that which is needed, and fill the vein with moist cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	And let the wound rest until the abscess is calmed, and make sure of the stopping of blood.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then begin to extract from the bone, and it is done in two ways of work.
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	the one way is that you copy the narrow incision before, and it's the shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then after a second more extensive cutting than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is that you have to have various tools in number, some are sharp and others long, and they should be pointed, and made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and when you work lightly, so that you do not strike the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and thick, it is advisable that you pierce through it, so that you can administer tools with care, not by cutting too deeply, lest the tool goes beyond the soft bone of the chest, and the edge of the tool should be left above the point with a margin or circle, lest the point go beyond the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and it is advisable to have more, so that each comes in its own time with the splinter of the bone, so that you always have care for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three kinds of tetanus:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The ones that cut through the bone are that you place tetanus on the bone, and turn to your left and right until you know when the bone has been pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then put tetanus in another place a little after, and so do all around, then cut at the spaces of the bone between the punctures, doing it more subtly than you can, lightly, just like we said, until you draw out the bone with your hand, or on any of the things that you have, such as with tongs, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and be careful not to touch the brain or the pit.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and cut out the bone, if it seems that some part of the bone remains hidden from view, but must be removed with another instrument resembling an incisor, but it should be done more thinly and subtly than other incisors.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if it doesn’t fix anything with small bones or scales, but rather lightened the weight of the limbs.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then treat the wound of tenons and ligaments which we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And other kinds of work are as he [Gaul] says, which is more difficult.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and his words were very strong, and that's what he said.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover a part of the bone, at that place or where the fracture opens up, so that when you have uncovered that part, you put under the lower edge of this cut-out lens-like structure, because it is in this shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut close to one side, and the damaged parts are on both sides, so that cutting is done towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then use a small hammer on top, so that you can lightly beat the bone all around, and take good care to protect yourself from the cloth below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	When it is scraped against the bone, because the bone is lightly scratched, for the pain is felt well, and there is fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the break of the bone is not pierced until just after the cloth, and the bone is hit only from above, with small pieces, it will cover again that roughness, and remove the scales at the subtle raspener which you must have different quantities for, in order to give to each one the most comfortable treatment, according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have many coarser rasps and after more subtle ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	For each other type of capillary wound and subtle fracture, you should take measures according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is a thing that has no response from one who puts their study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the abscess is uncovered, it is necessary that you apply a linen bandage dipped in oil rose, according to the quantity of the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another bandage doubled in two or three, and moisten it with wine and oil rose, and put it on the first bandage.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And make it as easy for you as possible that you do not burden yourself further, lest you grieve the wound more, then attend to this other link from above, and do not strain him too much unless he only causes the pain of the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	And let him lie on this day or the next, until the swelling of the abscess is eased, then take him out, and administer medicines such as willow bark, flour from mulberries, powdered incense, and saffron, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And make powder of these things, and put it on the wound, and administer the remedies with onions and without chewing.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	And be sure that the wound is made clean, lest you leave on it ointment, or do not leave it alone to dress with a bow (or cloth), for when the bow is applied over the skin of the brain, it causes corruption and bad results, and brings great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	For when you place a sharp thing upon its surface, it is cut by above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Preventively then, if no accidents occur to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful in its presence of doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if it does not come back fiery only because of the medicine you have placed upon it, which has power in it, then it is fitting that you press a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and beeswax, and apply it to its surface.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then the remedy of cures which he is suitable for, until he becomes healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Which says that the two lower parts of the neck are often broken in two, or one alone, because they are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and that below is cartilaginous, and it does not break, unless it makes the bone bow or twist, and then becomes sound.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	If one of the two parts is broken, so that you put your little dough or plug into the wound, and place it inside the broken part at your index finger, and in a pouched area by default, until it regains its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this lightly, and warn the patient so that they do not feel pain from your treatment.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the fracture is in the upper part of the arm and it cannot be straightened, so that you put equal to the head of a stick one foot thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is of two parts, you do this again, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if possible;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if this is not the case, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses are calmed down, then put on a cloth made of linen around your head with a plug, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	If you put another bandage on top of this, if there is a break.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And the tents should be so large that they fill in the empty wounds.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said any restorer that you should moisten the linen in butter and move each one every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	I do not think it is well, but it is necessary that they be moist in the making of flour and yeast.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then let the tent be left, until the bone is hardened and the cartilage is set.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And no time should be wasted applying owl's feathers instead of tents, and if the dressing is wrapped around well, and kept in place, and blows are blown into the wound.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or use a bellows to blow.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the nose while you are working, apply a clot or cotton soaked in oil rose, or in one half of vinegar.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscess is not caused by this, so he applies plaster made of mummy's linen, and powder of incense, mixed with honey, then puts on light bandages, and does not bind tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the broken bone is small and it breaks into tiny pieces, if you can get to the instruments suitable for this, then cut the split, and the treatment of things that are difficult to reach, with soldering, as with plaster and ointments suitable for this;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the bone, he treats with poultices, and puts caustic onions in it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the removal of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is removed below, and there is no wound to be found, and the fracture is absent except for swelling alone, without bruising in the marrow, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	it is necessary, if the break is in the right hand, that you put your thumb into the mouth of the patient;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left mandible, so pour your thumb into the fracture of the right hand, and push it gently into the fracture, and press with the other hand, and make even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is on both sides (II), it is necessary to administer an extension of II parts, so that it may be even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	and if the movement of the teeth has happened, or a rupture, so take out the thread of gold, silver, or silk from one of them, and put it on the fractured mandible with cerote, and put a double cloth on.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and put on a long and thick leather belt or an estee well made, or a piece of leather according to the mandible, and tie it on the jawbone that you can use, and instruct the patient to rest, and serve light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	and if you see that the figure has changed, so loosen it on the third day, and then put back what is changing.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And put plaster on it, from the powder of flour milled with many spices and a great amount of oil or flour of senna, after that you have cut out the membrane.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And put a second, lighter layer of plaster on it, and if the plaster sets, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it that way until it is healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times heal in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscessed foot comes, as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if it has a fracture and a wound together, then reward yourself with no piece of bone that is removed.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if subtlety of the osteomach [bone marrow] has extracted what is convenient to it.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then expand it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all those pieces of bone, and there is no remaining part, then dress the wound, if it is large, and put on suitable bandages to bind well, so that it may be healed.
de la forcele	of the fistula
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The fractured bone should be pounded more often in front of the shoulder, and the fracture will occur in three different manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	When she is broken and severed into two parts, and it has many pieces, and this is the lightest to restore.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there are breaks with wounds.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And if the injuries are on the side of the break, where you have two ministers, so that one holds the arm that feels the break's strength;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends his elbow towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then puts the break on his two hands, so that the form is as it should be, and has no appearance or swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you have need to extend it further, then puts under the shoulder of the patient a round spear of cloth or linen, and so thick as is necessary;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And hold and lift the swelling, and restrain the spear with your hand, so that you place even the break, as it seems.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot treat the head of the feeling, because it comes into the very marrow, it is fitting that the patients lie on their hateful bed, and put under the shoulder a soft pillow, and have the ministers pour water down the back, until the bones of the feeling are raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then direct the break to your two fingers, and if you find that it is shattered, so as to cut it.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	And carry the pieces lightly away, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means of closure, so that the cut is on one of the incised parts you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but place this swelling instrument under it to guard against its fall.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and resembles a spoon, and is not wood, and be as large as it seems, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the hand.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And let both shoulders be, as you see, and let one be long and the other short, just as is the custom of the wound that you have made when you treated the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are certain of an abscess, cut the wound, and if the swelling is small, do not doubt it, but apply the wound with drapes and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If a swelling comes upon the foot, so moistens the cloth in rose oil and in ash and in wine, and puts it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The binding of the bone when it is against wounds and swelling is that you place the bone under the plaster of powder from the mill and with beeswax, and put light strips on it, and set a spear underneath, if you have need of it;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very thick bandage of one palm's width, then put two drapes on top of the strips and the plaster;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a slender rod of 3 doves in length and breadth, and bend it around the bent elbow, so that the elbow of the bent limb is stretched.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the rod on the break, and turn the bent limb towards the neck, and beneath the healthy shin, and beneath the unhealthy shin.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and smooth out both parts, and whenever you see that the limb holds the break in place immediately, and you clearly see that the rod does not move over the broken bone, then reward each part every day, and when the ligament is tied, restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put under him a small pillow beneath the shin, to lift the shoulder upward.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If you lighten the break of the shoulder with the stretching of the shoulder, or by tying the arm to the neck, and do not loosen it in case of a bad accident, then after twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then reapply the plaster, if you see it necessary, and bind it and leave it so that he is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And she is restored to the best after twenty-eight days, and less in some cases.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder break
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	But it happens rarely that the shoulder breaks or is dislocated, and neither healing occurs nor does one feel fire only by touch.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If the appearance corresponds to the shape of the break, and is reset according to its natural form, in all the ways you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then put powder of the mill on the place with a lot of oil and fine ashes, and puts up a draplet double.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then puts a large and subtle stake on it, about an inch wider than the shoulder, and cuts through the stake in any place of the shoulder, so that the cut makes ashes of linen, thus making the stakes equally.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then tightens it to the whole strong band tightly, so that the stake does not move from its place, and keeps a close eye on it every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time it swells, he tightens it again, and puts the stake back in its place if it has moved, and sets the patient on his cost (i.e. bed).
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder joint has returned to its place in twenty days or twenty-five days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when these numbers are completed, if the dislocation occurs again, and be sure, because it is not bone that is set in place lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes and not below the level, then they do so, and put in, the bone, and do what we have said in breaking the abscess of the sharpness.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The flesh is broken only once in a thousand times, but it happens often.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it breaks frequently even when not expected.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it inclines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and shortage of blood, and swelling, and sometimes vomiting blood, and opens up the veins in the broken bone, and the sensation becomes better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is so that the patient's flesh heals on his back, and he puts a cloth between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the two breast bones to your hands, and subtly puts them in all possible ways until the figure of the bone is such as it should be.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Puis met sur emplausters and estoupes above the subtle star of salt, or other lighter fuselage, and blow out with an I-shaped draft, and tie it upon the broken bone, so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the round knot towards the back, and restrain immediately, and reward each hour the limb, and if it relaxes, tighten;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it seems fit to loosen, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the limb, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and loosen, and scrape the emplaster, and direct what has come from this cure.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove the emplaster, and restrain so that it is safe.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the breast
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	The injury from a broken rib comes only when the ribs are swollen after the back and chest, and do not flex only because they are curved;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and therefore he feels very bad at the examination as if it is true.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedies are such that you place equal the break, as it is fitting.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply plaster, and tie with a stake, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the ribs are broken inward, he feels the patient great pain and puncturing, as well as pleurisy, because the bone pokes into the membrane;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and he has pains, swelling and vomiting of blood, and this is from bad health, and the old men have put great effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if to those who say it is fitting to administer foods that swell the belly, in order to ward off the fracture in advance.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this unless it has come from a source of flesh.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it is from a source, that it be pure.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they said none of them would put hot air bladders on the body, to cut out pus, and it seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	All things come to pass, doubt has led us not to attract the excesses towards the living because of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the limb with a wet linen in hot oil, and put tourniquets between the ribs to keep the joint even, then either be cured of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
