Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient suffers great pain because he cannot bear through the bone that has pierced the flesh, and doubt is at the patient, then it is advisable to break open the living being of the broken chest, and it is advisable to put on certain instruments to guard the wound.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus one must cut the bone and treat lightly, and then sew both lips of the wound if it is great, and cure with emplastries until he is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if an abscess comes to pass, then put on moist cloths in olive oil over the wound.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until the joint is properly opened, and the swelling subsides on the affected area or where it should be, so long as it becomes sound.
de la brisure dou col	of a broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	There is no fracture when the bone of the neck breaks, and then they collapse;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens and you don't know if it will be cured or not, if you see that the hands are softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move nor stretch, and when you press with a needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many types of conditions, and if they are silent and feel well when you restrict them with a point, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient will recover from wounds, if they are put on treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you see that it will heal or not, take care: if the bones are soft, and if there are accidents in your hands, and on the back, they suddenly fall with great movement and expulsion against one's will;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when it falls to the back of its abdomen, it suddenly expels with no will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	When he is swollen on his back and it hurts him, if he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	It's fatal.
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	If one does not work on his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this happens to him repeatedly, then it is the lighter condition.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And if the treatment is such that you reward him with hot pus, apply oil of rose or oil of mutton fat until it cools down;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then put on a comfortable plaster and drying it, bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and does not lie on that part where he feels pain, until he is cured.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if some bones are fractured, it is advisable to cover the wound;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and break the bone, then reassemble the two sides of the wound, if it is large, with a seam, and treat with bandages soaked in vinegar, until he is cured;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the head of the bone is broken, which are called "head of the cow", pour water from your left hand pouch into your right, and put it equal to your power, then apply plaster and steel above, if you have need;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and then tie it up, and if it has bone exposed, make a stitch above, and bind the osteum and heal the wound until it is clean.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the femur
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	There is little that the bone of the hamstring is broken, and if it has, then do not have for much pain at the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and treat for a long time, and incline to the padenders, and it comes to the patient pain in the limb, and point, and swell what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And let the healing begin by stretching out your hand above, until you are above the break.
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know what kind of fracture and its nature is;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is only in the head alone, then hold that fracture equal so it may take on its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or it curves inward, then you make the patient lie on his stomach, until the restoration of that fracture has been prepared.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have put it equal, then apply the plaster, and put on a splint of wood or bone, and bind the fracture so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and apply plaster underneath the ribs, until the limb is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to lie on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if an abscess comes in, do not touch it, until the abscess is alleviated, and apply what we have previously said;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	And then he returns to the restoration, and holds it in place as needed, if there is no further injury.
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joint is the one between the arm and the head of the shoulder; and if it is broken, you should restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	which is that you take a flint or stone of middle size, according to this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And place both shoulders on both bones, and tie them to the top, and cut the patient above the joint;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then the jointed arm is put on top of the broken limb so that it comes to a standstill, and has in it an iron bar, then tie above any weighty thing or stretch it downwards as directed by the ministers;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Now puts the mirror on the broken bone equally with his hands together, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is that they place the patient on his back, and tie the hand to his neck, then instruct both ministers to pull each of these things: one pulling above at the break with their hands, and the other below at all the joints, and stretching out each one to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is further, then tighten both the joint below and above the break, and stretch out each one of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, so that you must put in the middle of the bone and the other side towards the cut.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the break is towards the cut, so that you must put in a light ligature, under the work, until the break is even on its original place and on the cut.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then puts it in even order, as he wishes, and holds it, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess comes, do not hold it tight for seven days, and put on a moist linen in isolation and oil rose, until the abscess is calmed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Now the shoulder's head is to be strained, and the manner of straining it is that you put plaster on the break, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or under the breast.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put a dress on it, and strain the shoulder and arm, so that the arm is in its place, unless something prevents it from being so, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and put one larger and stronger splint on top of the break, with space between each splint of two fingers' width, and so that each splint is as large as to cover the break three times from each side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then strain the splints, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter on the break, more firmly and less in a way that causes it to move.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	If you see the opening of the vein and the strangulation, as we have said, when you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is being formed, if it leaves it closed for six days, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then look at each one after three days the swelling, which itches and swells, does not come to the surface, or the suppurations do not come to the member because of its extreme constriction.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If he is ill, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents occur, and do not release the swelling after three days or longer, and the patient lies on his back, and holds his hands above his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and puts on the arm a certain skin of flax equally, and looks at each one every hour or half an hour, whether the figure of the broken member moves, or its joints are softened.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If the remedy is by virtue of medicine, and they give us meat that we had put before, in such a manner that the meat is at the first subtle.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he tries to take it back, if it is large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be reset after forty days from the beginning.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and therefore one must unwind and administer baths and medicines for ointments to aid the remedy.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is swollen and blocked, so it does not open after one or two days.
de la brisure du bras	of a broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscil", one small and that one who follows the pouch.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, which is under, towards the small joint;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	Because of chance break the great frost bite alone, or the small one.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the frost bites are broken, restorations are light and cures occur.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the great ones are broken, it is their cure that is bad, and more grievous than when they were broken alone.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it's a broken little finger, they can make it stretch slightly lighter, and put it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is a great frost bite, then one must strain harder.
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	And they must extend it above the joint, and make the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small ones lower than the others, so that the patient crosses himself upon his own body, and puts the joint above him, and looks upwards before him more high, so that the patient suffers no labor.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend the minister's outstretched arm to the part below to their hand or to the joint, and one other minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put it in its proper place, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If the break has pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is no remaining deviation that can be taken to hold the cure, and it cannot be restored to its proper place, then cut out (remove) the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with a fracture there is an opening, I have told the singular surgeon about this.
si pren la cure.	so take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of restoring a wound there is an opening with pus, you should apply a cloth of lard made of oil rose and white wax so that it is neither too hard nor too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and tie the cloth up above subtly, until the pus is eased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the cloth, and apply a poultice made of powdered flour with abundant lye, since you put the splints, and make the splint of the fracture as strong as possible, and one piece slightly larger than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	And he says that he must have six joints or more of the arm affected, or else.
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	or if it is a fracture in one of the bones, or in two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and bind more tightly above the fracture than elsewhere, and every day for less time, as I have said from the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the dressings that are on top of the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or harsh.
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the threads that are strained on him be linen, neither too big nor too small, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any other bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes on the limb, you should raise the limb in hot water, until the itching is alleviated.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the binding, and if the joints are loosened and the bones deviated, and so similar, address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling does not come back to the limb, because it is too strained, then you should loosen it a little, and let it stay that way for some days, until the swelling goes away, and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If no such thing happens to the patient as we have said, so that he does not come to injury within 20 years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	and then turn the hands onto his neck, and let his neck be even, and guard against movement and dexterity, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and by chance twenty days, according to the humors and the constitution of the person.
de la brisure de la main	of a hand fracture
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Observes that on the back of the hand, and near the wrist, there is little fracture, but only a frequent pain.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the finger of the hand is broken or bent, it is fitting that the patient should cross his fingers, and sit straight in front of him equally;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then puts his hand over the broken joint, and stretches out the limbs of the broken bone, and sets them even with the joints, until they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and apply plaster and poultices, for if there is no abscess, then put a stitch according to the quantity of the wound;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be wrapped up in an arrow-shaped bandage of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the break is in the small tendons under the stomach of the foot, make a bandage and instruct the patient to tie it to his broken foot;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then tie the bandage of linen so tight as to rival the plantar fascia of his foot, and tighten the bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the elbow, so it may be fitting to put a splint above and below in the limb, so that the wrist is straightened and set right, then tie everything together around the hand, and secure the joint between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the break comes from two sides, and it's swollen, then apply ice if necessary;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	And hold it with the plant, and if you see so, put a small stick straight to lift the break, and do not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	And if the break is in another place, such as on the index or one of the others, if it's even, and you tie it with a healthy hand that is after.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	Or tie them tightly in the hand holding it, if you value or put on a splint, as one would.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And take care in restoration and in the arrangement of an abscess, and heal those who come to you, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the cross breaks
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the shoulder is often broken, and it can be seen how much it is turned when she twists before and behind.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is done by tying it to the bone above the fracture, and to the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And patients are given on their face, then each of these ministers stretches out the tie evenly.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the bone is completely healed into place.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the cross, then it is one of the ligaments at the joint and the others are below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also when it is near the joint, and then so are the bonds of the joint, and so is the extension below.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then he puts the mirrors on the bone to its two sides, so that it is according to its natural form, and then he puts in plaster, and the tie, so that no abscess comes.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if it has an abscess nearby, he will let it calm down first and then return to its work and treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The limb is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary to wrap around the wound with a bandage that is twice as thick as a normal one, or three times thicker; and let the swelling subside, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the base of the knee, and pour one long thread between the thigh and the leg, from below, and put the head above with the thread.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn up the leg and over the thigh the bandage, then put in the wound stakes, and place a stake on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then apply the eight-yard length between the thigh and the groin to tie up a soft wrap to equalize the constriction, then begin to bind the wound in a figure of three or four turns.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	And when you go up higher on the fracture, and it is stretched less.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then take the two threads that you have inserted between the joint and the bone, and tie three stitches on top of them; then return to below towards the head of the thread until you find something on the ground.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and hold the strain if it does not move from its place; then let it be so, unless an abscess forms or an ulcer appears, or any other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it forms, cut away the part and address the thing that comes, just as we have said many times.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are fragments of bone that remain, it is advisable to cover them, if possible;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	And if you cannot do so, then it is advisable to cut the limb, and apply force;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment as we have said, for when he is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And at no time is the bone broken as it is when you meet a spear, just like in the shoulder and arm.
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Every time, even in the restoration as done, does not close again the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it is known that the bone is restored in three days, or less or more, according to the diversity of the constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the wound on the groin.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	The thing is broken near the groin but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	But if it breaks, then it's only a split or an opening, and there is great pain from the wound and the sensation of pain.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is as when you put equal to what was broken at his joints, until they are assembled and can be done.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then applies the plaster, and puts a round arrowstick if you have need, and binds as it is necessary, then rewards all the arrangements which we have said on other breaks, just like abscesses and similar appearances.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is anyone who needs this knowledge, let them know it, so long as they are healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, so that one is called "moustelle" and the other "fossicle".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And it happens that another fracture comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is done similarly to the arm, and all the wounds are equal. And if the two bones are broken together, turn the leg in all parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, then straighten them in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the big bone is fractured, it causes great pain and one can see well.
et torne desoz.	and turn below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	And then apply extension, and put it in its place, and tie the ligatures equally.
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	But it is advisable, if the break is ugly, and there are more pieces than not, that the extension be smaller and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and apply according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two wooden sticks that pinch the thigh from one side and the other, and are long as far as the knee.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then tie in two lengths of bandage above and below, and bind them at the middle, so that the leg cannot incline to the right or left, and this is well done;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and one must tie two sticks of the same length as the leg, and with them, hold the leg steady to move it, because done in this way is proper in the break where there has been an injury;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	And move everyone every day the leg, to see if it has an abscess or other injury.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the cure is soothed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the broken bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no break, but at times with the two feet the bones come to a break and do a little damage, and there are only few cases of further damage.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if he has a bone with a broken foot, and you see the bones forming on top of each other, if you put the sick person's foot on the ground, as it would walk, and then put your own foot on its side, where the bones are raised, press down so hard that they come into their place.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then put plaster and poultices on it, and place a small table over the foot with two flat stones, then bind the foot firmly afterwards, and wrap yourself in bandages, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, if you cut the ligament, because you will find the bones in their place, whether they are broken, dislocated, or misaligned.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if he has any broken bones, then restore them, just like we said about the bones of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then put an arrow in the broken bone according to its length, and a little bit wider, then put on the foot that I told you about, and it will become stable;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, then put an arrow in each bone according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen bandage, and strap the foot with it;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if you are standing above the head of the foot on the outside of the belly, if it is well taken.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is fitting that you do not forget the other things I told you about when we spoke about other broken bones.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and secure each accident as it occurs.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of a bone in the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of the woman's nature is broken, if it becomes enlarged, then incline it towards the part behind her back, and hold it there.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the bone with the cloth of the patient's gown, and put in also as much as it is in the (presumably a medical) instrument.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then bind the woman and raise her back slowly, little by little, and then put the cloth in as it comes to meet the bone, which returns with the instrument.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, put the cloth back, and when she has urinated, remove it again, and do this for seven days before.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	If it is restored the break, and if you see, take a vessel of goat's milk, and tie to the puncture a thread, and pour all the vessel into nature;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow through the thread formed, until the vessel is sucked in inside;
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the natural process will restore the break;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then be filled with cotton, and let it be so for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone at the point of the elbow or in a woman's body is broken, or as we have said on the bone of the willow.
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and do not conceal these close breaks in those who have put their study and practice into it, and heed my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the break means more injuries on the right path of restoration:
enten le donques.	which is therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the vagina, when it is broken, take a goose's gizzard and pour it into the vagina;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap bandages around it inside, and let him lie there for three days or so, and he will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with a wound, especially if it is great, as the bone of the shoulder or the humerus or something similar, that they should be healed immediately, if the healings that we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the wound is clean, then apply vinegar to it. If you have no other option, then do it again on the same day, or the next day, unless an abscess appears on the site of the break.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If an abscess appears on the site of the break, then leave the restoration for the next new day, until the abscess is healed, and do not touch it or apply it again on the third day or the fourth, lest you will bring about a bad misfortune.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the bone is broken and appears near the joint uncovered, it would be fitting to put it at a lighter point in your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the splint is not suitable for putting equal weights on your hands, if the splint made of iron with seven or eight fingers and the width according to the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this is a task on the surgeon that he applies three or four times, according to what he needs in each of these fractures;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and if it is red and small, that it does not bend at the pressure on the limb above, and so in front, and big near the middle towards the forehand, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palanch" because it must be placed on the curved bones above the skull of the bone.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and it is one to one, that they are even with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the splints cannot firmly grasp the bone, so that it fits well, then you must copy the head of the bone, as long as the splints have a chance.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot return the bone as we have said, so that it cuts with an instrument suitable for this, or with a knife or smoother, to your power;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then remove what is stuck in the bone from sharpness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is set and the patient feels great pain after, recognize that it's not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If you do this so it is in its place, then fill it with red wine vinegar black, and properly it is said to be like that;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put any clotting substance or other thing on the wound except oil, lest it bring decay and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer ointments as soon as you have restored the bone, and let the wound uncovered, and cover the covering all over, according to the quantity of the wound, and do well to guard that the wound is not constricted with the break;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many have done this, and they have made the patient worse, dead, or corrupted sometimes;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and so the grip is more gentle and softer than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or severe, and you doubt that no greater accidents will come upon it, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, so it cannot be put on a splint.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap and cover with hard bandages, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is healing because of what you put on it, and if you apply ointment to healing wounds, just as ointment has tetter (or tetanus) and similar afflictions.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary to move the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is softened and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary that the limbs be covered in such a way that the wound heals quickly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day they trespass and it cannot heal but re-open with bleeding, see if there are small pieces of bone, because you must treat the wound with care, and remove all these unwanted things that make this pain come.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if an abscess comes to the joint, or another kind of corruption, it is fitting that you cure it, according to what he writes in his book previously.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	But when the bone is broken and opens up in the limb, just like the bone of the shoulder or of the elbow, and other large limbs, it should not be treated with care, because often death comes from this, but let it wait until it can mend itself.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	But perhaps you will die from the wound after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of burns that come from the fire
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We come many times after the health of the fracture, particularly when it is near the joint, and see a strange thing with the figure of the limb.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance he may not be able to restore the limbs to their natural state.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Be cautious then, for if the limb is frozen.
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if you administer medicines that are bitter, such as aloes, incense, and mira, and sarcocolle, aloe, and other similar things, so that you do not take any of these things or all together, and mix them with bitter wine or with large amounts of water or with oil.
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and place it on the nose in poultices, and bind it well, and do not untie it in hands for a day.
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then you remove the dislocation and repeat it until the knots are removed;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you strain on a piece of bone very well done;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	because the property of the bone if it is that it removes all the swellings above the members;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the knot has become hardened like stone and it is necessary to remove it, if you cut above it, and make the superficiality appear;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you take it to no razor, until it is removed, and the treatment until it is healed;
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	One weak member after the guard
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is restored and it remains after the weak and subtle limbs, if it happens due to many causes;
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	Because one was too tight, and not tied as it was needed.
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	because of having too many ties, and the circulation does not come to the member.
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or for excessive bleeding;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or from too great movements, not in its own hour;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because it has little blood in its body, so is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the physician is that you should make the patient eat and make the body soft, until they are multiplied in him.
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer a bath, and give joy and ease;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	Then apply poultice to the limb, so that the poultice attracts great swelling, and the arm rises frequently with fever, until the swelling subsides from the member.
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is twisted after the health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone breaks open, and the form of the member is ugly, all that can be done is its natural repair.
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	if you do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb entirely new.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this work is blamed, and it often leads to great evils, and sometimes death.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	whenever the nodations and tortures are fresh, it is advisable to arise them with hot water, or herbs cooked in a gentle manner, as those of balm, and roots, and melilot, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	And let the patient have a mollifying poultice, as quailon is well made, and take the musk of valerian, and congeal it with goose fat or olive oil, and apply poultices on.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	Or take figs with fat, and grind them with flour of rye, and similar medicines that relieve the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the joint is dislocated due to continuous friction and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And so move the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the twisted parts are old and hardened, like stones, and require the application of the hot iron, so that they will cover just with the bone, at the subtle incision.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put on a bandage and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs, if you want to now move the joint again with care.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if it is delayed, for the swelling of the limbs, and by chance if it is put back in place with pains at the joint;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	Because of this we do not want to move it while it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times causing pain and other evils.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	whenever it happens, if you wish to heal the patient, then let him go, until the abscess is closed.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then apply a hot and oily remedy to the limb, then gently reset it, and treat each member as the healer comes to his place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the physicians for treating dislocations of the shoulders with three fingers.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It often happens that the mandibles are dislocated in both, and there are two kinds of dislocation:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they have a little bit of bone in their joints, and become soft a little.
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	When they are completely dislocated and fall toward the bone, and cut the saliva from the mouth so it cannot be held, nor can close the mouth, and move the tongue with the voice.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, so too does the movement repeat itself according to its disposition.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and completed, then you must reset it quickly, without delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the physicians tie up the head of the sick person, and pour into him some powder from one of his hands at the root of the dislocated mandible within the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two from each hand are avoided, to make even.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften his mandibles and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he gives it equal, so that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if it is reset severely, especially when the two mandibles are assembled together, apply hot water and oil until the dislocation occurs lightly;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	Do not try to force it back again, if as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset evenly, and the mouth of the patient is closed well with a softening, apply moist cloths in a rose oil made from oil and wax, then tie it lightly with moist threads;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patients sleep on their backs, and their shoulders be between two pillows, so that it does not move or twist to either side, nor try to force them to fix, but gently apply meat, until their pains are gone, and the jawbones stop aching;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then handle what he wishes lightly, and do not labor to open the mouth to swallow and drink, until the mandible is well closed and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be returned to their place in an hour, and are not converted to their own, then it comes with fever and sweating accustomed, and by chance, vomiting from the belly, and by chance, vomiting clear.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see that, then know it's a sign or portent;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times he dies within seven days.
de la forcelle	of the arm.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The arm cannot be dislocated from the breastbone inside and at the elbow, and it is never dislocated without great pain, and one can feel this always.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is only when the patient lies on his back and extends his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press firmly on the left side of the palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then puts on the plaster and the bandage, and binds it;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the head that is towards the shoulder cannot dislocate;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	If it does not heal, and if he becomes dislocated any time, then settle him in his own place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then put the plaster and bandage on him, and bind him, instruct the patient to rest until he is healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And in the same way, the head of the horse is brought back to its place when it is dislocated.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	It is known that the shoulder joint can be dislocated in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	because one way it is dislocated at the lower part of the shoulder, below.
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second way is at the level of the elbow;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	And by chance dislocation occurs at the part above, and this happens often.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and do not dislocate behind the shoulder or inside the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and more often dislocation occurs below towards the heel, particularly in those who have little strength, because they will soon fall.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	but to those who have enough strength, they will break bones and return to bones.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some men that percussion or crushing, and inflating the shoulder area of an abscess, and thinks it is dislocated due to this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	You should therefore try it, until you are certain.
et adonques encomence la cure.	And then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that dislocations occur when they fall below towards the heel, and you will find a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will discover their diversity.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	And you will find a hollow at the shoulder, and beneath it at the top of the shoulder, just as we have said.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patients cannot return their hand to its normal position or move it in any way.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if she is swollen at the top, if it's not hidden, because you will find it clearly in the top of the shoulder.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this type of dislocation is not very difficult to treat when it's new, or if the patient has fever.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the manner is that you lift the hand of the patient at the top, then place your fingers under the shoulder joint, and lift the joint with force to its normal position.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	And let the ministers ease the hand, and extend it upwards, because it is placed below.
si venra hastanment.	if it comes to a swift cut.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come to the swift cut, as we have said in our hands for many days after, it is fitting that the patient be bathed in hot water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and they should administer the remedy for mollifying and soothing, just as the decoction of aloes and fenugreek and melilot in water, and be given.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then put the patient on his back, and lay a thin cord of linen down so that it is neither too soft nor too hard, then tie Mires' foot onto the cord, and lift the shoulder joint with virtue, and treat the hand of the patient.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	And let us other servants take hold of the patient's head, so that it does not move again.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	That shoulder returns to its place now, and if you observe how it moves accordingly;
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and that you make him stay in a place where he is greater than the patient.
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and be straight towards the chest, and pour water over his shoulder below the arm of the patient, and lift the arm above, so that the patient hangs from the rope.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And another servant treats the hand of the patient downwards towards the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, so they are weighed with no heavy thing, and the dislocation comes back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And you also dislocate it in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is good to strike a long bone into the earth, where its joint is also in proportion with the piston, and not too big nor too small.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	and then it should be put under the patient, but if he has bandages soft on his long stick, and the patient is lying on a long staff.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	and then stretch his hand towards the other side forming, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not return for all these things which we have said, then do this cure:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take a bone from the upper arm of great size and four bones of width, which have their head in front for them to enter into the hollow of the axle, in this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	Then tie up the head with a cloth to prevent the patient from bleeding, then place it underneath the armpit of the sick person;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	And stretch one arm up to the long bone, and tie the assistant's arm to the bone, and the arm above the elbow of the hand, then place the arm on the spine of a large scale, and extend the hands downwards, and let the body hang from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint is now set.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is thus fixed, in any manner whatsoever, it is necessary that you put down the wound with a spear of wool equal, then apply the plaster made of powdered flour of the mill, with incense and wolf fat, on all the shoulder and back; then pull out from below the wound immediately, and turn the bandage upon the plaster, and embrace the hand on its neck, so that the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	and it is fitting that he waits for a little while, until the limbs are comfortable, because he will recover more quickly;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then move him after five or seven days, and the joint.
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is hardened and does not soften, then it is sound.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is swollen from moisture that has come upon it, or from another cause, it is fitting to administer cauterization three times, as with the cauterization tool in front of or on the cauterizing instrument.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all that, and after seven days the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift even one arm up, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are cut or stretched out or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint is never fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that occurs in the hip or knee, or behind the elbow, is done through force and stretching of the hands, and it is treated with another joint.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure until he is sound.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes greyness to the limb and late movement, then use the patient many times in baths until the greyness is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder cut
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the collarbone is dislocated at times and comes back.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it has swollen all around, and itself before and behind, and the dislocation is not corrected, because one can see it well and feel it well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and swelled according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick with the healthy one, so you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For when the joint is swollen, and cannot flex the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is therefore necessary to reset it in such a way that the abscess will heal, because if the abscess comes out, then it would be a source of great suffering.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by chance it cannot be reset entirely, especially when it is located behind.
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	so it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and by chance one can die.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is so great that when it can be set, you must stretch out your two hands to each hand.
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	Instruct the patient to let his arms be expanded and his hands be pulled in such a manner according to the length of his arm from shoulder to hand, from above down, and back again, so that the joint is loosened at its roots or on the base of his palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if a dislocation occurs, when he doubles his hand to his hand, and proud of the root of the palm, the wound is inflicted.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	If he does not return to its place, then administer great stretching.
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	And that both stretch the arm and both pull the hand with equal force so that it does not move with stretching.
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	Then turn the arm in each direction, after having wrapped a double strip of cloth around it, long and wide.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the fingers hold the joint to his hand, if there is oil to anoint the joint, then pull the joint firmly until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	Instruct the patient to put on plaster bandage in place on the wound with some wax of bees, and tie the strain tightly, then bend the arm against the pain of the patient, and leave it for some days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, so release the bandage and leave it.
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	And if you see that the joint is not tight, so reapply the plaster bandage and the tie, and leave it in this way for some days, until it is firmly set.
puis le deslie.	Then release.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels great pain after the restoration of the joint, and it does not move, so bathe him and rub him well, and press until he is eased.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	Instruct to put on the joint a swine's fat skin, then let it stay for one day and one night, then take out the bone, and make it enter into the bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	And when he cries out, rub the joint temperately, then put on the skin again, and then make it enter into the bath.
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do this twice or three times, until he is cured.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	And if you see, put under a fennel of vinegar moistened with hot butter and strain it.
si revenra a sa disposition.	if he returns to his condition.
li dislocation de la main	Dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The dislocated joint of the hand is less painful, and when it returns, it is lighter than the other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	It is necessary to return it to its place immediately, in the same house where it was displaced, so that the joint may be swollen, or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And if you return it to its place so that the doctor places his hand on a board, and extends the fingers of the other hand, and looks at it equally, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and presses until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	It is necessary that you look at him well;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	so then the doctor puts his foot on top of a board at extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then place the patient's back against a board and straighten his fingers on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	Now that it has returned, it is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, so if the strain of applying poultices to abscesses is calming the pain, then let him wait and then resume in that manner.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you are not able to put him on the mend after some days, if the joint remains twisted.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and it is not wise to let the patient suffer unless his hands are completely numb, and he cannot stretch or strain anything.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then know that the nerves have been struck, or the arteries.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	so if there is no other remedy except to strain with cautery on the affected case, and by chance it may be worth anything.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put the dressing on top of what we have said, then apply the strain and leave it for a day, then remove and leave as before.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot move well, and there is no great affliction, then apply the hot water to the affected area, and rub it so that he may recover.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of both hands
